# Operator — Roadmap

## Launch-blocking

Items that must clear before submitting to the Anthropic community plugin
marketplace ([clau.de/plugin-directory-submission](https://clau.de/plugin-directory-submission)).
Submission triggers automated safety screening + manual review; after
acceptance, version bumps auto-publish (CI re-pins the catalog on push),
but the *first* submission is the one gate.

- **Run `claude plugin validate` against operator-plugin.** Cheap insurance against bouncing on something mechanical. The auto-screen checks: plugin.json manifest schema + required fields, SKILL.md / agent frontmatter / hooks.json schemas, hardcoded credentials (API keys, tokens), absolute paths, sensitive-data patterns, MCP endpoints must be HTTPS/WSS not HTTP/WS, basic path-traversal / injection. Fix anything it flags before submitting. Manual review criteria are opaque; the bar can only be inferred from the existing accepted catalog at `anthropics/claude-plugins-community/.claude-plugin/marketplace.json`. Plugin name (`operator`) becomes the skill namespace (`/operator:dial`, etc.) — irreversible once accepted, so worth a final sanity-check that the namespace + skill names read well.

- **Enable the aec3 CI build so releases auto-attach the binary.** Today the aec3 universal binary is built+attached **manually** per release via `scripts/build_aec3_universal.sh --upload vX.Y.Z` (release-runbook step 7.5) — the GitHub Actions build (`.github/workflows/build-aec3.yml`) is dormant because `macos-13-large` Actions billing isn't enabled. This is fine during the dev cycle but a launch footgun: forgetting the manual step ships installs **without** the speaker-bleed cleaner (it already bit v0.1.39–42; re-attached in S252). Before launch: enable `macos-13-large` billing, confirm the workflow builds + lipos + attaches `aec3-darwin-universal` (+ `.sha256`) to the release tag, then drop the manual step from the runbook. Until then, runbook step 7.5 is REQUIRED on every release.

## Post-launch

Items deferred until after launch — not blocking, parked here so they
don't keep accreting in current open-items lists.

- **H-23 AEC pre-shift hardcoded for built-in speakers** (renumbered H-8 in `docs/launch-audit-findings.md:849`). AEC's 150ms pre-shift compensates for SCStream's 63ms output-buffer skew on built-in laptop speakers, but is wrong for headphones (different device latency, reference signal misaligned). Recommended config (headphones) still works *good enough* unaided; built-in-speakers users get degraded AEC. Multi-session scope: probe each output device's actual latency via CoreAudio + refactor the Rust AEC binary's stdin protocol to accept dynamic device latency. **Note (S248):** Core Audio Tap migration shipped in v0.1.35; SCStream is gone. The 63ms skew that drove the 150ms pre-shift no longer exists. AEC3 is still wired in (wire format unchanged) but the pre-shift may now be off in a *different* direction. Only relevant for built-in-speakers users (the user is on AirPods). **Gated on validation first (S250):** `docs/qa-monday.md` §9 has a built-in-speakers-vs-AirPods A/B to determine whether the migration neutralized this at all — don't design a fix against the stale 63ms-skew premise until that A/B says it's still real. **RESOLVED — CLOSED (S252):** controlled test `wos-ioww-qeg` (remote speaker in another room → audio reaches the Mac only via built-in speakers; raw corpus in `debug/14_37_aec_tune/FINDINGS.md`) showed the mic captures **0.001 rms (silence)** while the speakers play at 0.10–0.25 — i.e. **zero speaker→mic echo on this hardware** (built-in mic/speaker hardware AEC already handles it). The 150ms pre-shift is moot (nothing reaches the mic to mis-align). No fix needed; do not re-investigate without new evidence of actual echo. (The "[M] bleed" reports were the user's own direct voice while co-located with the dial Mac — not echo.)
- **A3 promotion candidates + duplication cleanup** (S241 carry). Audit 3 tabulated 110 numeric constants across all 8 components; only 5 live in `config.py`. ~9 strong promotion candidates already pre-comment-blocked in-source with rationale (5 chat_runner + 3 claude_cli + `CDP_READY_TIMEOUT_SECONDS`). Plus 7 documented duplications (bracketed-paste timings across classifier/claude_cli, audio frame protocol across aec_cleaner/attach_adapter, faster-whisper config across audio/doctor, the 120s permreq timeout ↔ 125s safety ceiling pair, `/tmp/operator.log` 3-site path, `~/.operator/bin/Operator.app/...` 3-site path, `_FAILURE_PTY_TAIL_MAX=2000` ↔ `_pty_tail n_bytes=2000`). Pure code hygiene — single source of truth for tunable knobs.
- **`/ultrareview` + `/security-review` on launch branch** (Pass 5+6 of pre-launch audit). User-triggered slash commands; can only be run by the user. Recommended once v0.1.35 lands with the Core Audio Tap migration so the reviews see the final shipping audio architecture.
- **`docs/runbook.md`** (Pass 8 of pre-launch audit). One-page "what to do when it breaks" for the 5 most likely failure modes.
- **PyPI publish verification.** v0.1.27 + v0.1.28 wheels failed to publish (uv missing in publish job — fixed in `9cfaf80`); next tag v0.1.29+ should have published correctly via the fix, but the job's success has not been verified yet. `gh run list --repo 1-800-operator/operator --workflow publish.yml` will say.
- **Stale `--yolo` flag references in docs/strings.** Pre-launch hard-cutover left a few comment-level mentions where the flag is still described as if it does something; it's a parsed-no-op back-compat shim now.

---

*Last updated: May 20, 2026 (session 253 — branded "Operator Browser" shipped as the DEFAULT dial browser (v0.1.47): a locally-generated, ad-hoc-signed copy of the user's Chrome (operator icon + name) so the meeting window is visually distinct from the user's own Chrome; re-bakes on Chrome update, falls back to system Chrome (`OPERATOR_USE_SYSTEM_CHROME=1` kill switch). Spike + recipe in `debug/14_37_branded_chrome_spike/`; runbook "Maintaining the branded browser". Then root-caused + fixed the multi-session install-time TCC deadlock (v0.1.48/49): the system-audio prompt fires on tap CONSUMPTION (IOProc start), NOT on AudioHardwareCreateProcessTap — the helper waited for the grant before starting the pipeline; fixed by waiting after AudioDeviceStart; verified live (both dialogs, both granted). Concurrent S252 session shipped v0.1.44–46 (TCC warmup correctness/latency + doctor disclaim) and closed the AEC [M]-bleed as a non-bug. Latest release: v0.1.49.)*

**Session 251 highlights:**

- **Launch-time precision self-update — built, hardened, live-validated (v0.1.39→v0.1.42).** Operator auto-ships CLI/wheel fixes (esp. Meet/Chat-DOM scraping) with no reinstall and no `/operator:update`: `pipeline/selfupdate.py`, called at the top of `_run_dial`/`_run_wiretap` before fork, fetches `release-manifest.json` over HTTPS and, if a newer wheel is published, swaps just the ~472 KB wheel (`uv tool install --force`, ~0.2–0.6s warm) and re-execs. The re-exec replaces the whole Python process, so the wheel is fresh by construction; the only persistent code is the injected page JS + the separately-versioned helper/aec3. **Security invariant:** exactly as trustworthy as a fresh `install.sh` run, never weaker — HTTPS+canonical-host pinned, strict-redirect, roll-forward-only (downgrade-proof), `ref` shape-validated (vX.Y.Z tag or 40-hex SHA, no shell), optional sha256 byte-pinning, single-flight flock, fail-safe to installed code on any error, never mid-meeting, opt-out `OPERATOR_NO_SELFUPDATE=1`. Spike: `debug/14_35_selfupdate_spike/`; tests: `tests/test_selfupdate.py` (26).
- **Real-world dry run on a fresh install of this machine caught 3 bugs the spike's mocks missed — all fixed + shipped in v0.1.41:** (1) `_download_wheel` saved the wheel under a non-PEP427 temp name → `uv tool install` exited 2 (now preserves the real filename); (2) a failed local-wheel install didn't fall back to the git-ref path (now does — this alone would've made the first swap succeed); (3) **observer staleness on reused pages** — the chat MutationObserver install was idempotent, so an observer/DOM fix shipped via self-update silently never applied on a reused dial-Chrome page (the Pass-1 tab-reuse path: reconnect, or a relaunch into a still-open meet tab). Fixed by **version-stamping the injected JS** (`stamp_observer_version` in `chat_dom_js.py`) — install tears down + replaces a different-version observer. The **fail-safe was proven live**: the buggy swap failed and operator simply joined on the installed version — a broken update never broke the meeting.
- **`install.sh` now writes `~/.operator/.components.json`** (wheel/helper/aec3 versions) for the launch-time diff. Component gating validated: across 4 self-update swaps the wheel updated while helper/aec3 stayed put (they're the manual `install.sh` channel; manifest keeps them ≤ installed so legacy installs aren't falsely nagged).
- **Docs:** `docs/release-runbook.md` — the safe-update process (version bump → wheel + sha256 → manifest → tag + release on `public` → verify), rollback procedure, and the gotchas (CDN lag, observer version-stamping, helper/aec3 manual). Linked from CLAUDE.md. Throwaway test releases v0.1.40/v0.1.41 deleted; `origin` synced; latest is the clean **v0.1.42**.

**Session 250 highlights:**

- **Google Chat space-embed (workspace meet) chat support.** A Meet attached to a Google Chat space renders chat in a cross-origin `chat.google.com` iframe instead of the in-page `[data-panel-id]` panel. Root cause of "dial reads nothing in workspace meets": Playwright's `connect_over_cdp` does NOT stitch that OOPIF into `page.frames` (it's a plain `type=iframe` target; `setAutoAttach` doesn't surface it; `CDPSession` can't route to the flattened sub-session). Fix reaches the iframe by its **own CDP target websocket**: `connectors/cdp_ws.py` `CDPTarget` is a minimal stdlib-only synchronous websocket/CDP client (no `websockets` dep — `asyncio.run()` collides with Playwright's loop on the browser thread, so a sync client is the clean fit). `attach_adapter` gains `_discover_gchat_target_ws` (+`/json` target list) + `_iframe_evaluate`/`_iframe_send` (lazy connect, reconnect+retry); `_install_chat_observer`/`_do_read_chat`/`_do_send_chat` branch by `_chat_surface` (`iframe`/`classic`). Classic path byte-for-byte unchanged.
- **Read quality.** `INSTALL_GCHAT_OBSERVER_JS` observes `[data-topic-id][data-is-user-topic]`; sender from `span.njhDLd` (strips the `…, domain_disabledExternal user` workspace badge); `DRAIN_GCHAT_QUEUE_JS` re-resolves the `Name loading…` race AND carries grouped consecutive-author senders forward by `data-creator-id` (cap-proof — resolved in the DOM before the Python history cap). Drain self-heals if the panel close/reopens (OOPIF replaced).
- **Send.** `GCHAT_INSERT_JS` = focus+clear, `execCommand insertText` (preserves the `[🤖 Claude]` astral emoji that CDP `Input.insertText` drops mid-string) + dispatched `InputEvent` (what enables Google's model-based Send button) → poll-click `button[aria-label="Send message"]`. Validated live: posts with the emoji intact (Google renders it as `<img data-emoji>`).
- **Self-echo loop fix → shipped v0.1.38 (confirmed live).** Because Google renders the emoji as `<img>`, the bot read its own reply back as `[ Claude] …` (emoji gone, sender "You") and re-dispatched it. Final implementation (simplified from an initial emoji-tolerant regex): `AttachAdapter._own_prefixes` is the two literal read-back forms — the prefix verbatim `[🤖 Claude] ` and the emoji-stripped `[ Claude] ` (derived once from `reply_prefix`). `_do_read_chat` DROPS any message matching either, on BOTH surfaces — the reply-prefix is the bot's only reliable self-signature. **Removed the entire sender-name / text-match identity layer** (`ChatRunner._is_self_sender`, `_own_messages`, `_self_name`): it never caught the real echo (Google labels own messages "You", not the tile name) and it muted any participant who shared the bot's display name (the live name-collision bug — bot tile + test identity both "Jojo Shapiro"). `_seen_ids` (ID dedup for repeat reads) and `_last_self_name` (audio speaker attribution) are unaffected. 25/25 tests green; full dial read→reply loop confirmed live with a separate same-named participant. Released as v0.1.38 on both remotes + GitHub release (aec3 binary mirrored from v0.1.37, sha256 `09456b5b…`).
- **App-icon inset fix.** The icon filled the 1024 canvas edge-to-edge (rounded square flush to the frame), so against other macOS icons it looked oversized and the corners read as a light fringe. Rebuilt to Apple's Big Sur+ template: the orange squircle now occupies ~80% of the canvas (transform `translate(19.5 19.5) scale(0.805)` on the 200×200 source) with transparent margins — matches Claude.app / Chrome proportions. Re-rasterized 10 PNG sizes via `rsvg-convert`, rebuilt `Operator.icns`, re-signed + re-notarized `Operator.app` (notary `0a65fb80…`), copied into the wheel-bundled `src/_1_800_operator/swift/Operator.app`.
- **Audio-replay corpus.** `OPERATOR_AUDIO_RAW_DUMP=1` writes continuous float32 PCM per leg (`~/.operator/debug/raw_<slug>/{S,M}.f32` + `meta.json` wall-clock anchor); `debug/14_34_audio_replay/load_corpus.py` loads it paired with the speaker-snapshot timeline for offline VAD/attribution iteration. Built to debug the multi-speaker misattribution (single-winner attribution stamps a 14s multi-speaker whisper blob with one name).
- **Silero read-only crash fix.** `_silero_is_speech` handed `np.frombuffer`'s read-only view to ONNX on exact-512-multiple chunks → `assignment destination is read-only`, silently degrading to RMS-only. Added `.copy()` on the pad==0 branch.
- **Lobby-wait diagnostics + empty-meeting raw-dump fix** (screenshots at 30s/exit; mkdir the dump dir before meta write).

**Session 247 highlights:**

- **slip → dial brand rename.** Hard cutover across CLI verbs (`slip`/`slip-strict`/`slip-yolo` → `dial`/`dial-strict`/`dial-yolo`), state paths (`~/.operator/slip_profile/` → `dial_profile/`, `slip.pid` → `dial.pid`), 50+ constants/functions (`SlipAttachError` → `DialAttachError`, `REPLY_PREFIX_SLIP` → `REPLY_PREFIX_DIAL`, `_run_slip`, `_acquire_slip_lock`, etc.), tests, docs, marketplace.json. Plugin v0.1.26 ships matching `skills/dial/`, `skills/dial-strict/`, `skills/dial-yolo/`. User's persisted Google session `mv`'d in-place to preserve dial Chrome cookies. All 22 tests green throughout.
- **Phase 14.20.5 — signed + notarized audio helper shipped in wheel** (`788e27f`, v0.1.28). install.sh already had the production path (path (a) at install.sh:333 — copy from wheel + TCC-warmup); what was missing was the .app itself. Ran `scripts/build_signed_helper.sh` → signed + notarized + stapled .app → dropped into `src/_1_800_operator/swift/Operator.app/` → hatch wheel includes it. Verified end-to-end on wheel roundtrip: `codesign --verify`, `stapler validate`, `spctl --assess --type execute` all green. Means new installs get real system audio capture out of the box, not the ad-hoc-signed dev fallback that silently broke SCStream callbacks on macOS 14+.
- **AEC3 universal-binary CI** (`.github/workflows/build-aec3.yml`). Matrix on `macos-14` (arm64 native) + `macos-13` (x86_64 native) — webrtc-audio-processing-sys's meson build doesn't honor cargo `--target`, so cross-build from arm64 isn't viable. Each arch's runner installs `brew install meson ninja pkg-config`, runs `cargo build --locked`, runs a native smoke test (generates 1s silence WAV, batch-mode runs aec3 with mic == ref == silence, asserts non-empty WAV out), uploads to release. `lipo-and-release` job downloads both, `lipo -create`'s the universal binary, attaches to GitHub release. install.sh's AEC step replaces "build from source via cargo" primary path with "download universal binary from release"; cargo fallback still wired for dev/offline.
- **Plugin marketplace + plugin clone HTTPS fix** (`0f95383`). QA on the fresh laptop hit `git@github.com: Permission denied (publickey)` on `claude plugin marketplace add 1-800-operator/operator`. Real launch-blocker: Claude Code's plugin installer defaults to SSH for github sources, but real new users don't have SSH keys. install.sh now uses explicit `https://github.com/1-800-operator/operator.git` URL; marketplace.json switched plugin source from `{"source": "github", "repo": ...}` to `{"source": "url", "url": "https://..."}`. Both forms support the `ref` pin (v0.1.26 supply-chain pin preserved).
- **Dep pin tightening** (`7b0c4de`). Three transitive deps (cryptography, pygments, python-multipart) bumped from `>=` floors to exact `==` for pre-launch v0.0.1 reproducibility. Comment documents the trade and intent to relax post-launch. Fixed mlx-whisper → faster-whisper drift in `requirements.txt` (S233 backend swap was never propagated to that file).
- **publish.yml uv fix** (`9cfaf80`). v0.1.27 + v0.1.28 PyPI publish jobs failed with `uv: command not found` — `astral-sh/setup-uv@v5` was on the build job but missing from the publish job. Fixed.
- **TCC warmup iterations driven by QA** (v0.1.29-34). User installed on a fresh laptop, hit five separate TCC issues in sequence; each got a targeted fix: (1) v0.1.29 helper Swift bumped 3s SR-grant + 10s mic semaphore timeouts to 60s polling loops; (2) v0.1.30 install.sh probe uses `_disclaimed_spawn` so TCC attribution resolves to Operator.app, not the parent terminal/IDE; (3) v0.1.31 added "Quit-and-Reopen recovery" — detect SR=ok mic=not_determined after `open -W` returns, relaunch helper; (4) v0.1.32 swapped from blocking `open -W` to background `open` + 2s poll loop, so the mic grant lands in install.sh within 2s of user click; (5) v0.1.34 force-activates the helper via AppleScript after launch so the mic dialog appears above System Settings instead of behind it. Each shipped as a separate version with retag-or-bump in install.sh's OPERATOR_INSTALL_REF default. By the end of the iteration: install still goes through SR + Quit-and-Reopen + mic dialogs, but the dialogs surface correctly and the install completes — which set up the architectural decision to migrate away from SCStream entirely.
- **Core Audio Tap API migration spike** (`/tmp/tapspike/`). User showed me a screenshot of macOS Settings with Granola in a separate "System Audio Recording Only" section, distinct from "Screen & System Audio Recording" (where operator currently lives). I had been telling them Screen Recording was Apple's only path to system audio — wrong. Granola uses the Core Audio Tap API (`AudioHardwareCreateProcessTap` + `CATapDescription`, macOS 14.4+) which triggers a different TCC service: `kTCCServiceAudioCapture`. No Screen Recording, no Quit-and-Reopen. Spike validated end-to-end: built signed test app, ran via LS, user clicked through dialogs, 469 audio callbacks/5s captured at ~94/sec — normal rate, no SR involvement. Migration locked in for next session (~5-6h). Eliminates the entire v0.1.30-34 TCC-iteration code path.

**Carry forward (post-S247):**

1. **Core Audio Tap migration** ✅ shipped in v0.1.35 (S248). Full 8-phase rewrite: `AudioHardwareCreateProcessTap` + private aggregate device + IOProc for system audio (`kTCCServiceAudioCapture`), `AVCaptureSession` for mic (`kTCCServiceMicrophone`). Dropped Screen Recording dependency + the ~50 lines of Quit-and-Reopen recovery in install.sh. BT path (AirPods + Chrome WebRTC) validated end-to-end including STT round-trip with intelligible transcripts. Spike artifacts at `debug/14_32_avcapture_mic_spike/` and `debug/14_33_vpio_spike/`.
2. **AEC3 universal binary verification** ✅ resolved (S248). Free `macos-13` runners are structurally unavailable; the v0.1.31-v0.1.35 CI runs were never picked up. Cancelled the stale queued runs. Switched `.github/workflows/build-aec3.yml` to `macos-13-large` (paid) but Actions billing is off for now during the dev cycle. Local-build path scripted at `scripts/build_aec3_universal.sh`; used to produce the real universal binary on v0.1.37's release (`09456b5b…`).
3. **Pre-launch audit Pass 5/6/7/8** (ultrareview, security-review, dep pinning, runbook) — items still in Post-launch.

**Session 248 highlights:**

- **Phase 14.32 — Core Audio Tap migration (v0.1.35).** Eight phases over the session: AVCaptureSession-for-mic spike (Phase 0, validated against Granola's existence proof); Tap API validation on this machine (Phase 1, fixed an `AudioBufferList` iteration bug in the original spike that masked 100% of bytes as zero); production helper rewrite (Phase 2, ~660 lines of Swift); Info.plist + entitlements (Phase 3, NSAudioCaptureUsageDescription + LSMinimumSystemVersion 14.4); Python TCC checks (Phase 4, doctor + __main__ + attach_adapter + _disclaimed_spawn); install.sh cleanup (Phase 5, ~50 lines of SR recovery deleted); test pass (Phase 6, all 22 tests pass, [S]/[M] streams smoke-tested); sign + notarize + ship (Phase 7, Apple notarization Accepted in ~90s). Live-validated against AirPods + Chrome WebRTC: 570 [M] callbacks in 12s 100% non-zero, STT transcribed two harvard sentences essentially verbatim, three-channel VPIO-vs-AVCaptureSession resampler comparison etc. — see `docs/handoff.md` for the data.
- **v0.1.36 — AVFoundation deprecation silenced.** Added `NSCameraUseContinuityCameraDeviceType=YES` to the helper's Info.plist. Opts into `AVCaptureDeviceTypeContinuityCamera`, silences the deprecation warning that fired at every helper startup because AVFoundation's audio-device enumeration internally touches the camera registry.
- **v0.1.36 — Desktop folder TCC dialog fixed.** Added `chdir("/")` at the very top of the helper, before any AppKit/AVFoundation/Core Audio init. Pre-existing bug (the v0.1.34 SCStream helper had no chdir either) surfaced more visibly post-migration because AVCaptureSession + Core Audio HAL initialize more file-system machinery than SCStream did. Without the chdir, the helper inherits CWD from operator → which runs from `~/Desktop/operator/` → macOS Files-and-Folders TCC fires a "Desktop access" dialog the first time any framework touches the current directory.
- **v0.1.36 — Audio Capture grant poll.** Symmetrized the install/first-run warmup with the existing mic-permission wait. There's no public `requestAccess` API for `kTCCServiceAudioCapture`; the dialog fires implicitly when `AudioHardwareCreateProcessTap` is called and the call returns immediately. Under the install.sh / __main__ warmup (`open -W -n -a` with stdin=/dev/null), the helper would hit the stdin-EOF lifecycle within ~100ms and exit BEFORE the user could click — leaving PROBE_AFTER reporting not_determined. Fix: poll `TCCAccessPreflight` for up to 60s after tap creation, only when initial probe returned not_determined (fast-path skipped on already-granted).
- **VPIO investigation, rolled back.** The S209 finding that drove SCStream-for-mic — AVAudioEngine.inputNode losing to Chrome's WebRTC over BT HFP — was specific to AVAudioEngine.inputNode's IO unit semantics. Spiked AVAudioEngine + `setVoiceProcessingEnabled(true)` (Apple's native AEC/noise reduction/AGC via `kAudioUnitSubType_VoiceProcessingIO`) and confirmed the BT race is gone in macOS 14+. But VPIO's output level on AirPods is wildly variable across runs (5 identical-config runs produced RMS 0.0004 → 0.032). AGC trade-off is unresolvable: AGC on → clips low-energy phonemes (articles, fillers); AGC off → AirPods HFP signal is below whisper's recognition threshold. AVCaptureSession+aec3 stays. Spike artifacts at `debug/14_33_vpio_spike/`. Don't re-investigate without new evidence.
- **v0.1.37 — Universal AEC3 binary attached to release.** Free `macos-13` runners are gone; the v0.1.31-v0.1.35 CI runs each queued for 1h+ without ever being picked up. Cancelled the stale queue (8 jobs). Switched workflow to `macos-13-large` (wired for the future once Actions billing is on), and built the universal binary locally tonight using a Rosetta + standalone-x86_64-tools approach: ninja universal from github releases, locally-compiled x86_64 pkg-config, meson wrapper that forces `arch -x86_64 /usr/bin/python3` so meson's host detection reports x86_64 (key for AVX2 source inclusion in webrtc-audio-processing-sys). Result: `aec3-darwin-universal` (2.6 MB, sha256 `09456b5b…`) attached to v0.1.37 release. Both slices smoke-tested with `echo_return_loss: -30 dB` matching the S225 spike measurement.
- **scripts/build_aec3_universal.sh.** Codified the local-build recipe so future dev releases run `scripts/build_aec3_universal.sh --upload v0.1.X` in one command. Idempotent: re-runs skip prerequisite setup, only the cargo builds re-run (~5 min total). Handles install of x86_64 rust toolchain via rustup --force-non-host; downloads/builds the x86_64 tools to `/tmp/x86_64-tools/` on first run.

**Carry forward (post-S248):**

1. **Live Meet end-to-end smoke** ✅ shipped in S249. Multiple full integrations completed across the session including a 4-device-swap stress test (built-in → AirPods → built-in → Bose → built-in) with 6 distinct utterances all captured verbatim, plus background-noise + identity-format-bypass + Silero validation runs.
2. **Actions billing for macos-13-large** — when dev velocity slows and releases become less frequent, enable Actions billing on the org. The CI workflow takes over automatically; no source changes needed.
3. **Pre-launch audit Pass 5/6/7/8** — still parked in Post-launch.

**Session 249 highlights:**

- **Phase 14.32 follow-up — device-swap convert-error bug fixed (Swift).** First live-meeting smoke exposed `OSStatus -1` (paramErr) from `AVAudioConverter` on every mid-meeting built-in → BT swap. Helper would die ~1s later, killing [M] capture for rest of meeting. Hypothesis-driven debugging across three notarize+test cycles narrowed it to the identity-conversion case: when Bose came up in HFP mode (16kHz/1ch → matches our 16kHz/1ch target), the converter would return paramErr on the first post-swap buffer. Boot-path identity conversion worked fine; only swap-path identity broke. Fix: bypass the converter entirely when src and target formats are identical, writing the input buffer bytes straight through. Validated against built-in → AirPods (24kHz, real resample) + built-in → Bose (16kHz HFP, identity bypass) + reverse swaps. No more convert errors across any device combination.
- **Hybrid asymmetric VAD shipped (S249).** Replaces RMS-only VAD (`UTTERANCE_SILENCE_RMS=0.02` from voice-preserved) with Silero ML-based VAD + RMS safety net. User pushed back on accepting "speak louder / raise mic gain" as workarounds — argued the code should adapt to users, not vice versa. Investigated SCStream vs AVCaptureSession amplitude differences (turned out the input-volume slider does affect AVCaptureSession, not bypassed as initially suspected). Spiked Silero VAD on existing WAVs to validate it correctly classified speech regardless of amplitude (RMS values 0.024 below RMS threshold still got Silero speech-probability 0.99). Tested 4 variants on a recorded 10s "fox + countdown" sentence: pure RMS, pure Silero, hybrid OR, hybrid asymmetric (start on either, end on silero-only with boundary-restart). Asymmetric won — full content capture (caught "Three" via RMS where Silero underweighted the unvoiced Th- onset) + clean sentence boundaries (Silero's silence judgment more reliable than RMS for true silence). Validated against background-noise recording (0 spurious utterances at new RMS=0.04 threshold). Final tuning: silero=0.5, rms=0.04, silence_threshold=3 (1.5s).
- **Silero-gated hallucination filter.** Existing `WHISPER_HALLUCINATIONS` list (`"thank you"`, `"thanks"`, `"bye"`, `"sorry"`, etc.) couldn't tell real participants from phantoms — both produce identical text. Plus the filter was effectively dead code because it didn't strip whisper's trailing period. Fix: track `silero_ever_fired` through the utterance loop, only apply the filter when Silero never said yes (= input was probably noise, not speech). Real participant says "Thank you" → silero fires → kept. Phantom whisper-on-noise → silero silent → dropped.
- **`operator doctor` Silero VAD check.** Surfaces broken Silero installs at diagnostic time rather than as mysteriously-bad captions in production. Loads the model, runs a silence-probe sanity check, reports `ready (loaded + silence probe = silent)` or specific failure mode.
- **Debug instrumentation added (kept, env-gated).** `OPERATOR_AUDIO_DEBUG=1` writes per-utterance WAVs to `~/.operator/debug/audio_<ts>/{S,M}/` for offline triage. Per-stream `[S]/[M]` tags now in every `AudioProcessor:` log line. Swift helper has post-swap delegate-callback counter + AVCaptureSession runtime-error notification observer + verbose convert-error dump (first 3 errors) — kept off by default but in-tree for the next time something device-swap weird shows up.

**Session 246 highlights:**

- **Respawn circuit breaker** (`45d9ddf`). **Doctor MCP-registration check (S245).** New `_check_meeting_record_mcp` in `src/_1_800_operator/pipeline/doctor.py` — verifies that `operator-meeting-record` is registered with claude (parses `claude mcp list` for the `✓ Connected` status) AND that `mcp__operator-meeting-record__*` is present in `~/.claude/settings.json`'s `permissions.allow`. Catches two silent failure modes that today only surface mid-meeting: uv-tool path rot after a reinstall (registration exists but points at a now-gone python path → `✗ Failed to connect`) and profile-move asymmetry between machines (settings.json travels easily; the MCP registration in `~/.claude.json` rarely does). Single CheckResult covers both halves; fix in either case routes through `_installer_fix`. Closes the S243 PM carry. 7 new test cases in `tests/test_doctor.py`; 16/16 doctor tests green.

**Dual-target installer fix lines (S245).** New `_installer_fix(suffix="")` helper in `doctor.py` replaces 8 "re-run install.sh" fix strings across MCP / audio-helper / faster-whisper / aec3 checks with consistent dual-target wording: `"ask Claude to fix this, or re-run the installer: curl -LsSf https://1-800-operator.com/install | bash"`. Same line works for desktop-app users (the model reading doctor output can run the install commands directly, since install.sh is in-repo and claude has Bash + Edit) and terminal-only users (the curl one-liner is copy-pasteable). Auth / Chrome / git / TCC / workspace-trust fix lines untouched — those aren't installer remediations. Inner-claude / outer-claude jargon scrubbed from all user-facing doctor strings; now just says "Claude".

**Briefing tab-close awareness (S245).** Added 47 words to `_BRIEFING` in `src/_1_800_operator/pipeline/providers/claude_cli.py`: "A meeting can end without leaving a marker in your scrollback — the user may close the browser tab instead of running /operator:hangup. Don't infer from chat history that prior meetings are still running; run `operator status` (via Bash) to see what's actually live." Killed the false-duplicate "another bot joined / 3 bot instances running simultaneously (PIDs 31953, 32157, 32315)" confabulation that was putting Claude Code sessions into "Needs input" state across browser-close reconnects. Live-validated by user. Root cause: when claude is re-spawned via `--resume-session` after a tab-close, its scrollback has the prior meeting context with no end marker (operator's `_shutdown` SIGTERMs the PTY claude rather than letting it close cleanly), so claude reads partial history at face value and confabulates duplicate processes. The briefing line is the cheapest possible signal — see [[project-briefing-minimal-tokens]] memory for the design rationale.

**Plugin v0.1.24 — SKILL copy rewrite (S245).** All four meeting-mode skills rewritten end-to-end. `dial` (default): "guarded mode" wording removed entirely; added **Permissions** / **Hears the meeting** (real-time local audio transcription + privacy note) / **Context-aware** (your Claude Code session + MCPs + connectors + skills are all loaded) bullets. `dial-yolo`: reframed as "the chat panel becomes a full Claude session" — dropped the hedging language ("noisy", "if you'd prefer the alternative"). Sold as the goal mode for solo or small-group work. `dial-strict`: same context/audio bullets; "Same guarded permission flow" → "Same permission flow (Claude pauses to ask in chat before unapproved tools)". `wiretap`: highlights local recording + privacy ("never leaves your laptop"), drives users to `/operator:recap` explicitly, mentions querying any past meeting by date / participants / topic.



**Whisper worker subprocess (S244).** New module `src/_1_800_operator/pipeline/whisper_worker.py`. Main process owns Chrome + audio helper + AEC3 + JS observer; the worker subprocess owns AudioProcessor (S+M), speaker timeline + attribution, bleed dedupe, and caption JSONL writes. Wire protocol: 1-byte tag + 4-byte BE length + payload over worker stdin. Tags S/M = framed Float32 PCM, E = UTF-8 JSON control event (speaker_start/speaker_stop/mic_label/shutdown). Worker `start_new_session=True` so it lives in its own session group; the shutdown safety-net reaper takes an `exclude_pids={_audio_worker_pid}` arg so the worker isn't SIGKILL'd before it drains. Worker is sole owner of the JSONL seal (participants_final + meeting_end) whenever it was ever spawned — eliminates the duplicate-seal race that surfaced when the page-close path closed worker stdin before `_shutdown` could send its shutdown event. ChatRunner pushes attended/self_name snapshot to the adapter every poll tick via `update_pending_shutdown_payload`; `_stop_audio_pipeline` flushes the buffered event right before closing worker stdin, so the seal lands with rich attended even when the browser thread tears down the audio pipeline autonomously.

**Worker respawn on mid-meeting crash.** `_send_worker_frame` detects `proc.poll() is not None` and calls `_maybe_respawn_worker`, which spawns a fresh worker and replays the speaker timeline + re-sends mic_label so attribution + M-leg labeling survive the crash. The bleed-dedupe deque (worker-local) is reset on respawn — acceptable degradation. Uses a separate `_audio_worker_respawn_lock` to avoid reentrancy with the IPC write lock. Idempotent under concurrent callers.

**AudioProcessor drain-on-shutdown fix.** Pre-S244 bug: `capture_next_utterance` exited its while loop when `capturing` flipped False without draining `_audio_buffer` one final time — bytes that arrived between the last 0.5s tick and the flag flip were lost on the floor. Fixed: drain once more after loop exit, append residual to utterance_audio if speech was already detected OR if the residual RMS itself is above threshold. New unit test in `tests/test_audio_processor.py`.

**Dead-code cleanup.** attach_adapter went 2430 → 2096 LOC. Removed: `_caption_callback` + `set_caption_callback`, `_audio_processors`, `_recent_s_captions`, `_whisper_warmup_thread`, `_warm_whisper`, `_attribute_s_leg`, `_normalize_for_dedupe`, `_is_recent_s_caption`, `_record_s_caption`, `_audio_utterance_loop`, and all legacy worker_mode branches. `set_caption_callback` also dropped from `connectors/base.py`. `__main__`'s `_on_utterance` callbacks deleted from both dial + wiretap entry points. Attribution + dedupe + normalize unit tests moved to new `tests/test_whisper_worker_logic.py` targeting the worker copies (8 tests, all passing). `tests/test_helper_spawn_smoke.py` deleted — its concerns are covered by doctor + spike5_attach_adapter_integration + live meeting tests. `tests/test_attach_audio_wiring.py` rewritten for the new wiring (5 tests, all passing).

**install.sh perms cleanup.** Shipped allowlist updated from `mcp__transcript__*` (dead since S238 rename) to `mcp__operator-meeting-record__*` (wildcard, future-proof). Includes a migration step that prunes the stale entry on existing installs.

**Validation.** Five spikes upfront (drain timing, O_APPEND concurrency, detached-child survival, worker E2E, AttachAdapter↔worker integration) all green. Live wiretap + live dial meetings validated end-to-end: trailing mid-sentence utterance captured, single meeting_end seal, sub-second main exit, ~3-7s worker drain in the background, same-link reconnect appends to existing JSONL with clean per-session seals. 20 test files green.

*Previously (session 243 evening — startup-latency optimization + reply-latency observability + plugin v0.1.22 SKILL prose softening).*

**Startup-latency tear-down (`52d75ad`).** Built top-to-bottom TIMING probes for the cold-start path: `dial_startup` (pre-fork phases: python_boot / argv / lock / claude_check / tcc_preflight), `tcc_preflight` (sub-phases: ls_cleanup / probe / warmup / reprobe), `browser_join` (post-fork: cdp_probe / chrome_launch / playwright / cdp_attach / meet_tab / lobby_wait), `cdp_probe` (sub: socket / page_count / uds / evict / settle / evicted). First measurement: pre-fork was 4.3s, of which 92% was `tcc_preflight=3957ms`. Drilled in: `ls_cleanup_ms=3855` was 97% of preflight. The cleanup runs `lsregister -dump` which enumerates the whole macOS Launch Services DB — cost scales with installed-apps count, not with what we're searching for. **Fix**: probe first, skip cleanup unless a warmup dialog is about to fire (cleanup is only load-bearing there — to anchor the user's click to the canonical bundle path). Background daemon thread post-fork sweeps stale entries cosmetically. Pre-fork startup dropped to ~0.4s (10x).

**Chrome eviction tightening (same commit).** Post-fork `cdp_probe` had a 5s outlier on cold-launch-with-eviction. Decomposed: `evict_ms=4301` + `settle_ms=522`. Built a 30-line spike (`/tmp/eviction_spike.py`) to verify load-bearing claims before changing code. Empirically: SIGTERM-death typical 106ms (vs the 2s ceiling we were waiting); port releases instantly on Chrome death (the 0.5s "settle" sleep buys nothing); SIGKILL leaves a stale `SingletonLock` but next Chrome launch reclaims it cleanly (the safety-net cleanup I was about to add wasn't needed). Shipped: SIGTERM ceiling 2000ms → 500ms with 50ms poll cadence, dropped the 0.5s settle sleep entirely, WARN log on SIGKILL escalation. Eviction worst-case ~4.5s → ~600ms.

**Reply-latency observability (committed in `1a995ee` mid-session as part of S243's broader TIMING expansion).** Per-turn breakdown: `claude_cli_turn` carries `pty_paste_ms` + `ttft_ms`; `turn_complete` carries `send_chat_first_ms` + `send_chat_max_ms`. Together they decompose `to_first_visible_ms`. Live data: pty_paste deterministic ~350ms (matches the 50+100+200 bracket-sleep budget); ttft dominates short-reply latency at ~1.3-2s (model latency, not operator overhead); send_chat 100-300ms per post.

**`t_first_visible_ms` semantic fix (`36bdfdd`).** Caught while analyzing the reply data: the metric was stamping on first `kind="chat"` send of any kind, which includes permreq questions and failure-narration. Turns with a permission ask read suspiciously fast (3.4s) while the actual claude reply landed 9s+. Numbers didn't reconcile with `pty_paste + ttft + send_chat_first`. Fix: added an `is_reply=True` kwarg set only by the streaming `on_paragraph` callback; gated `t_first_visible` stamp on `is_reply` instead of `kind`. Send-queue tuple shape bumped to `(text, kind, is_reply)`; one test updated.

**Audit-doc consolidation.** Five audits (A1 security, A2 edge cases, A3 constants, A4 hooks, A5 secrets) merged into a single `docs/launch-audit-findings.md` (1637 lines). **Day-scoped meeting slugs (H-7 from Audit 2).** `slug_from_url` now returns `<code>_<YYYYMMDD>` (local time). Recurring meetings (same Meet code, different day) land in separate JSONLs — `find_meetings` now returns one row per day per code instead of one merged blob. Test assertions in `test_chat_hardening` + `test_meeting_record` updated to compute today inline.

**Camera-controls predicate fix.** `GET_SELF_NAME_JS` was mis-identifying the local Meet tile in 2-person calls. Old predicate "the tile WITHOUT a 'Pin <name>' button" worked in 3+ person meetings (only local lacks Pin) but silently failed in 1-on-1s because Meet hides the Pin button entirely when there's only one other person — both tiles satisfied the predicate, the picker returned the first in DOM order (typically the remote tile), and `_is_self_sender` started filtering the user's own `@claude` messages as if they were the bot's. New predicate: presence of "Reframe" or "Backgrounds and effects" buttons (camera controls only render on the local tile because they only apply to your own video stream — validated in 2-, 3-, and 4-person calls via DevTools dumps from a live meeting). Same predicate swap in `INSTALL_SPEAKING_OBSERVER_JS` which shared the negative-space bug → audio attribution in 2-person calls was also broken (observer was observing the local tile and skipping the remote one).

**Teardown parallelized.** Empirical TIMING data over 5 baseline shutdowns showed total ~12s dominated by `runner.stop()` running `provider.stop()` + `classifier.stop()` sequentially (5.7s each, both hitting SIGTERM-timeout-then-SIGKILL every time — neither claude subprocess exits gracefully within 5s). Three changes that compose: (A) SIGTERM grace 5s → 0.5s in `_terminate_inner` (claude_cli + classifier); (B) `runner.stop()` parallelizes provider + classifier in threads with per-branch try/except + 30s safety join; (C) `_shutdown` (dial + wiretap) parallelizes `runner.stop()` + `connector.leave()` in threads. `meeting_record.close()` runs in Phase 2 after both branches join (needs `_attended_participants` stable). `_kill_orphaned_children` runs in Phase 3 so it doesn't SIGKILL grandchildren a branch was still tearing down. Post-fix TIMING across 5 spike meetings: dial 1.82–2.63s, dial-yolo 3.67s, wiretap 0.84s. JSONL integrity verified clean (session_start / participants_final / meeting_end markers match across all opens; H-10's append-after-close seal protects the worst-case write-after-SIGKILL race).

**Brittleness audit (subagent run + 5 shipped, 1 dropped, 2 deferred).** Spawned a general-purpose audit subagent looking for parallel landmines to the camera-controls bug — places where DOM scraping silently misbehaves when scenario (participant count, locale, view, etc.) differs. Surfaced 8 findings; shipped 5 (`c3dd5c8`): #1 `--lang=en-US` Chrome launch arg (locks Meet UI to English regardless of dial-account locale); #2 drop "Leave call" check in `_wait_for_meeting_entry` (chat-button alone is sufficient; host-disabled-chat surfaces as send-time failure instead of entry hang); #5 locale-agnostic sender extraction (replaces AM/PM regex with structural 2-line + digits-in-second-line check); #6 chat panel located directly via "contains textarea OR `[data-message-id]`" rather than `closest()` from textarea (two positive signals OR'd together — robust against textarea-rearranged and empty-chat cases); #7 one-shot silent-breakage warning when 10+ min into a meeting with zero speaking events (detects future BlxGDf class rotation without silent wrong-attribution); #8 match Meet room-code segment in `_find_or_open_meet_page` (auth bounces / `?authuser=N` / transient `/_meet/...` no longer cause duplicate tabs). Dropped #3 (subagent's "spaces/ prefix" concern unfounded — user validated consumer account uses spaces/-prefixed IDs). Deferred #4 (`span.notranslate` dependency — user not concerned). Localization caveats noted: #1's lockdown means the camera-controls + chat-button selectors stay English-stable in production.

**TIMING instrumentation expansion** (commit `1a995ee` — landed by user/linter pass on top of the teardown work). Structured TIMING markers across dial startup phases (Python import overhead vs preflight phases vs TCC preflight fast-path vs warmup-path), per-turn `send_chat_first_ms` + `send_chat_max_ms` round-trip into ChatRunner's `_turn_timing`, first-block-vs-last-block timestamps in claude_cli's transcript tail for time-to-first-token. All under the existing `grep TIMING /tmp/operator.log` convention.

Removed via `claude mcp remove transcript`, re-added the correct `operator-meeting-record` registration via the same incantation install.sh uses. NOT added to operator doctor — diff-detected the gap (doctor doesn't verify MCP registration), filed but deferred.

**URL hygiene + plugin v0.1.23 (S243 PM).** User reported "no reply from claude" after pasting a Meet URL with `?authuser=0`. Triage revealed three layers: (a) slug parser was fine — `urlparse(url).path.strip("/")` already dropped query strings, so the JSONL filename came out clean; (b) but the raw URL flowed through to `connector.join(url)` and the JSONL meta field unchanged, plus there was no shape validation at CLI entry — a garbage URL would daemonize, launch Chrome, fail silently 30s into join; (c) **the actual root cause was the plugin's `/dial` slash command running `operator dial claude $ARGUMENTS` unquoted** — zsh treats bare `?` as a single-char glob, `nomatch` aborted the command before `operator` ever ran, so the daemon never even started. Three fixes:
- **`normalize_meet_url()`** in `connectors/session.py` — strips whitespace, prepends `https://` if missing, drops query+fragment, validates Meet code shape (`xxx-xxxx-xxx`), returns canonical URL or None. Wired into both dial + wiretap CLI entries before any daemonize/Chrome work. Bad URL → friendly stdout message + exit 0. 17/17 cases pass.
- **Held-failure surface** — both join-failure paths (timeout + reject) in `chat_runner.py` now write `last_failure.json` (the existing schema doctor reads); `operator status` surfaces `last dial failed: <reason> (meeting <url>)` when there's no current meeting and the failure is <1h old.
- **Plugin SKILL.md `$ARGUMENTS` quoting** — all four `!`-block templates (dial, dial-strict, dial-yolo, wiretap) now use `"$ARGUMENTS"`. Verified against the desktop-app's "Contains expansion" rejection — `$ARGUMENTS` is substituted before the check runs, so quoting is safe. Plugin bumped to v0.1.23 + marketplace.json updated + tagged + pushed.

**Session 242 (May 17, 2026) — Audit 2 (edge cases) + Audit 4 (hooks) ran and resolved.** Carry-forward from S241. The remaining file-tailing surfaces either have no matching hook event (per-block streaming, mid-turn) or would re-couple operator to inner-claude internals deliberately decoupled. **What landed (per finding, all in commit `90b1de3`):**
- **H-16** CDP foreign-Chrome attach → new `_chrome_user_data_dir_on_cdp_port()` via lsof + ps; reuse path now verifies the dial profile path before attaching. Closes C-1's residual where `--remote-allow-origins=*` would have let a foreign Chrome accept operator's Origin header.
- **H-18** `_unavailable` recovery → `_run_turn` clears the latch on entry so each new `@claude` gets a fresh per-incident retry. ChatRunner's "say unavailable once per episode" flag also resets on successful turn so a meeting cycling broken→working→broken re-announces.
- **H-19** `_pty_dump` unbounded → `collections.deque(maxlen=_PTY_DUMP_MAX_CHUNKS=64)`; `os.read` caps each chunk at 4096 bytes → ≤256 KB ceiling.
- **H-20** denied-tool announcement leak → refactored `_assistant_texts_split` to delegate to new granular `_extract_with_attribution` returning `(immediate, attributed, denied, seen)` tuples. `_poll_transcript` now carries cumulative seen/denied state across polls and buffers text attributed to a tool_use until its tool_result lands (drop on deny, release on allow). End-of-turn fallback releases unresolved items after the Stop drain.
- **H-21** stale `.current_meeting` marker → MCP `_resolve_record_path` now gates the marker-fallback branch on `dial.pid` liveness (signal-0 probe). Env-var path unchanged (intrinsically fresh).
- **H-24** silence_count + helper starvation → removed the empty-drain branch entirely; silence_count only advances on real silent audio. `max_duration` guard still bounds the wait.
- **H-25** late append after close → MeetingRecord.append() silently no-ops after close() to seal the JSONL against post-close writes (audio caption threads stay alive between meeting_record.close() and connector.leave()).
- **H-26** hangup returns too early → `_run_hangup` polls dial.pid disappearance rather than daemon pid exit. Lock is released ~500ms after SIGTERM (intentional early release per the documented fast-recovery UX), so hangup returns truthfully in <1s. Belt-and-suspenders: self-releases the orphan lock if daemon died without releasing.
- **H-27** permreq `?` opens indefinite continuation → clear `_last_reply_had_question = False` in both permreq-resolution sites (`_resolve_permreq` real-answer path + `_check_permreq_chat_for_answer` safety-timeout path).

**H-15 design conversation outcome:** Originally proposed a `.teardown_in_progress` sentinel + `_wait_for_prior_teardown()` to gate a follow-up `/operator:dial` from racing the prior session's still-in-flight `connector.leave()` on shared resources. Built it, live-tested it, found the 5s ceiling was too tight (real teardowns hit 10-15s), bumped to 20s — and the user pushed: *what does the 20s actually buy us?* Worked through it together: H-16 (user-data-dir check) handles the CDP/Chrome reuse, H-25 (sealed JSONL) handles the append race, audio helper is independent per-process, marker is unlinked before connector.leave starts. The sentinel's only unique defense was a theoretical Playwright timing race against the shared Chrome — recoverable. **Cost**: 5-15s of wait on every back-to-back hangup→dial. **Verdict**: not worth it. Ripped the entire sentinel/wait machinery (helpers + call sites + test file). Net effect: hangup → re-dial → joined now ~7s end-to-end (vs ~15-25s with the sentinel). Live re-verified.

**Live tests run:**
- **H-21** (CLI-only): planted stale marker pointing at real prior-meeting JSONL with no dial.pid → MCP `_resolve_record_path()` returned None + `list_captions()` returned empty-state. Then wrote dial.pid pointing at test process → MCP returned the path. Both directions confirmed.
- **H-26** (with Meet URL): hangup measured at 169-306ms (vs 3s pre-fix ceiling).
- **H-15 + H-26 sequence**: hangup → immediate re-dial → joined in ~7s (sentinel ripped). Sentinel mechanism was verified working in an earlier run (the "still present after 5s" warning fired before we bumped the ceiling), then removed entirely after the design discussion.
- **H-16** (with foreign Chrome): launched decoy Chrome on 9222 with `--remote-allow-origins=*` and `--user-data-dir=/tmp/op-h16-foreign-chrome`; `operator dial` printed the exact designed warning `Chrome on port 9222 has user-data-dir='/tmp/op-h16-foreign-chrome' (expected /Users/jojo/.operator/dial_profile) — foreign Chrome, evicting + relaunching`, evicted it, launched dial Chrome with the right profile, joined the meeting.

Verified: no pre-tool narration leaked to chat (only the permreq question and a clean `ok, won't write it then` response), `/tmp/h20-marker` was not created.

**User-noted design wart** (carry forward, not a hot fix): the shared-context bridge means every assistant turn the user's IDE-side Claude generates also goes into meeting chat as `[🤖 Claude] …`. Surfaced cleanly during H-20 live test — my test-coordination text to the user ended up in the meeting alongside the actual permreq exchange. Three possible mitigations discussed: (1) tell users to do operator dev/test from a separate Claude Code session (no architecture change), (2) explicit `<meet_chat>` envelope discipline (medium change), (3) operator becomes aware of which assistant turn responds to a `<meet_chat from=…>` envelope vs free-floating prompts (bigger change). Recommendation in handoff: option 1 as the practical workaround, plus design conversation about whether the bridge model needs refinement.

**Latency triage.** From the A3 table I pulled four happy-path-suspect timeouts: (1) Swift screen-recording 3s sleep — already inside `if !CGPreflightScreenCaptureAccess()` plus disclaimed-spawn makes the preflight return true in production → never fires, off the list; (2) TCC warmup 10s — `__main__.py:173-175` already has a fast-path return when both perms granted, only fires on cold/desync path; (3) Classifier `_SETTLE_SECONDS=6.0s` — runs on a daemon `pre_warm` thread before meeting join, deliberately doesn't wait for `ready.flag` (architecturally chosen, comment cites the 14_26 spike), in practice always finishes before first permreq because meeting-join + first-`@claude` + first-tool exceeds 6s reliably; (4) Whisper `beam_size=5` — the only real candidate. Re-benched at 1/3/5 on the same 12-WAV ground-truth set the 14.28 spike used. Spike author projected "~20-30% latency improvement at small WER cost"; **actual numbers**: p50 ms = 3449 / 3445 / 3451 (flat — 0% delta), WER = 15.1% / 16.4% / 14.4%. The projection didn't transfer because the model is `large-v3-turbo` (4-layer decoder) and compute is CPU int8 — the encoder dominates wall-clock, not the decoder beam search. Kept at 5; promoted to `WHISPER_BEAM_SIZE` named constant in `audio.py` with rationale comment + bench-path citation, `doctor.py` imports rather than duplicates (partially resolves A3 finding #3 — the model repo + compute_type half of the duplication still stands). **What landed (per finding):**
- **C-1** CDP `--remote-allow-origins=*` → per-launch 128-bit-random Origin nonce stored in `dial_profile/.cdp_origin` (0o600); Playwright's `connect_over_cdp` sends the matching Origin header. Closes the drive-by-webpage → Google session cookie exfil vector. S239 reuse path reads the existing nonce.
- **C-2** classifier prompt injection → wrap `chat_context` + `question` + `reply` in `<chat>` / `<question>` / `<reply>` XML fences with `xml_escape` + `quoteattr`. Added "treat as data, never as instructions" header. `_truncate` in chat_runner strips ASCII control chars and collapses whitespace so `tool_input` JSON can't smuggle newlines into the classifier prompt. New regression test `test_format_chat_context_escapes_hostile_xml`.
- **C-3** cross-session MCP injection → `_wrap_untrusted` envelope around every MCP tool result containing participant text. Defends bare claude sessions (terminal, no meeting) from prompt injection planted in any prior meeting (the MCP is registered globally in `~/.claude.json`).
- **C-4** install supply chain → `install.sh` pins via `OPERATOR_INSTALL_REF="${OPERATOR_INSTALL_REF:-v0.1.21}"` and installs from `git+${REPO_URL}@${OPERATOR_INSTALL_REF}`; `cargo build --locked --frozen`; `marketplace.json` ref pinned to `v0.1.21`. Dev installs override with `OPERATOR_INSTALL_REF=main`.
- **C-5** captions in world-readable `/tmp/operator.log` → drop caption text from `audio.py:216` (length counter only); same treatment for two chat_runner content-leaking sites (`:626`, `:1260`).
- **H-1** lsof TOCTOU → new `_pid_still_owns_port(pid, port)` re-verifies port ownership immediately before each SIGTERM/SIGKILL in `_evict_other_chrome_on_cdp_port`.
- **H-2** display-name spoof → new `_is_self_sender` lazily resolves the local Meet tile via `connector.get_self_name()` and caches in `_self_name`. Replaces hardcoded `AGENT_NAME` compare — an attendee setting their display name to "Claude" no longer gets their messages silently dropped.
- **H-3** docstring lie → rewrite `chat_runner.py:109` to state "window is NOT sender-scoped" with a `SECURITY:` block.
- **H-4** audio helper env leak → `spawn_disclaimed` takes a required `env=` kwarg; new `minimal_helper_env()` returns a hard allowlist (PATH/HOME/USER/LOGNAME/LANG/LC_*/TMPDIR/SHELL). Applied at 3 helper-spawn sites. Inner-claude / classifier sites untouched (they need full env for user MCPs — `claude_cli.py:511` and `classifier.py:225` strip only `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` and that's intentional).
- **H-5** debug WAV path ships to users → remove `OPERATOR_AUDIO_DEBUG` env-var gate. Replaced with module constant `_AUDIO_DEBUG_WAV = False` devs flip locally; destination moves off `/tmp` to `~/.operator/debug/audio/` with 0o700.

Marker kept as legacy fallback. New regression test `test_poisoned_path_rejected_by_safety_filter`.

**Session 239 (May 17, 2026) — dial Chrome stays alive on hangup + tab-close.** User flagged two related UX bugs from live-test: (1) closing the meeting tab in dial Chrome killed the whole Chrome window with all the user's other tabs, (2) `/operator:hangup` similarly ended the meeting (kicked the user out of the call) instead of just detaching claude. Both traced to one root cause: `connector.leave()` called `_evict_other_chrome_on_cdp_port()` at the end of every teardown, regardless of whether the user wanted Chrome killed. Before fixing, verified the longstanding "Chrome 121+ refuses Browser.setDownloadBehavior against any Chrome that previously had a Playwright session attached" claim documented at `attach_adapter.py:525-531` — the user asked for a spike rather than just trusting the comment. `debug/14_30_cdp_reattach_spike/` proved the claim was overstated: re-attach works fine when Chrome has ≥1 tab; it only fails in the zero-context (macOS menu-bar-only) state. New three-way startup branch in `_browser_session`: CDP alive + ≥1 tab → reuse (open meeting URL as a new tab inside existing dial Chrome); CDP alive + 0 tabs → evict + launch (escape the zero-context trap); CDP dead → launch fresh. `_find_or_open_meet_page` calls `page.bring_to_front()` after opening the new tab on the reuse path so it lands foregrounded. New `_cdp_page_count()` helper queries `/json/list` for the page-count probe. All 19 tests green; live-validated hangup-leaves-Chrome-alive and tab-close-leaves-other-tabs-alive. Single commit: `44cf251` on operator-main (not yet pushed). Saved a feedback memory: spike load-bearing platform claims before designing around them.

**Carries forward:**
- **Real-meeting validation of the dial-Chrome-reuse path** (second `/operator:dial` while previous dial Chrome is still alive with user tabs) — design + unit tests done; only the hangup + tab-close halves were live-validated.
- **Real-meeting validation of the zero-context evict + relaunch path** — covered by spike, not yet live-exercised.

**Session 238 (May 16-17, 2026) — four-mode redesign + classifier context + pre-tool narration deny filter.** Started as Monday-meeting QA prep, turned into a multi-phase design + implementation pass.

**Design phase.** User flagged three issues from Saturday-morning live test: (1) sender-scoped sticky window guard not visibly working (turned out to be unverifiable from logs — the H1 permreq path also accepts any sender), (2) the "ok, putting it back to green" bug — claude's narration shipped after user said "no nevermind green" then "actually pink", contradicting the deny verdicts. Root-cause: classifier returned ALLOW on the "no nevermind green" (it weighted the "green" instruction over the "no") AND on "actually pink" (saw redirect-shaped as approval). Held narration drained on those (mis)allows. (3) Confused about the modes/naming. Resolved into a 4-mode redesign spec (`docs/four-mode-redesign-plan.md`) with 8 open questions worked through with the user: `dial` (default guarded) / `dial-strict` (every prompt @claude) / `dial-yolo` (no gating) / `wiretap` (no bot). Hard cutover of `dial-guarded`, no back-compat. MCP rename to `operator-meeting-record`.

**Stage 1 — classifier context + redirect-as-deny + directive deny payload.** Commit `6a956a1`. Classifier prompt now includes the last 5 chat turns as context. Prompt explicitly classifies redirects as NO. Deny payload reshaped to tell claude how to handle the reply: "if it's a flat refusal, stop; if it suggests a different action or redirects to another goal, pivot to that instead of retrying the action you just attempted." Live-validated: classifier returned `deny` on "actually silver", claude pivoted to silver on a fresh permreq.

**Stage 2 — wiretap mode + MCP rename + find_meetings.** Commit `d8fec4c` (operator-main) + `06fbcc7` (operator-plugin). New `operator wiretap <url>` subcommand: no bot, no permreq path, no narration. ChatRunner gains a `mode` parameter. `MeetingRecord.close()` writes `participants_final` + `meeting_end`. Rename `transcript_server.py` → `record_server.py`; `FastMCP("operator-transcript")` → `FastMCP("operator-meeting-record")`; install.sh re-registers under the new name. New `find_meetings(participants=[...], date_range_iso=..., url_contains=...)` MCP tool. `list_meetings` surfaces attendees. New `skills/wiretap/SKILL.md`. Plugin 0.1.20.

**Stage 3 — trigger-gating refactor.** Commit `7103f44` (operator-main) + `7941078` (operator-plugin). Three speak-mode CLI subcommands: `dial`, `dial-strict`, `dial-yolo`. `dial-guarded` removed entirely. ChatRunner's `_dispatch_user_message` branches 4 ways (wiretap no-op / yolo always forward / strict trigger-required-no-window / dial trigger + sticky window). `?`-driven indefinite window: `_send` sets `_last_reply_had_question` on every chat-kind send; `_process_messages` clears on any non-self incoming. `_continuation_active()` returns True on flag OR time budget. Sender-scope check removed. Plugin: deleted `skills/dial-guarded/`, rewrote `skills/dial/`, added `skills/dial-strict/` and `skills/dial-yolo/`. Plugin 0.1.21. CLAUDE.md commands + Tool Permissions rewritten. 14 new continuation-window + mode tests.

**Stage 3 follow-up — pre-tool narration deny filter.** Commit `c46e354`. Live test caught: "Making that change now." shipped AFTER the user said "no" to the permreq. Diagnosis took several iterations. The hold-on-permreq + purge-on-deny path is wired correctly — but the pre-tool narration NEVER LANDS in the send-queue during the permreq window because Claude Code defers writing in-progress assistant messages to disk while a PreToolUse hook is blocking. When the hook unblocks post-deny, the entire turn flushes at once and the pump catches both text blocks in the same batch. Compounding: pre-tool narration and tool_use commonly land as TWO separate assistant events. **Fix:** `_assistant_texts_split` walks events chronologically, accumulates assistant text blocks in `pending` until a tool_use lands; attributes pending to that tool_use_id and drains. If the tool_use is in the denied set (its tool_result starts with operator's "The user did not approve this action." signature), drained texts go to `denied_texts`; otherwise to `texts_to_post`. New user prompts also drain pending to `texts_to_post`. End-of-events drains the post-deny response. `_poll_transcript` uses the split helper + tracks denied so the Stop-hook backstop won't re-inject filtered text. Live-validated.

**Session 237 (May 15-16, 2026) — TCC permission warmup for the audio helper.** QA reproduced silent broken-audio dial: user tccutil-reset the helper's TCC, ran `/operator:dial` from Cursor, saw exactly one TCC prompt (for Cursor, not the helper bundle), and got `operator-audio-capture: FATAL — Screen Recording permission denied` ~3s after helper launch — zero captions captured. Root cause: when operator exec's the inner binary as a subprocess of operator-of-claude-of-Cursor, macOS's responsible-process attribution can land on the wrong app and silently deny without ever showing the dialog. Spiked the fix: `open -W -a` invocation correctly attributes prompts to `com.1-800-operator.audio-capture` (validated via TCC log inspection — Mic prompt fired and was user-granted cleanly; Screen Recording hit Apple's prompt cooldown only because the test env was over-cycled). Implementation: install.sh runs `open -W -n -a` after copying the .app, with `--probe` before/after to skip if already granted and warn-not-fail if user denies; `_run_dial` runs the same warmup as a first-run fallback after the claude preflight, before daemonize, so users whose TCC drifted post-install (OS upgrade, manual reset, .app re-copy) get the prompts surfaced synchronously before the meeting work begins. README "Permissions & safety" section got a new "macOS permissions you'll see" subsection documenting all three prompts users encounter (Screen Recording + Microphone for the helper bundle, plus "App Management" attributed to the parent IDE on first dial — triggered by operator's `open -na "Google Chrome"` to launch the dial window). Also added two exact-match allow entries to `~/.claude/settings.json` for the `/operator:update` skill's `!` blocks. Three commits: `82194f0` install.sh warmup, `4497553` README docs, `c89f915` dial-path preflight. Pushed to origin + public.

**Session 236 (May 15, 2026) — recap + status UX polish.** QA observed two related misreadings during a meeting debrief: (1) `/operator:status` returned `not in a meeting` post-meeting and claude responded "the bot didn't successfully stay connected" — speculating failure where status is actually just a state check; (2) `/operator:recap` of a 488-caption hour-long meeting returned only ~133 events (12KB ceiling) and claude told the user "operator only captured the tail end of the meeting" — false, the full meeting is on disk, the tool just paged the display. Fix: raised `RESULT_BYTE_CEILING` 12KB→80KB so a typical 1-hour meeting fits in one tool call (the right shape for recap/synthesis where the user wants the model reasoning over everything); rewrote the truncation notice in `_enforce_byte_ceiling` to lead with "Operator recorded the entire meeting. This response is paged for display" and added an explicit paging recipe (call again with `end_minutes_ago` matched to the start of this page), plus a literal "Do NOT tell the user 'only the tail was captured'" instruction. Recap + status SKILLs rewritten with defensive prose; recap SKILL also nudges claude to use `search_meeting_record` for targeted queries instead of paging through `list_meeting_record`. Test fixture for byte-ceiling grown to 150 captions (~127KB raw) so it still trips the new 80KB threshold. Plugin 0.1.19. Three commits: `6c4e4a3` ceiling+notice, `c01afed` SKILL rewrites, `331fcea` marketplace bump.

**Session 235 (May 15, 2026) — timeline-based S-leg speaker attribution.** User reported caption attribution flips in real-meeting transcript `dko-pgom-bfe.jsonl` — Kyle and Michael consistently swapped across consecutive turns. Initial hypothesis: the DOM `BlxGDf` "speaking" class lingers on a tile after speech ends (visually observed as a persistent border), so when two speakers are both lit the attribution falls back to `_last_s_speaker` and picks wrong. Wrote a console-paste DOM snapshot script that captured class state across four scenarios (cam-off speaking, cam-off post-talk, cam-on speaking, cam-on post-talk) plus running CSS animations. Diff disproved the hypothesis: `BlxGDf` clears the instant speech stops, on both camera-off and camera-on tiles. The lingering border is a CSS fade-out, not a class persistence. **Real culprit:** attribution at `attach_adapter.py:1573-1581` reads the *current* speaking state at the moment Whisper finalizes a segment — but Whisper waits for silence (~300-1000ms) before committing. In back-to-back turns the next speaker has already grabbed the indicator by finalize time, so utterance N gets stamped with N+1's name. Trace: Michael 0-3s → finalize at 3.5s (Kyle now active) → Michael's words stamped Kyle. **Fix:** bounded `_speaking_history` deque (maxlen=512) of `(t, name, kind)` events using the JS observer's own `Date.now()` (more accurate than Python drain time). `AudioProcessor.capture_next_utterance` now returns `(text, speech_start_time)` instead of just text — the start timestamp was already captured internally at line 171, just discarded. New `_attribute_s_leg(chunk_start, chunk_end, default)` reconstructs intervals from history and picks max-overlap; falls back to most-recent prior stop, then caller default. Spike at `debug/14_29_speaker_attribution_spike/`: simulator with 5 scenarios + ground truth, snapshot strategy scores 5/11, timeline strategy scores 11/11 (fixes Kyle/Michael flip 1/3→3/3 and three-way round-robin 1/4→4/4 without regressing solo or silent-gap cases). Four new unit tests in `test_attach_audio_wiring.py` covering the flip, overlap-picks-dominant, and both fallback paths.

**Session 233 (May 15, 2026) — UI-tool wedge briefing + MLX/Metal dropped + plugin 0.1.17.** Three independent threads converged in one session: closed an open question (what happens when inner-claude calls AskUserQuestion in a meeting?), uncovered + permanently fixed a known crash family (MLX/Metal async completion-handler aborts), and shipped the long-deferred operator-plugin 0.1.17.

**Thread 1 — UI-tool wedge briefing.** Question was: inner-claude has AskUserQuestion in its always-loaded toolset; what happens if it calls it in a meeting? Spike at `debug/14_27_ask_user_question_spike/` answered: the TUI renders a pick-list operator can see in the PTY bytes but can't drive; the transcript JSONL writes *nothing* about the in-flight call until it completes; claude blocks indefinitely (3+ minutes of pure spinner observed); operator's per-turn timeout would eventually fire after 600s. Same failure shape on `EnterPlanMode` / `ExitPlanMode` — model forms a plan, calls ExitPlanMode, TUI waits for keyboard approval, room hangs. Fix: one paragraph added to `_BRIEFING` in `claude_cli.py` covering both tools. Spike validated the 2x2 (explicit + natural triggers wedge without briefing; both produce plain text with it). Live-meeting validation confirmed the chat-text flow: `@claude ask me whether to use X or Y, then A or B` → claude asked X or Y inline, then A or B, then `"going with X and A ✓"`. Fresh-Claude-session control confirmed the trigger still surfaces the UI baseline, ruling out the resumed-session-context confound.

**Thread 2 — MLX/Metal crash family eliminated.** Live validation tripped a previously-known MLX failure (`XPC_ERROR_CONNECTION_INVALID` during whisper warm) that should have been benign (operator catches and switches to chat-only mode) but instead aborted operator's main process ~3s after a successful chat turn. Root cause: MLX's `mlx::core::gpu::check_error` throws a C++ exception from inside Metal's completion-queue dispatch thread when a previously-submitted command buffer completes with error, `__cxa_throw` → `std::__terminate` → `abort`. Same mechanism as S227 (which only took down MLX-internal fork-children; today's variant took down operator main). The chat-only-mode fallback catches the *sync* exception but cannot cancel command buffers already submitted to Metal — async detonation is structural. Two crashes in a row triggered the spike at `debug/14_28_cpu_whisper_spike/`. Bench result: `faster-whisper-large-v3-turbo` (CTranslate2) on CPU has identical WER (13.7% float32 / 14.4% int8 vs MLX's 13.0% — within noise), lower worst-case latency (3.8s max vs MLX's 6.2s), ~5× slower p50 (3.4s vs 650ms) that's invisible because transcripts are queried via the MCP, not consumed live. Backend swap shipped — module-level WhisperModel singleton + load/use locks; CTranslate2 segment generator is not thread-safe so the use-lock serialises S-leg and M-leg transcribe calls; segments materialised inside the lock. `aec_cleaner.py`'s S227-era `os.posix_spawn` workaround reverted to plain `subprocess.Popen` (the fork-after-mlx hazard no longer exists; net -132 LOC). Doctor's `_check_mlx_whisper_warm` became `_check_faster_whisper_warm` with first-time download messaging.

**Thread 3 — operator-plugin 0.1.17.** Bundled the S232 yolo-off mode (committed as 5f8bc52 last session but not yet released) with the S230 doctor SKILL.md per-shape interpretation guide (uncommitted on the plugin repo). Marketplace.json bumped to match.

Spike chain in `debug/14_24_permreq_spike/DECISION.md`: 14_24 verified `PermissionRequest` fires in PTY mode and JSON-only deny is the right hook contract (T3 found `exit 2` retry-loops claude — generalised to all hooks); 14_25 rejected the deny+verbatim+retry approach (claude's prompt-injection defense quarantines tool-result-channel text — same dynamic that killed Stop-block); 14_26 validated the classifier sidecar (19/19 scenarios match, 2.6s avg, $0 marginal cost on subscription pool).

**Session 231 (May 14, 2026) — caption attribution + STT model swap.** User flagged two real meetings (morning `sqr-vyex-wob`, afternoon `gte-dmiw-spw`) where transcripts had attendees missing entirely + one attendee massively over-attributed. Investigation surfaced three compounding bugs and a separate STT-quality concern; fixes shipped for the bugs that data supported.

**Speaker-attribution bugs (#1 + #2 fixed, #3 deferred):**
- **#1 — self-name scrape.** `GET_SELF_NAME_JS`'s `button[data-idom-class]` predicate matched every tile, so "first in DOM order" won — dial Chrome's first-rendered remote tile got mis-identified as local. Consequence: every mic-leg utterance (the user's own voice) got tagged with a random remote name (`Michael Powell` morning, `Adam Swanson` afternoon); that person's tile also got *excluded* from the speaking observer via the same predicate, so their actual speech got latched onto whoever pipped most recently. DOM-capture session in a 3–7 person test Meet confirmed the negative-space predicate: every remote tile has a `"Pin <name> to your main screen"` button (idomButtonCount=3); the local tile doesn't (idomButtonCount=2). New predicate: `tile.querySelector('button[aria-label^="Pin "]')` → if present, remote; if absent, local.
- **#2 — late-joiner blind spot.** Speaking observer installed once at meeting entry (`attach_adapter.py:558`), never rescanned. New participants rendered new tiles but no observer attached — their speech got attributed via `_last_s_speaker` fallback (whoever pipped most recently). Fixed by making `INSTALL_SPEAKING_OBSERVER_JS` idempotent at the per-tile level (observers, state, queue persist across calls; only new pids get wired up) and re-invoking it every `_SPEAKING_RESCAN_INTERVAL_S = 2.0s` from inside the existing `_drain_speaking_queue` tick. Late joiners get attribution within ~2s of rendering.
- **#3 — overflow pagination.** DOM capture session reached 7 participants with no pagination — Meet's grid view fit them all. Deferred; revisit if a future big meeting actually drops participants from the transcript.

**STT quality — model swap shipped, prompt lever rejected.** User flagged transcripts as "nonsensical" and "fractured." Built a scrappy benchmark (`debug_snapshots/.../benchmark_initial_prompt.py`) against 12 hand-corrected ground-truth utterances (67.9s mid-meeting from `gte-dmiw-spw`). Findings:
- **Aggregate WER on whisper-base: ~22%.** Failure distribution bimodal — 3/12 utterances at 0% (long clean single-speaker speech), 5/12 at 50-300% (short utterances, proper nouns, near-silence hallucinations).
- **Initial_prompt with attendees-only: -1.4 WER points.** A cheated version with project terms (`Janus DTC`, `flagging`, etc.) hit -11.6 points, but project terms aren't derivable at runtime from a user's meeting — only attendee names are. Honest test confirmed the lever is small.
- **Model swap whisper-base → whisper-large-v3-turbo: ~22% → ~13% WER.** 40% relative reduction from one line. Latency budget OK on M-series (p50 650ms, worst-case 6.2s for a 10s utterance — 0.57x realtime). Initial_prompt actively *hurts* on top of the bigger model (+1.4 points) because the stronger decoder reads the audio unaided and the prompt becomes biasing noise. Dropped the prompt lever entirely.

**Dial-profile decoupling clarified.** User confirmed the dial Chrome profile signs in to a different Google account than what they join meetings as — so self-name has to come from the in-meeting tile, not from the Chrome profile. Saved to memory.

**Memory artifacts:** ground-truth worksheet + benchmark script + audio snapshots all preserved at `~/.operator/debug_snapshots/{sqr-vyex-wob-2026-05-14-am, gte-dmiw-spw-2026-05-14-pm}/` for future STT work.

- Read the resulting transcript — proper-noun recovery, longer coherent utterances, less "fogging"/"refuel"-class nonsense.

The work imports `pipeline.confirmation` which doesn't exist on disk — 3 tests broken until that lands. Flagged for that workstream.~~ **Resolved in S232** — the missing module was deleted as part of the redesign and chat_runner no longer imports it; all 15 test files green.
