New log lines this session: `speaking observer installed — observing N remote tile(s) (added M this call); local_pid=<pid>` (CHANGED — was `installed on N remote tile(s)`) and `speaking observer rescan — added N tile(s) (<names>); now observing M` (NEW). Document when reconstituted.



**Session 230 (May 14, 2026) — integration pass closed; failure surface consolidated; doctor faceleted.** Closed out the DECISION.md 20–24 integration pass that S229 left half-done, then collapsed claude's whole failure surface into one shape and gave doctor a post-failure section so users never need to read `/tmp/operator.log`.

**Integration pass (20/22/24 — 21/23 done last session):**
- Cut **test 25 (`--fresh` mode)** from scope — never implemented, not worth the surface area pre-launch. `DECISION.md`, `integration_pass.py`, and the handoff all cleaned up.
- **Test 20** (long-meeting compaction) — PASS. 40/40 turns coherent in 2.6 min, compaction triggered (2 transcript markers), Stop hook kept firing through it.
- **Test 22** (foreign-hook interference) — PASS. New standalone harness `debug/14_22_pty_spike/test22_foreign_hook.py`: pre-trusts `bench/` via `~/.claude.json` (never touches `~/.claude/settings.json` — the S229 hazard), seeds the bench Stop hook's `decision:block` queue, verifies operator's `notices` path surfaces the foreign-hook interruption and the turn still returns a real reply.
- **Test 24** (resume from desktop-app session) — PASS, but only after catching that the first run used stale installed code. `CLAUDE_CODE_SESSION_ID=24f38462…` bridged correctly, `boot_to_ready=1.27s source=resume session=24f38462…`, inner-claude quoted the outer session's content back accurately. Doc-staleness gotcha: the handoff's `TIMING ClaudeCLI boot_to_ready` line wasn't appearing because the installed CLI was pre-PTY-pivot — `uv tool install --reinstall .` then it appeared.

**Turn-0 briefing leak (the bug live-test-24 surfaced).** On plugin 0.1.16, resuming a large session made `_send_briefing`'s 60s timeout expire; operator "proceeded anyway" with turn 0 still in flight; the briefing's reply (`"No response requested."` — claude's compliant ack of the briefing's "don't reply" instruction) bled into the next real turn via the transcript tail. Fix: `_send_briefing` now blocks until turn 0 is **genuinely consumed** — timeout means **abort with raise**, not **proceed**. Marker-based, not timeout-based.

**Failure surface consolidation (the bigger lever).** The user pushed: stop piling on code, find the consolidation. Result:
- **Two ceilings → one.** `_READY_FLAG_CEILING_SECONDS` (180s) + `_BRIEFING_REPLY_CEILING_SECONDS` (300s) collapsed to one `_BOOT_CEILING_SECONDS = 180s` shared deadline across the whole boot (spawn → ready.flag → briefing). The two phases stop being reasoned about separately.
- **Kill-on-failure → "alive but wedged" stops existing.** `pre_warm`'s except adds `_terminate_inner()`. After any boot failure, `_proc` is dead — only two states (working / dead), no third state to reason about.
- **Retry-once-per-incident, structural.** `_run_turn` is now a thin wrapper around `_attempt_turn`: try → catch `ClaudeCLIProtocolError` → terminate → retry once → on second failure, latch `self._unavailable` + raise. The "once" is the single nested `except` — no counter, no flag.
- **ChatRunner's exception-class ladder collapsed.** `NotFound/Subscription/Protocol` ladder → one path: any exception → `"claude is unavailable — run /operator:doctor to see what's wrong"`, said once per meeting (gated by `_claude_unavailable_announced`).

Net: **deleted more than was added.** Verified end-to-end via a new simulation harness (`debug/14_22_pty_spike/simulate_boot_scenarios.py`) driving real `ChatRunner` + `LLMClient` through a `FakeConnector` that prints what the meeting room would see — both the slow-boot-then-success path and the ceiling-abort path.

**Doctor facelift.** Per the user's "don't make users read logs" steer:
- New `~/.operator/last_failure.json` (path in `config.LAST_FAILURE_PATH`) written by `ChatRunner._write_last_failure` at unavailable-announcement time. Schema: `ts, meeting_url, meeting_slug, exception_class, message, phase, pty_tail, operator_log_tail`. Phase is set on the provider when `_unavailable` latches; PTY tail captured via a new `ClaudeCLIProvider.snapshot_failure_context()`.
- Cleared on each successful dial start (`__main__._run_dial` does `Path(config.LAST_FAILURE_PATH).unlink(missing_ok=True)`) — doctor's "Last meeting failure" always means "since your most recent attempt."
- Doctor's `_render_last_failure()` reads + **dumps verbatim**. Crucial design call (the user spotted my inconsistency): **no classification in code**. The model reading doctor's output is the translator — same pattern as the rest of doctor (which dumps `claude CLI: not on PATH`, never `"please install claude"`). The doctor SKILL.md (operator-plugin) was updated with a per-shape interpretation guide for the model.
- Tested end-to-end: sim produces a real failure record → `operator doctor` renders the section → the model reading it can pinpoint specific MCP servers as the wedge cause from the PTY tail (much better than a regex classifier).

**MeetingRecord.meta** is now kept on `self` (was passed in and discarded — small fix to support the failure snapshot's `meeting_url` lookup).

**Next** — pre-launch polish + plugin re-publish:
- ~~Bump operator-plugin to **0.1.17** (the new doctor SKILL.md content). Optional, not required for `/operator:doctor` to work (the new section renders regardless; the SKILL.md update just gives the model better interpretation guidance).~~ **Done in S233** (operator-plugin `00bf582`, marketplace `958166e`).
- `model-log.md` is still missing from the repo; new lines this session — `briefing acknowledged; turn 0 consumed`, `ClaudeCLI: turn failed (…) — retrying once`, `ClaudeCLI: claude unavailable — retry also failed (…)` — should be documented when it's reconstituted. The old `briefing reply never landed — proceeding anyway` warning is **gone**.

**Session 229 (May 13–14, 2026) — 14.22 section L, branch merge, and a boot-hardening pass.** Closed out the last 14.22 refactor item, merged the branch, and shipped a follow-on boot-hardening pass that grew out of the integration testing.

**Section L + merge.** Rewrote the obsolete `tests/test_claude_cli_provider.py` as fully-mocked tests for the PTY+hooks architecture (part 1, the plugin install smoke test, needed no code change — hook scripts are git-tracked `100755` and invoked interpreter-explicit). Then `phase-14.22-pty-pivot` (~20 commits — S227 `daedf21`/`a857412` + the full S228 G/I/J/K reshape + S229 L) merged into `main` and pushed; the three doc conflicts were reconciled by hand.

**The DECISION.md integration pass started — and cracked the "95s slow boot" mystery from S227.** An integration harness (`debug/14_22_pty_spike/integration_pass.py` + `instrument_boot.py`) revealed the slow boot was never slow boot or slow MCP connects — it was Claude Code's first-run **workspace-trust dialog** blocking `SessionStart`, so `ready.flag` never appeared. That discovery drove a **boot-hardening pass** — six planned items, four shipped, two cut:
- **Item 1** (`fe69ca9`) — `_wait_for_ready` reworked: a 180s hard ceiling (was a 30s soft timeout + 5s blind-settle that *silently lost the briefing*), fail-loud on process death / PTY EOF / hang, plus a structural, text-free `_diagnose_stuck_boot` ("rendered output then went silent" = blocked on an interactive prompt — generalises to any prompt, present or future; a soft text heuristic only enriches the message).
- **Item 3** (`7cffc2a` + operator-plugin `0.1.16`) — `ready.flag` carries a JSON payload (SessionStart fields + a `ts` stamp); the provider logs `TIMING ClaudeCLI boot_to_ready=` on every run, so the next slow boot leaves a forensic trail. Filename kept (not renamed to `ready.json`) so the two repos stay cross-compatible — no forced lockstep deploy.
- **Item 5** (`367324f`) — `_run_turn` gates on a `_boot_done` signal: an @mention that races the boot waits + posts a one-line "still getting set up" instead of pasting into a half-booted TUI; a held boot failure surfaces only here, on an actual @mention (never-post-unprompted). Also fixes a real gap — a `_wait_for_ready` failure leaves `_proc` non-None, which the old `_run_turn` missed.
- **Item 6** (`f1ac33d`) — `operator doctor` workspace-trust check: warns upfront if the cwd isn't trusted. Inform-only — operator never *writes* the trust state (that would be patterning against a Claude Code security prompt).
- **Items 2 & 4 cut** — pre-launch-premature guards. Item 2 (plugin-installed check): no installed base exists yet, so the version-skew it guards can't happen. Item 4 (briefing retry): guards an unobserved race that already has a 0.3s settle. Two design principles were locked and saved to memory: **never-post-unprompted** (operator never posts to chat unless `@claude`-triggered; failures held silently, surfaced only on @mention) and the **pre-launch lens** (don't build runtime guards for failure modes that need an installed base).

operator-plugin **0.1.16** published (session_start.sh JSON payload; reconciled a pre-existing 0.1.14/0.1.15 `plugin.json` vs `marketplace.json` version mismatch). Also a `--fresh` finding: it was **never implemented** — `__main__.py` has only `--resume-session` + the `CLAUDE_CODE_SESSION_ID` env tier, and the implicit "fresh" default spawns in `os.getcwd()`, not the clean-room `~/.operator/sessions/<id>/` DECISION.md section M describes.

**Next: finish the DECISION.md 20–25 integration pass.** 21 (hook latency — PASS, p50 0.43s pickup lag) and 23 (tear-down race — PASS) are done. Remaining: 20 (long-meeting compaction — long/token-heavy, not run), 22 (foreign-hook interference — `settings.json` write hazard, run by hand), 24 (resume from desktop-app session — needs Claude Code Desktop). **25 (`--fresh` mode) is BLOCKED on `--fresh` being implemented first.**

**Session 228 (May 13, 2026) — 14.22 refactor: sections G/I/J/K + a mid-course reshape.** Continued the PTY+hooks production refactor started S227. The headline is that **section G got reshaped, not just implemented**: the original spec had operator narrate Claude's tool calls from a `tools.jsonl` hook tail; live testing showed those `running Bash: <raw command>` lines were cryptic and `PostToolUseFailure` was being mis-narrated as a permission denial. So the model changed — **Claude now self-narrates in its own voice**, prompted by an operator-authored *first-paste briefing*, and operator delivers it in real time by **tailing the Claude Code transcript JSONL** (which also restored the streaming the early PTY pivot had lost). This narrowed the naked-spawn invariant: it constrains spawn *flags* (no `-p`, `--append-system-prompt`, `--mcp-config`), but a first-turn briefing paste is in-bounds. The `[☎️ Operator]` switchboard voice was purged entirely — there is no operator persona, the bot is just Claude. Also done: **#4** inner-claude respawn fix (stale `ready.flag` + leaked threads), an **audit** that caught a real protocol-error silent-failure bug, **section I** foreign-hook detector (`"Stop hook feedback:"` detection via the transcript tail, surfaced as a `ProviderResponse.notices` chat line), **section J** (reshaped to a 3-line clean-exit tweak — transcript-tailing already solved the real lost-reply risk), and **section K** Claude Code version floor (≥ 2.1.141, gated in `_probe_claude_code` so both `doctor` and the dial preflight enforce it). operator-plugin bumped to 0.1.14 (dead `pretool.sh`/`error.sh` hooks removed).

SessionStart→`ready.flag` handshake with 30 s timeout falling back to a 5 s settle if the plugin isn't installed. Dropped `preexec_fn=os.setsid` from the Popen call because `__main__.py` monkey-patches Popen to default `start_new_session=True`, which already calls setsid in the child — passing both ran setsid twice and the second call failed EPERM. Switched to `start_new_session=True` explicitly so the spawn works independently of the monkey-patch. Also surfaced the spawn exception text on the subsequent ProtocolError so a future failure here is diagnosable from /tmp/operator.log.
- `operator-plugin@f9900f9` (0.1.12, pushed to GitHub) — ships `hooks/hooks.json` + `hooks/scripts/{session_start,stop,pretool,error,_common}.sh`. All gated on `$OPERATOR_SESSION_DIR` so they no-op on the user's normal Claude Code sessions.

Turn 3 (duplicate the file, used Write tool): 5.31 s. **Known regressions to fix in follow-up commits:**
1. **No tool-narration / denial / connection narration** in chat (`[☎️ Operator] running Bash…` etc.). Section G of DECISION.md wires these off `tools.jsonl` + `errors.jsonl` tail loops + PTY EOF.
2. **No mid-generation streaming.** Stop hook fires at end-of-turn, so paragraph-flush is batched. Chat still posts paragraph-by-paragraph, just delivered as a burst. This is the documented cost of hooks-as-output (vs. screen-scraping the TUI).
3. **`tests/test_claude_cli_provider.py` is now obsolete** — written for the per-turn shellout shape. Pair its rewrite with section L.

**Hard-won knowledge captured below (`docs/agent-context.md`):** double-setsid via the Popen monkey-patch — silent-fail mode where the child appears to spawn (Popen returns a pid) but the preexec_fn crashes pre-exec and the parent sees "Exception occurred in preexec_fn." with no other detail.

**Prior session in parallel (also S227, same day):**

**Session 227 (May 13, 2026) — AEC3 speaker-bleed cleaner shipped.** Picked up S225's spike plan and ran the full 7-step integration. AEC3 now lives in production as a long-running Rust subprocess (`~/.operator/bin/aec3`) wired into operator's dial mic path; helper `[M]` frames are echo-cancelled before reaching whisper. Two commits on `main`, pushed to `origin`:

- `bc56fad` — S227: AEC3 speaker-bleed cleaner — integrate spike into live mic pipeline (13 files, +1622/-59). Rust source moved from `debug/14_23_aec_spike/aec3/` to `src/_1_800_operator/rust/aec3/` (parallel to the swift/ helper); binary gains a streaming mode that reads the audio helper's framing protocol on stdin, holds mic in a 150 ms delay queue (S225's empirical pre-shift), and writes cleaned-mic frames on stdout. New `pipeline/aec_cleaner.py` subprocess manager spawns the binary via `os.posix_spawn` directly (NOT `subprocess.Popen`) to avoid fork() in operator's mlx-whisper-loaded process. `connectors/attach_adapter.py` rewires: `[S]` feeds both `s_proc.feed_audio` and `aec.feed_render`; `[M]` feeds `aec.feed_capture`; AEC's `on_clean_mic` callback hands cleaned bytes to `m_proc.feed_audio`. Far-end VAD bleed gate fully deleted from `pipeline/audio.py` (`far_end` param, `speech_active` field, `BLEED_` rename — all gone), since AEC handles bleed natively at -30 dB and the gate was falsely dropping genuine double-talk. M↔S leg fuzzy bleed dedupe added: rolling 4 s deque of normalized S-leg captions; M-leg captions with `SequenceMatcher.ratio() ≥ 0.75` against any entry get dropped before the caption callback fires — catches residual bleed AEC doesn't fully cancel. Tunables in `config.py` (`BLEED_DEDUPE_WINDOW_SECONDS`, `BLEED_DEDUPE_SIMILARITY`). `install.sh` step 8.5 runs `cargo build --release` from the wheel's rust source and installs to `~/.operator/bin/aec3`; soft-skip if cargo missing. `pipeline/doctor.py` gets a new `aec3 cleaner` check + introduces optional checks (`!` glyph, doesn't drive exit code). 6 new test cases (`tests/test_aec_cleaner.py` 4-case binary round-trip, `tests/test_attach_audio_wiring.py` 2-case dedupe).

- `bcb672f` — S227: doctor — pre-warm mlx-whisper to surface Metal compile failure (1 file, +80). Adds an `mlx-whisper warmup` optional check that runs the same warmup operator does at dial entry. Catches the `[metal::Device] Unable to build metal library from source` failure mode at diagnostic time instead of mid-meeting — operator already handles the exception cleanly (chat-only fallback) but MLX *also* spawns an internal helper that can crash as a fork-child producing a scary macOS crash dialog. Cold-cache first run takes 3-20s while MLX compiles Metal shaders; subsequent runs <1s. Stderr progress hint before the check so users don't think doctor is hung.

**Live-validation results (two real-Meet runs):** clean spawn through the production path, binary reports `echo_return_loss: Some(-30.0)` on both teardowns (exact match for S225's spike measurement), bidirectional frame flow, mic-leg whisper had zero errors. M-leg captions captured 4/5 user utterances correctly attributed; 1/5 was a YouTube-meeting bleed phrase that slipped through (AEC cancelled most but residual was loud enough for whisper). That's the case the new M↔S dedupe is designed to catch when both legs successfully transcribe — couldn't catch it in this specific instance because the S-leg whisper hit the metal::Device intermittent error and never produced a caption to dedupe against. Doctor pre-warm check addresses the underlying flakiness.

**Hard-won knowledge captured:**
1. **Don't use `subprocess.Popen` for spawning long-running subprocesses in operator's process if mlx-whisper has been loaded.** Operator's Python 3.14 build doesn't take the posix_spawn fast path in `subprocess.Popen` (specifically, the `close_fds=True` default falls back to fork+exec absent `_HAVE_POSIX_SPAWN_CLOSEFROM`). A fork() in operator's process lets inherited Metal completion-queue threads fire in the child, where MLX's GPU command buffer state is invalid, and MLX's `check_error()` throws an uncaught C++ exception → child abort → macOS crash dialog. The fix is `os.posix_spawn` directly (Python builtin since 3.8), with file_actions for pipe plumbing. The spike's `subprocess.Popen` worked fine in the standalone test (mlx not loaded), masked the bug until live integration.
2. **MLX's Metal shader compile is flaky on Python 3.14.** First-run compile can hit `XPC_ERROR_CONNECTION_INVALID` against Apple's Metal-XPC compile service intermittently. Operator already catches the exception (chat-only fallback) — but the crash dialog comes from MLX's own internal fork-helper, not operator's code path. Best mitigation we can do: doctor pre-warm to surface failure at install time. Pin to Python 3.10-3.13 if recurring.

**S225 → S227 7-step plan, all complete:**
1. Extend `aec3_spike` Rust binary to streaming mode ✅ shipped in `bc56fad`
2. New `pipeline/aec_cleaner.py` subprocess manager ✅ shipped in `bc56fad`
3. Wire into `connectors/attach_adapter.py` ✅ shipped in `bc56fad`
4. Delete dead far-end bleed gate ✅ shipped in `bc56fad`
5. Build pipeline + install path for the Rust binary ✅ shipped in `bc56fad`
6. Unit + integration tests ✅ shipped in `bc56fad` (already landed alongside step 2)
7. Live validation ✅ done — two clean Meet runs, -30 dB ERL match

**Open question carrying to next session:** Phase 14.22 PTY-pivot refactor (the S226 architecture decision) still hasn't started. The AEC work was a parallel track that landed on top of the un-pivoted `claude -p --resume` architecture. When the PTY refactor begins, it doesn't touch the audio path — should layer cleanly.

**Prior status: Session 226 (May 13, 2026) — Anthropic billing pivot.** Anthropic announced this morning that starting **2026-06-15**, `claude -p` and Agent SDK usage no longer count toward subscription limits — they draw from a small per-plan Agent SDK credit ($20 Pro / $100 Max 5x / $200 Max 20x), then pay-as-you-go API rates. Operator's entire architecture spawns `claude -p --resume <id>` per meeting; under the new rules, a Max-20x user running operator on daily meetings would drain the credit in days. The "free on your existing subscription" economic premise dies for `-p`.

**Spent this session validating the pivot and committing the plan, not refactoring production code.** Seven spikes in `debug/14_22_pty_spike/`, full reasoning in `debug/14_22_pty_spike/DECISION.md`. Single commit `8816cef` (S226: 14.22 pivot spike — claude -p → interactive claude via PTY+hooks).

**Architecture decided:**
```
INPUT:  bracketed-paste wrap + \r into PTY  →  arrives as a normal user turn
OUTPUT: hooks (operator-plugin ships hooks/hooks.json; Stop, PreToolUse,
                PostToolUseFailure, PermissionDenied, StopFailure, SessionStart)
PERMS:  claude --dangerously-skip-permissions  →  no permission prompts
SPAWN:  cwd = user's project dir (so --resume finds the session JSONL)
```

**Key spike findings:**
1. **Stop-block as input mechanism is dead** — Claude Code prepends "Stop hook feedback:\n" to any `reason` returned by a Stop-block hook, and the model's prompt-injection defense fires on it, refusing every message as suspected injection. Even a counter-instruction at session start doesn't override the defense. Filtering the prefix at the API layer would deliberately bypass an Anthropic safety feature → strategic non-starter.
2. **Bracketed-paste wrap is the universal input strategy** — `\x1b[200~ <msg> \x1b[201~\r`. Survives quotes, backslashes, multi-line, emoji, code fences (SHA-256 round-trip verified). Char-by-char typing at any speed silently dropped chars on long messages.
3. **Hooks deliver everything we need for output** — `Stop.last_assistant_message` gives the reply text directly (no transcript parsing, no screen scraping). `PreToolUse` gives `{tool_name, tool_input}` for the progress callback. `PostToolUseFailure` + `PermissionDenied` give the denial callback. `StopFailure` gives connection/API error events.
4. **`claude --resume <id>` works interactively, but is cwd-scoped** — session JSONL lookup is keyed by project-dir-derived path. Cross-cwd resume returns "No conversation found." Operator must spawn inner-claude with `cwd=<user-project-dir>`. No `--working-directory` flag exists (only `--add-dir` which widens tool access).
5. **`--dangerously-skip-permissions` works with interactive claude** — confirmed via spike. Tool failures (missing file etc.) still surface via `PostToolUseFailure`.

**All four user flows preserved:**
- `/operator:dial <url>` from Claude Code (desktop or terminal) — plugin entry point unchanged
- Pre-loaded context survives via `--resume` of the user's main session
- Post-meeting continuation — shared session_id means the user's main Claude Code session has every meeting interaction in context when they return
- Transcript MCP — unchanged, MCPs are user-level config inherited by any claude session

**Escape hatch:** `/operator:dial <url> --fresh` will spawn inner-claude with no `--resume` and `cwd=~/.operator/sessions/<id>/` — clean room for when a foreign hook is suspected of misbehaving or when the user wants a meeting bot without inherited context.

**Open question (untestable until June 15):** does Anthropic classify PTY-driven interactive claude as subscription usage (planned) or reclassify as programmatic (bad)? Watch Claude Code release notes between now and June 15. If they reclassify, BYO-API-key remains as a ~10-line escape hatch (documented in DECISION.md step M).

**Codex preparation:** revisited the second-provider question (previously resolved NO per `project_second_provider_resolved_no.md`). Decision: keep the existing `LLMProvider` abstraction clean during the refactor (no Claude-isms leaking into `pipeline/llm.py`); preserve `-p` architecture in git history (this commit), not in-tree. Codex's integration when we add it is a separate `CodexCLIProvider` against the same contract — independent of how Claude's provider is implemented underneath.

**Production refactor plan committed to `debug/14_22_pty_spike/DECISION.md`** with numbered sections A–M for the refactor steps and 20–25 for the integration test pass. Refactor estimate: 1-2 focused sessions for spawn + input + hooks plumbing + callback remap, 1 session for lifecycle + real-meeting integration testing.

**Prior status: Session 225 (May 13, 2026) — AEC bleed mitigation spike.** S224 left open question #1 ("`[M]` bleed: many user-attributed captions are clearly echoes of remote participants playing through room speakers"). Spent this session building an offline AEC spike to determine the right algorithm + parameters before touching production code. No production commits this session.

**Key findings, all empirical on a scripted bleed test (90s, built-in MacBook speakers, realistic volume):**
1. **WebRTC AEC3 (via `tonarino/webrtc-audio-processing` Rust crate, features `bundled` + `experimental-aec3-config`) gives -30 dB bleed cancellation with -0.1 dB user-voice damage.** Double-talk gives -8 dB bleed with mostly-intact user voice. speexdsp was tested as a baseline and gave only -3 dB on the same data — not viable.
2. **There is a 63 ms anti-causal timing skew in our SCStream capture:** the mic stream leads the system-audio reference by ~63 ms. Caused by macOS output-side audio buffering between the system mixer and SCStream's tap point. Mic capture has near-zero such buffering, so the two streams are out of sync. This was THE bug making the prior coincidence-VAD bleed gate ineffective and why earlier speexdsp tests gave -3 dB regardless of volume. **Without compensation, AEC3 also fails (-1 to -3 dB). With compensation, AEC3 gives the -30 dB result.** Confirmed empirically via a shift sweep across both algorithms.
3. **AEC3's internal causal-direction delay-search window covers ~63 ms to 500 ms — over-shifting is safe.** All pre-shifts from -63 ms to -500 ms gave the same -30 dB result on test data. Past 500 ms, AEC3 falls off a cliff. So we don't need per-session calibration; a conservative hardcoded shift works.
4. **Design pick: 150 ms hardcoded pre-shift.** Covers built-in speakers (the ~63 ms case) with 85 ms margin; well below 500 ms ceiling. Scope decision (user-confirmed): only optimize for built-in-speakers bleed. Headphones (wired or BT in-ear) have no bleed; HDMI/TV speakers are documented as "use headphones." Saved as `project_aec_design_findings` memory.

**Integration plan — all 7 steps shipped in S227 (`bc56fad`):**
1. ✅ Extend `aec3_spike` Rust binary to streaming mode (read framed PCM stdin, write framed cleaned-M stdout)
2. ✅ New `pipeline/aec_cleaner.py` — manages subprocess + 150 ms M delay buffer + S-M frame pairing
3. ✅ Wire into `connectors/attach_adapter.py` — route S to AudioProcessor_S + AecCleaner; route cleaned M from AecCleaner to AudioProcessor_M
4. ✅ Delete dead bleed-suppression code from `pipeline/audio.py` (`far_end` arg, `speech_active` cross-leg coupling, `BLEED_*` rename)
5. ✅ Build pipeline for the Rust binary (install to `~/.operator/bin/aec3`)
6. ✅ Unit + integration tests (`tests/test_aec_cleaner.py` + dedupe cases in `tests/test_attach_audio_wiring.py`)
7. ✅ Live validation in real Meet — -30 dB ERL match across two runs

Spike code lives at `debug/14_23_aec_spike/`. Rust binary at `debug/14_23_aec_spike/aec3/target/release/aec3_spike`. Test recordings at `debug/14_23_aec_spike/session_{S,M}.wav` + `session_log.txt`. Archive of full-volume v1 test recording at `debug/14_23_aec_spike/archive_v1_fullvol/`.

**Prior status: Session 224** — `[S]` speaker attribution fix, retire state-scan tier, lazy chat-panel send, error-surfacing fix, desktop-app assumption audit.

Five commits on `main`, pushed to both `origin` and `public`:

- `528587c` — exclude local tile from `[S]` speaker attribution. The DOM speaking-indicator (BlxGDf class) fires for the runner's local tile constantly because the mic is hot (room audio bleeds in), so `[S]` utterances were getting tagged with the runner's name even though `[S]` only contains remote audio. JS observer now skips the local tile via the same predicate as `GET_SELF_NAME_JS`; Python drain filters defensively on `participant_id == local_pid`. Resolves S223 open question #2 (the "Jojo in `[S]`" mystery — was attribution, not audio capture).
- `8a8734d` — three stale truncation-notice assertions in `test_transcript_mcp.py` left over from S223's `8b4260e` wording rewrite. Brought in line with `"showing the most recent N of"` / `"omitted to fit response size"`.
- `3937f75` — lazy chat-panel send + drop stale `_chat_panel_open` cache. The S223 cache flag desynced when the user manually closed the panel, so the send path tried to fill an invisible textarea (5s timeout, dropped reply). Read path no longer touches panel state (verified live that the observer survives panel toggles AND that messages flow into the same `[data-panel-id]` container while the panel is hidden — Q1 and Q2 from S223 both green). Send path checks textarea visibility at send time and opens lazily if needed.
- `e7bdd30` — **retire state-scan tier** + surface `error_during_execution` detail. Today's debugging traced a silent-fail cascade to operator's `state-scan` tier resolving a `cliSessionId` from the desktop app's `claude-code-sessions/` catalog that the CLI conversation store no longer had. Every operator turn failed with empty `error_during_execution` (operator was reading `error` singular; actual detail was in `errors` plural). State-scan was introduced in S217 because the desktop app neither propagated `CLAUDE_CODE_SESSION_ID` nor honored the slash command's `--resume-session` flag — both have since started working (verified live: `CLAUDE_CODE_ENTRYPOINT=claude-desktop` shows env var present; `source=env` resolution wins on real `/operator:dial` runs). Resolver drops from three tiers to two: `--resume-session` flag, then env var, then fresh.
- `f1add9d` — fix `_ensure_chat_open` closing an already-open panel. Predicate had been Meet's send-button `disabled` attribute, which is ALWAYS disabled when the textarea is empty (panel state aside). So operator was clicking the toggle while the panel was open, closing it, and then failing to find a visible textarea on the very first `@claude` send post-join. Switched the predicate to textarea visibility (what the pre-S224 code used, just without the stale cache flag that S223 introduced).

**Desktop-app assumption audit (this session):** went through 8 load-bearing assumptions from S216-S219 about desktop-app behavior. Three are now stale, three still hold, two not retested. Key findings: (a) `#1` desktop app DOES export `CLAUDE_CODE_SESSION_ID` today (`CLAUDE_CODE_ENTRYPOINT=claude-desktop`), state-scan retired. (b) `#2` the failure mode for `--resume-session ${VAR}` in skill bodies is NOT model mangling — it's a hardcoded harness rule rejecting `${VAR}` expansions with `"Contains expansion"`, verified live. New memory entry: `project_desktop_app_rejects_shell_expansion`. (c) `#5` desktop app still silences non-zero `!`-block exits, verified live; operator's exit-0-to-stdout convention stays load-bearing. (d) `#4` harness pre-execution + model double-fire (the S219 root-cause for the singleton-guard work) doesn't produce double-startups today; defensive SKILL.md prose costs nothing and stays.

**Post-MVP roadmap entry added:** "Gate `operator dial` behind the plugin (deprecate terminal entry)" — would delete state-scan footgun risk for terminal-launched users, move `OPERATOR_AUDIO_DEBUG=1` toggle off env-var prefix onto a `~/.operator/.audio_debug` file marker so slash-command flow can use it. Deferred until current chat-panel / audio-attribution work stabilizes.

**Open questions carrying to S225:**
1. `[M]` bleed: many "user"-attributed captions in `sqr-vyex-wob.jsonl` are clearly echoes of remote participants playing through the room speakers. Bleed-suppressor not catching these reliably. Mitigations to investigate: tighter VAD threshold on the mic leg, wider far-end-activity window, or accept that listening-on-speakers degrades `[M]` quality.
2. Claude reply-delivery feedback loop: when `send_chat` fails, the claude subprocess has no signal — it confidently said "I did reply to each one" today after every reply got dropped. Wiring failure back into the claude session as a tool-result error would close the loop.
3. Audio investigation continues next session (user explicit).

**Prior status: Session 223** — dial latency cliff fix + desktop-app error visibility + PyPI publish pipeline groundwork. Two operator commits pushed to `origin` and `public`: `1d2e61f` (earlier in S221 — `.github/workflows/publish.yml` for PyPI OIDC trusted publishing; no runtime changes) and `38700a0` (this arc — eight-fix latency + UX commit). The boot/MCP-attach/--resume-parse work happens in parallel with idle, silently. The pre_warm slots the subprocess as-is (no init-wait); when the turn arrives and writes its envelope, system_init fires nearly instantly because claude was already booted. Plugin commit `caf1cfd` on `1-800-operator/operator-plugin` ships **0.1.10**: SKILL.md rewritten to remove the "Invoke the Bash tool" prose directive that was causing the desktop-app model to fire Bash a second time. **Root cause established beyond doubt via JSONL transcript inspection:** the Claude Code desktop app **harness** pre-executes the ` ```! ``` ` block at SKILL-load time and inlines its stdout into the SKILL.md text the model receives — replacing the original command. Pre-S219 SKILL.md still instructed the model to "invoke the Bash tool with the command in the `!` block below as your very first action," so the model fired a second Bash call, reconstructing the argv from context (dropping `claude` in the process) and hitting operator's singleton guard. Verified: only ONE tool_use in the model's conversation transcript despite TWO `operator dial` processes hitting operator (proving the first came from the harness, not the model). **Live-test after fix:** single Bash invocation per `/dial`, single `entry` event in `~/.operator/invocations.log` diagnostic trace, clean three-line post-spawn note in desktop app, `@claude do you read me?` round-trip in 5.2s. **Lessons saved for end-of-session docs sweep:** JSONL transcripts at `~/.claude/projects/<cwd-slug>/<session-id>.jsonl` are forensic ground truth (use them before guessing); SKILL.md `!`-blocks are pre-executed by the harness — never also instruct the model to invoke that command. **Prior status (session 218):** UX hardening sweep across the model-improvisation surface. > **Session 213 — Phase 14.22.7 shipped.** `operator-plugin` repo created at `github.com/1-800-operator/operator-plugin` (private during pre-launch, flips public when 14.22.10's landing page is up): `.claude-plugin/plugin.json` (name `operator`, v0.1.0, MIT) + four skills (dial / status / hangup / doctor) each shelling out to one operator CLI subcommand. CLI side, `__main__.py` gains two slim subcommands: `operator status` (reads `.current_meeting` marker + JSONL meta → prints `in meeting <url>` or `not in a meeting`) and `operator hangup` (pgrep + SIGTERM the `operator dial` process, which triggers the existing graceful `_shutdown` handler; cleans stale marker if no process running). Deviation from spec: roadmap proposed `pkill -f "operator dial"` for the hangup skill body; implemented as `operator hangup` instead so teardown goes through the documented signal-handler path. 11/11 standalone tests pass.

> **Prior status: Session 209 — BT HFP exclusivity bug fixed; mic-leg E2E closed.** The mic-leg E2E test the user has been carrying since S207 went live. Initial test failed: AirPods + Chrome unmuted in Meet → helper's `[M]` callbacks fired on cadence with right byte count but Whisper got pure silence (RMS ~0). Symptom shape matches the BT Hands-Free Profile single-channel limitation: SCO carries one mono link, macOS gives audio to whoever bound first (Chrome's WebRTC), silently delivers zero-filled buffers to subsequent clients (our `AVAudioEngine.inputNode` tap). Validated empirically by confirming Granola captures the same scenario cleanly. Fix path: `SCStream.captureMicrophone = true` (macOS 15+ API) bypasses the per-process exclusivity because ScreenCaptureKit's audio path goes through Apple's privileged screen-recording subsystem (same fanout that lets QuickTime + cmd-shift-5 + OBS record mic without conflicting). Three gotchas folded in: (1) `cfg.sampleRate` is honored for system audio but NOT for the mic stream — mic comes through at the device's preferred rate (24 kHz AirPods HFP, 16 kHz Bose HFP, 48 kHz built-in); helper builds an `AVAudioConverter` from the actual buffer's source format and rebuilds it on detected change. (2) SCStream is sticky to the device that was the system default at `startCapture` time; doesn't auto-follow. To track mid-meeting device swaps (AirPods on/off, BT die, manual Sound Settings switch), helper registers a `kAudioHardwarePropertyDefaultInputDevice` listener and on fire stops the stream + rebuilds with `cfg.microphoneCaptureDeviceID = newDevice.uniqueID` + restarts (serialized via `restartQueue` with semaphore-blocked stop+start completion). (3) `kAudioHardwarePropertyDevices` listener is redundant with the default-input listener for this use case. Validated across 10+ spike runs in `debug/14_21_mic_capture_spike/` (AirPods + Bose NC 700) and a live `operator dial claude` session: built-in mic, AirPods connect mid-meeting, AirPods disconnect mid-meeting all transcribe cleanly with correct pitch and `sender="user"` attribution. `@claude what colors did I just say?` round-trip closed (yellow → orange → red, in order). One commit on `main`: `231c864` (Phase 14.21.1 helper rewrite + S207 carry-forward docs cleanups). 15/15 tests pass. Notarized helper rebuilt via `scripts/build_signed_helper.sh`. **Seven commits unpushed** ahead of `origin/main` (S206 trio + S207 docs + S208 pair + S209 single). **Mic-leg E2E gate from S207 is now closed** — `/ultrareview` and `/security-review` (Phase 5+6 of pre-launch audit) are unblocked. **Exact next step (session 210):** any of (a) push the seven unpushed commits to `origin/main`, (b) Phase 14.21.1 mic-mute privacy gate (~3h), (c) Phase 14.21.2 TCC pre-prompt UX (~2h), (d) `/ultrareview` and/or `/security-review` now that they're unblocked. Naming-note: the S209 commit was titled "Phase 14.21.1" but the roadmap's 14.21.1 below is the still-open mic-mute privacy gate; the S209 work was actually a Phase 14.21 prerequisite that wasn't in the original numbering. Treat the commit title as session-bookkeeping, not a roadmap-row claim.

> **Prior status: Session 208 — chat-permission gate deleted (~1058 net LOC).** Started as a debug session — dial mode was hanging on inner-claude write tools because the `PermissionChatHandler` ran on the provider's permission-pump thread and called Playwright's sync API across threads (`greenlet.error: Cannot switch to a different thread`). Right call — the chat-permission flow was added in 14.19.8 (May 5) as a Claude judgment about safety, NOT user-driven. Each UX edge case the flow created (recent-yes window, tiered auto-approve list, voice-rule question form, the threading bugs above) had been patched in-layer rather than triggering "should the layer exist?" Saved feedback memory `feedback_dont_invent_safety_scaffolding.md`. Two modes now, matching Claude Code's two: `--yolo` forwards `--dangerously-skip-permissions` (free run); without it Claude Code's `~/.claude/settings.json` rules apply, denials surface as plain-English replies. New `DENIAL RECOVERY` paragraph in the prompt rule tells the model to suggest `--yolo` when a tool gets denied. **Live-validated end-to-end across two dial sessions today** (Linear "do laundry" issue created cleanly in run 2 once user updated their settings.json). > **Prior status: Session 205 second pass — four live-dial reliability fixes + side-channel heartbeat + dep/env cleanup, all live-verified.** Parallel to the earlier S205 endurance-audit session, this pass surfaced and fixed bugs from a real dial-mode meeting. Five named fixes landed in working-tree state ready to commit at end-session: (1) **dial Chrome zombie recovery** in `attach_adapter.py` — when the previous dial session detached cleanly per design and the user later closed the last dial Chrome window, the process stayed alive in the macOS menu bar with zero browser contexts; the next dial run took the reuse-path on `_cdp_endpoint_alive() and _cdp_belongs_to_dial()`, then `connect_over_cdp` failed with `Browser context management is not supported` because there was nothing for Playwright to manage. Fix tracks a `took_reuse_path` bool; on connect failure during reuse, evict + relaunch + retry once. Identity verification ≠ liveness verification; `connect_over_cdp` itself is the cheapest liveness probe. (2) **Booted-from-meeting auto-leave** in `chat_runner._check_participant_state` — pre-existing auto-leave only fired on `count == 1 + _saw_others=True`, so when dial Chrome got bounced to `meet.google.com/landing` after Meet's lobby idle timeout (participant count 1 → 0, `_saw_others` never having flipped because the bot was alone in the lobby the whole time), the chat loop polled forever for a chat panel that no longer existed. New branch arms the same grace timer for `count == 0` regardless of `_saw_others`. Live-verified — clean exit at 62s after the bounce. (3) **Lobby false-positive in `_wait_for_meeting_entry`** — the existing `Leave call` button check tripped 8 seconds after dial Chrome launched (impossibly fast for an "Ask to join" → host-admit flow); DOM dump from a live repro proved Meet renders the in-call control bar (including the red phone icon = `Leave call`) even on the lobby waiting screen. The lobby state is missing `Chat with everyone`, the post-admit state has it. Detector now requires BOTH buttons visible. Live-verified at 146.5s in lobby + post-admit announce. (4) **Meeting-chat heartbeat** — model-authored side-channel `claude -p` call when the bot goes silent for 30s mid-turn. Previous run had a 90+ second silent stretch between an opening narration and a closing summary while the model chained tools; user explicitly preferred a heartbeat over a per-tool narration prompt rule (which had been added earlier this session and was REVERTED for this approach instead). Architecture: `progress_callback` from `ClaudeCLIProvider` populates a 10-item bounded `_recent_tool_uses` deque; per-turn daemon thread checks `time.time() - max(last_send, turn_start, last_heartbeat) > 30s` and on trip spawns `subprocess.run(["claude", "-p", prompt, "--output-format", "text"], timeout=20)` with the user question + recent tools as prompt context; race re-check after the call returns drops the result if a real reply landed during the side-channel; post via `kind="heartbeat"` so `tail_chat()` filters it out of inner-claude's prompt context. Constants: `HEARTBEAT_SILENCE_SECONDS = 30`, `HEARTBEAT_TICK_SECONDS = 2`, `HEARTBEAT_CALL_TIMEOUT_SECONDS = 20`, `HEARTBEAT_RECENT_TOOL_LIMIT = 5`. (5) **Heartbeat env-strip** — first heartbeat ship failed every invocation with `exited 1: ''` because `subprocess.run` inherited operator's full env, including `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` from `~/.operator/.env` (whose key had zero credit balance). The user's architecture is "no API key consumption — everything routes through claude code's own auth"; inner-claude already strips that env var (`claude_cli.py:437`) but the heartbeat call did not. Fix mirrors the strip: `env = {k: v for k, v in os.environ.items() if k != "ANTHROPIC_API_KEY"}`. Also: claude writes `Credit balance is too low` to STDOUT not stderr — failure log now captures both streams. **Two cleanup decisions resolved in the same session:** (a) **Second LLM provider in v1 scope?** — RESOLVED **NO**. Dropped `openai==2.29.0` + `anthropic==0.94.0` from `pyproject.toml` + `requirements.txt`, refreshed comment headers explaining operator's "no LLM API keys, everything via `claude -p`" architecture. Closes the long-deferred S203 product call. (b) **Stale API keys in `~/.operator/.env`** — `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` and `OPENAI_API_KEY` lines deleted (user authorized; user reminded to rotate both keys since they passed through the conversation context during diagnosis). Other voice/MCP keys in `.env` left untouched per scope of authorization. **Test coverage:** new `tests/test_heartbeat.py` (7 tests covering tool-deque population, arg-summarizer per tool type, threshold-trip, mid-call race re-check, side-channel failure handling, no-double-fire within window). Full suite 20/20 green throughout. **Two new Hard-Won Knowledge entries** captured: zombie Chrome CDP issue (identity-without-liveness pattern, generalizable to any remote-control protocol), and side-channel `claude -p` env-parity + stream-parity rule (mirror the parent spawn's env munging; log stdout AND stderr on non-zero exit because some CLIs write user-facing errors to stdout to keep stderr clean for shell pipelines). **Two memory entries saved**: `feedback_no_direct_llm_api.md` (durable rule about no LLM API key consumption ever) and `project_second_provider_resolved_no.md` (the dep-cleanup gating call). **Apple Dev cert still in flight from S198** — no movement this session, still gates 14.20.5. **Exact next step (session 206):** commit and push this session's changes (currently 8 commits ahead of origin/main from S204+S205 work). Then either continue endurance reads on remaining 🟢 catalog items, pivot to standalone workflow passes (Pass 1 install dry-run on a fresh Mac is highest-leverage; Pass 7 dep pinning; Pass 8 runbook), or take the install_preflight/readiness phantom-feature product call. `/ultrareview` + `/security-review` (Passes 5+6) remain gated on dial captions per memory. The Self-correcting MCP-hint loop entry from S204 was organically demonstrated this session (Sentry org-wide vs project-scoped miss → user correction → model self-acknowledgment with reasoning) — the manual version of that proposed feature is already happening; formalizing it (`~/.operator/hints/`, per-tool durable hints, model-prompt-time inclusion) remains queued for post-MVP per the roadmap's MCP Enhancements table.

> **Prior status: Session 204 — 1-hour-meeting endurance audit + resolved deferred `llm.py` follow-up.** New audit axis (resource/time behavior in long meetings, distinct from the static-cleanup pre-launch audit). Produced a 20-row suspect catalog across five failure modes: unbounded growth (transcript dict, tool-loop scratchpad, seen-IDs, log files), time drift (poll loops, silence-gap, heartbeat watchdog), stale handles (CDP, MCP pipes, OAuth tokens), retries, and participant flapping. **Top finding RESOLVED in commit `6b20483`:** every LLM call was re-reading the entire JSONL meeting record from disk to compute a 40-message tail; over an hour-long meeting with captions enabled this grows to MBs and adds measurable per-turn latency. User surfaced the bigger insight that captions were being prompt-stuffed at all even though the transcript MCP server already exposes them on demand — architectural duplication that also crowded chat history out of the 40-slot context budget in active meetings. Chose option (b) "keep tail but chat-only" over total deletion (chat carries a UI continuity expectation captions don't — people reference ambient talk explicitly when they want it). Fix: dropped captions from `_tail_messages`, added a `deque(maxlen=200)` chat tail in `MeetingRecord` populated by `append()`, new `tail_chat(n)` method serves it without I/O. JSONL on disk + `tail()` for generic queries unchanged. 19/19 tests green. **This closes the long-deferred `pipeline/llm.py` product decision** (`docs/pre-launch-audit.md` line 161, carried since S201). Two other 🔴/🟡 endurance findings queued for follow-up: claude_cli `_stderr_buf` accumulating every subprocess stderr byte for the meeting (deque swap fix); `macos_adapter.is_connected()` only checks an internal flag rather than actual CDP/page health, so post-sleep / network-blip the bot enters "looks alive but isn't" zombie state. **`openai` + `anthropic` Python deps decision is independent** of the llm.py question and still open — turns on "is a second provider in v1 scope?", not on how chat history is plumbed. **Exact next step (session 205):** claude_cli stderr deque fix (~1 LOC), then triage remaining 🟡 endurance items (MCP pipe death, OAuth token mid-meeting expiry, Google session mid-meeting expiry, audio helper 1hr behavior). Or pivot to standalone workflow passes (install dry-run is the highest-leverage one — `docs/pre-launch-audit.md` Pass 1, the #1 launch-day failure mode) or close the S203 phantom-feature product calls.

They wrapped the Python orchestrator in a `rumps`-based `.app` (`/Applications/Operator.app`); the Swift helper inherited a sane TCC chain. > **Prior status: Session 197 — Phase 14.20.2 + 14.20.3 SHIPPED.** **14.20.2** lands `src/_1_800_operator/swift/operator-audio-capture.swift` (288 LOC) — single binary that captures system audio via ScreenCaptureKit + mic via AVAudioEngine in parallel, writes framed `[1B tag 'S'|'M'][4B BE u32 length][N bytes Float32 16kHz mono PCM]` chunks to stdout, with per-stream 10s no-callback watchdog and TCC preflight for both Screen Recording + Microphone. Single-binary chosen over two-process design despite DECISION.md's "two procs simpler to reason about" — single cdhash means user grants TCC once per service against one binary, not twice; framing adds ~~10 LOC. Compiled clean (`swiftc -O`, 88KB). **Smoke-test results:** mic stream flowed perfectly (105 callbacks, 670KB, RMS shows real signal during `say`); system stream got zero callbacks → watchdog fired at exactly 10s with the diagnostic message DECISION.md predicted. This is the empirical replay of the spike's day-one finding — same TCC silent-failure mode (preflight true, startCapture succeeds, callbacks never fire). The SCK code path is structurally identical to voice-preserved's production `audio_capture.swift`, so this is environmental (parent-app TCC propagation, fixed by Developer-ID code-signing at release time per memory). End-to-end SCK validation belongs in 14.20.5 post code-signing. Spike-decoder helper at `debug/14_20_audio_spike/decode_frames.py` (untracked, kept for future test rigging). **14.20.3** adds `--probe` flag to the Swift binary (early-exit branch, prints `{"screen_recording":"ok|denied","microphone":"ok|denied|restricted|not_determined"}` JSON to stdout, never prompts) and two new `operator doctor` checks (`_check_screen_recording` + `_check_microphone`, gated on darwin only since dial is mac-only) that locate the binary at `~~/.operator/bin/operator-audio-capture`(production) with fallback to`src/_1_800_operator/swift/operator-audio-capture`(dev), invoke`--probe`, parse JSON, render fix instructions pointing at exact System Settings panes. > **Prior status: Session 196 — Phase 14.19.8 SHIPPED in one commit (`a30537a`).** The sterile templated `Run? tool: args\nOK?` card is gone. Inner-claude now authors the permission UX in the streaming reply path: reads narrate declaratively (`"Pulling your open Linear issues now."`) and auto-approve at the bridge; writes ask a question in the bot's voice (`"Want me to create the issue 'Vacuum my room' on Engineering?"`) and gate as before. Three reliability fixes layered on: (1) **recent-yes auto-approve** — when the user just said yes as the turn's input, the next gate auto-allows so a single approval doesn't get demanded twice (chat_runner tracks `_latest_user_msg` + `_approval_msg_ids_used`; 30s recency window); (2) **tiered bridge** — `auto_approve` lists `ToolSearch` + `Read/Grep/Glob/LS/WebSearch` + glob patterns `*__get_`*, `*__list_*`, `*__search_*`, `*__find_*`, `*__read_*`, `*__whoami` so reads never round-trip; (3) **YOLO override** — under `OPERATOR_YOLO=1` the WRITE tier flattens into the READ tier (declarative everything) and the bridge `auto_approve = ["*"]` belt-and-suspenders alongside `--dangerously-skip-permissions`. Voice rule explicitly defers to the agent's `system_prompt` persona (`"do NOT default to 'Want me to...'"`) so caveman/pirate bots speak in their own voice. **Stale comment from 14.19.2 corrected** — `--dangerously-skip-permissions` does NOT skip PreToolUse hooks (live-confirmed in S196: handler still fires under YOLO; the flag overrides denials but doesn't suppress the hook), now noted in `claude_cli._spawn`. Spike data: `debug/permission_mcp_spike/cli_probe_09_ask.py` (probed `ask` decision behavior under headless `claude -p` — model receives reason as a `tool_result` `is_error=True` and narrates it through normal reply stream) + `cli_probe_10_pre_tool_voice.py` (3/3 trials proved system-prompt steering reliably yields pre-tool voice) + `SPIKE_14_19_8_PERMISSION_VOICE.md`. The strategic call locked this session: **dial = "decide before joining"; mid-meeting handoff is impossible with CDP-attach.** Why: Chrome 121+ silently disables `--remote-debugging-port` against the user's logged-in default profile (Chromium issue 40066423, security mitigation against OAuth-token harvesting), unbypassable. Pivot: dial launches a separate Chrome window with its own profile dir at `~~/.operator/dial_profile/`. Sidesteps the restriction entirely. Trade-off accepted: if user is already in a meeting in main Chrome and wants claude, they must close that tab and rejoin via dial. **Cancelled mid-session:** Phase 14.19.3c.2-6 (Swift+ScreenCaptureKit+Whisper audio capture) — became moot once dial Chrome could be a separate (minimizable) window where DOM captions stop being magic-killing. > **Prior status: Session 175 — Zoom DOM inventory shipped end-to-end.** `docs/dom-inventory-zoom.md` covers every architecturally-critical Zoom lifecycle state: launcher page (state 1), camera + mic permission modals (2a — two sequential ReactModal dialogs, "Continue without microphone and camera" is a `<span role="button">` not `<button>`), preview + name input (2b — `#input-for-name` is the only stable hook, no placeholder/aria/name attr; Join enabled via `button.preview-join-button:not(.zm-btn--disabled)`), in-meeting toolbar (4a — aria-label hooks throughout), chat panel (4b — chat input is `div.tiptap.ProseMirror[contenteditable]` not a textarea, per-message DOM has `data-userid` + `data-name` on `.chat-item__sender` and a UUID `data-id` on the row for dedup), More menu (4c — `react-bootstrap` dropdown, `a.dropdown-item[aria-label]`), Captions submenu + first-run language modal + caption rendering (4c.1–4c.3), participants count + roster (4d — count exposed in toolbar button aria-label, `[role="application"][aria-label="<Name> (Me|Host),computer audio <state>,video <state>"]`). > **Prior status: STRATEGIC PIVOT (session 164, post-test-1.2-hardening): two-track product architecture.** Apr 25 11:00 AM PST: user re-upped $5 in Anthropic API credits last night and was already out by morning. Console showed Apr 25 = $6.50 spend across three models: Sonnet 4.5 $2.87 (matches operator's Sonnet 4.5 outer LLM in the log), Sonnet 4.6 $2.77 + Haiku 4.5 $0.87 (unaccounted by our log). Single API key in console — same one operator uses. Diagnosis (definitive proof in `~/.operator/debug/claude-stream.jsonl`): the inner `claude -p --worktree` subprocess spawned by `agents/engineer/claude_code.py` had `apiKeySource: ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` + `model: claude-sonnet-4-6` — meaning every `delegate_to_claude_code` call was billing API rates, not consuming the user's Claude Max subscription. Leak path: `pipeline/mcp_client.py:593` spawns MCP server processes with `env={**os.environ, **self._srv_config["env"]}`, operator's process loaded `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` via `load_dotenv(~/.operator/.env)`, child inherits it, claude CLI prefers env-var over claude.ai login when present. A "handful of worktrees" easily produces $3–4 of inner-Claude-Code spend because each delegate is dozens of internal LLM calls (Sonnet 4.6 sub-agents + Haiku 4.5 fast paths). API rates aren't hiked relative to subscription; rather, **subscription is heavily subsidized for the heavy-Claude-Code persona** — Max plan bills flat per month and meters by messages-per-window, not tokens, so Anthropic absorbs marginal token cost. API bills per-token with no flat cap. Same task that's effectively free under Max costs $1–3 on API. **This realization triggered a fundamental product rethink: operator today forces every user into the API-key path even when they have a Claude Code subscription that would cover their use case for free.** **The decision: pivot to a two-track architecture.** Track A — **plug-and-play claude bot**: `operator run claude` is the zero-setup zero-config zero-API-key default. Inner LLM IS the user's Claude Code (`claude -p` subprocess, subscription-billed). Brings Claude Code into a Meet, no other configuration needed. Personality + ground_rules pass through as system-prompt augmentation so the bot has meeting-tone voice (warm, brief, no walls of text) instead of solo-CLI voice. Permission MCP wires inner-claude's tool-use confirmations through Meet chat so a non-TTY caller can still gate writes. **The "claude" name is reserved for track A only** — the setup wizard no longer offers it as a choosable preset. Track B — **custom agent framework**: existing operator orchestration stays. Wizard pivots to "build a custom bot" only — the user names it themselves, picks a provider (Anthropic API / OpenAI / local model), wires their own MCPs, sets personality/ground_rules. Power-user path with the configurability we've already built. Two paths, neither with billing surprises: track A is free for Max subscribers, track B is bring-your-own-keys. The README's "Claude Code in your Google Meet" hero pitch becomes literal for track A; track B becomes the secondary "build your own meeting agent" story. **Launch is on hold pending track A.** The user explicitly: "I don't need to stop the bleeding now. I've made up my mind and want to fully pivot to this new direction now regardless of launch." All Phase 14.5 / 14.8 / 16.x dependencies pause until Phase 14.12 (the pivot) is complete. **Exact next step: Phase 14.12.1 — Permission MCP spike (1 day).** Probe whether `claude -p` exposes a Permission MCP host capability that lets a non-TTY caller (operator) intercept and resolve tool-use confirmations via Meet chat. If yes → track A is buildable as designed. If no → fall back plan needed (probably `bypassPermissions` mode for a sandboxed worktree, with the bot scoped to read-only ops outside the sandbox).

> **Prior status: session 164 shipped six commits hardening the live-test UX from Test 1.2.** (`1413318`) confirmation-decline UX fix — `chat_runner._handle_confirmation` now sends an unambiguous `[TOOL NOT EXECUTED]`-prefixed synthetic tool_result when the user replies non-yes during a pending confirm, so the LLM stops hallucinating "running, waiting for results" on a tool that never actually fired. Also added TTFT + first_flush instrumentation to `anthropic.py:complete_streaming` TIMING line — paid for itself the same session by definitively pinning a 50.3s call as `ttft=48.3s` (Anthropic-side request-queue spike, not our code). (`d0ff5a7`) stream-json side-log + live worktree progress — switched the inner claude CLI from `--output-format json` to `--output-format stream-json --verbose`, `_run_claude` reads stdout line-by-line and appends events to `~/.operator/debug/claude-stream.jsonl` (truncated per call), `chat_runner` spawns a tailer thread for `claude-code__delegate_to_claude_code` calls that posts real inner-tool_use events ("Reading config.py…", "Editing chat_runner.py…", "Running: pytest tests/test_x.py…") instead of cute placeholder verbs. Closes the demo gap where a 5-minute delegate looked like the bot was hung. (`20a6d58`) drop verb heartbeat infrastructure — deleted `pipeline/heartbeat_verbs.py` + `TOOL_HEARTBEAT_SECONDS`/`TOOL_HEARTBEAT_MAX_SECONDS` from config; `_execute_and_respond` collapsed to a `done_event.wait()` since stream-json covers claude-code progress and short MCPs (linear/github) are quick enough that placeholder pings added more noise than signal. Tests in `test_912_tool_timeout.py` rewritten to assert silent execution. (`b1b5058`) stuck-LLM watchdog with one-shot status ping — `LLM_STUCK_THRESHOLD_SECONDS=45` in config; watchdog Timer in `complete_streaming` posts `"Anthropic is taking longer than usual to respond — hang tight."` exactly once if no token has arrived by 45s. Cancel in try/finally so it doesn't fire stale on a failed call. Retry semantics deferred (would require chat-reader/dispatcher concurrency refactor; informational ping is the minimum viable). (`5af360c`) drop trailing newlines in stuck-LLM watchdog message — live retest caught a self-reply cascade: bot sent `"...hang tight.\n\n"`, Meet's DOM stripped trailing newlines on read-back, exact-text own-message dedup mismatched, bot reprocessed its own watchdog as a user prompt and the LLM looped on it. Trailing `\n\n` removed. (`1e7e3e1`) ID-based own-message dedup + stripped text-match fallback — the underlying brittleness was that `chat_runner._send` told the connector to send but never tracked the resulting `data-message-id`, so dedup relied on exact-text comparison that any DOM normalization could break. Connector contract updated: `send_chat` now returns the new `data-message-id` (macos_adapter snapshots existing IDs pre-send, polls every 50ms up to 1s for a new one to appear). ChatRunner adds the returned ID to `_seen_ids`, short-circuiting at the existing line-341 ID check. Text-match fallback hardened: `_own_messages` now stores `text.strip()`, comparison strips both sides — catches the linux-adapter (still returns None) path and the race window where the post-send DOM read times out. **Exact next step: re-run Test 1.2 (`migration-plan`) cleanly with the new dedup + stream-json + watchdog stack live; if it passes, move to Test 1.3 (`test-generation`), 1.4 (live coding delegation), Sessions 2 and 3, then Phase 15.10.5 (`operator worktrees` CLI — added this session as a deferred follow-up to ship before Phase 14.5 install.sh).** **Launch target: Apr 28–30 aspirational, May 1–2 acceptable.** MVP budget: ~5–7h remaining (session 164 burned ~2.5h on six commits + diagnosis of the cascade bug).

> **Prior status: session 163 shipped the headless bundled-Chromium pivot (`273b4b1`) + heartbeat fixed-cadence (`0d6f0e1`).** During Test 1.2 (`migration-plan` skill) the user instinctively quit Chrome to open a new browsing window — discovered macOS treats `Chrome.app` as a singleton: operator was launching the user's installed Chrome with `--user-data-dir` + `--headless=new`, but the `headless=False` Playwright flag won (so it ran *headed*), and the shared bundle ID meant the user's dock click + ⌘N got eaten by operator's process. Quitting Chrome killed the bot's tab silently and `chat_runner._send` blindly enqueued LLM paragraphs against a dead browser thread for ~70s with empty `queue.Empty` errors. Five self-contained probes in `debug/headless_meet_*.py` validated the pivot end-to-end against a real Meet URL with `heyoperator2026@gmail.com` invited: unauthed walls headless + headed equally (so the long-standing "Meet blocks headless" lore was actually "Meet blocks unauthed/uninvited"); auth + invite + headless → admitted normally; chat read (DOM observer), chat send (textarea fill + Enter), and caption observer (Shift+C + `CAPTION_OBSERVER_JS` + `__onCaption` bridge) all work in headless bundled Chromium. Root cause: `_ServerHandle.call_tool` had a hidden hardcoded `timeout=30` that silently undercut the bot's `tool_timeout_seconds: 600` config override; its `concurrent.futures.TimeoutError` stringifies to `""`, producing the empty-signature `Tool 'foo' failed:`  error line; meanwhile the asyncio task kept running and the subprocess finished the work, so the user saw both "failure" and a completed delivery. User rejected the initial two-stopwatches-with-margin proposal in favor of a single source of truth: the MCP layer owns the timeout, chat_runner only drives heartbeats. Implementation: `config.DEFAULT_TOOL_TIMEOUTS` map with ship-level defaults per MCP (claude-code 600, playwright 300, figma 90, github/salesforce 60, linear/sentry/slack/calendar/gmail/drive 30, notion 45); `_effective_timeout_for` walks override → default map → global fallback; `_ServerHandle.call_tool` now accepts a required `timeout`, cancels the task on expiry, and raises an informative `MCPToolError` that flows through the existing error signpost; `chat_runner._execute_and_respond` lost its deadline/`timed_out` branch entirely. Heartbeat became exponential (8s → 16s → 32s → 60s cap via new `TOOL_HEARTBEAT_MAX_SECONDS`). Tests: `test_912_tool_timeout.py` rewritten to match the new contract (added `test_heartbeat_interval_backs_off` + `test_mcp_timeout_is_signposted_to_llm` + `test_mcp_timeout_fallback_when_llm_fails`), `test_mcp_client_units.py` gained `test_effective_timeout_precedence`. Real safety net for transient bursts; doesn't fix single-call prompts that exceed the user's per-minute tier (those need either tier upgrade or prompt trimming). All pass. **Incidental fix:** `tests/test_skills.py` was missing `OPERATOR_BOT` default — one-line addition unblocked 5 silently-dead pre-existing LLM/ChatRunner wiring tests. **Behavioral finding confirmed (LLMClient):** captions skip the first-contact hint and don't mark the speaker as greeted — ambient talk is not a direct greeting trigger. **MCPClient race carve-out deviation:** there is no reconnect path in current code, so "tool timeout racing with reconnect" has no target; orphan-cleanup is already covered by `test_mcp_shutdown.py` — revisit if reconnect is added post-launch. Commits `e37b1c9` (tests) + `a23099b` (doc updates). **Prior status: Schema + wizard redesign shipped (session 132) — four-layer customization frame (Tools → Playbooks → Ground Rules → Personality) with yaml split and 7-step wizard.** User flagged that the three central customization levers (system prompt, MCPs, skills) had overlapping properties and no internal terminology signalling how they build on each other. Mapped the ambiguity and locked a four-layer frame with wizard-facing labels: Tools (MCPs) → Playbooks (Skills) → Ground Rules → Personality. Implementation split `llm.system_prompt` into two top-level yaml blocks (`personality` + `ground_rules`), composed at load time as `personality\n\nground_rules` so rules land last and get LLM end-of-prompt weighting. Hard cut — all three bundled bots migrated in same commit, no backward-compat shim. Uniform split rule: voice/identity → personality, always-true constraints → ground_rules. Only the text differs across bots; designer's personality kept its opinion-forward register ("That spacing is cramped — bump it to 16px" is the register), engineer's ground rules preserved the full tool-routing + delegation blocks. Wizard grew 5 → 7 steps with instructional copy on each: step 2 "Tools (MCPs)", step 3 "Playbooks (Skills)", step 4 "Ground Rules", step 5 "Personality", step 6 API keys, step 7 atomic write. Steps 4+5 pop `$EDITOR` (via `VISUAL` then `EDITOR` then `vi` fallback) with two modes — edit-preset gets a two-path picker (inherit-with-cursor vs start-blank), from-scratch is always blank. Wizard pedagogical order is ground_rules → personality (opposite of concatenation order — more intuitive to author rules first, then voice). `agents/README.md` gained a new "Anatomy of a bot" section naming the four layers and explaining the compose order; field reference tables updated (removed `llm.system_prompt` row, added new top-level `personality`/`ground_rules` tables). `CLAUDE.md` config bullet list rewritten to match. Tests: `test_setup.py` fixtures cleaned (`system_prompt` removed from llm blocks), `_step5_write` → `_step7_write` renamed. Commit `1fdbc4e`. **Not yet live-tested.** Pick up with live-smoke (intro-on-join from 131 still unvalidated too), then `docs/test-plan.md` Component B (MeetingRecord), then pre-existing `test_912` failure, then 13.2 log cleanup → 15.6 → 14 → 15 → 16. Budget: ~~14h vs April 19 launch (day-of). **Prior status: Self-intro on join shipped (session 131) — discoverability fix, not a roadmap-phase item.** Strategic conversation surfaced a real product gap: a user joining a meeting with Operator has no idea what the bot can actually do, and no idea where to tweak/shape its behavior. Mapped the four steering surfaces (tools = capability, system prompt = identity/always-on, MCP hints = server-scoped framing, skills = playbooks) and concluded the abstraction is right — what's missing is *visibility*. User scoped a one-toggle solution: new `agent.intro_on_join: true` field (defaulted true on pm/designer/engineer); on join, the bot generates a 2-sentence self-intro via the LLM (using already-injected skills + MCP context, no message history) and posts it to chat. Implementation lives in three places: `config.py` reads the flag; `LLMClient.intro()` fires a single `provider.complete` call with a strict prompt (2 sentences, "I can…" framing, no tool/MCP terminology, no greeting filler — focuses on outcomes/use cases to inspire actual usage); `ChatRunner` runs generation in a background thread (`_generate_intro`) so the polling loop starts immediately, with the main loop owning the actual `send_chat` call to keep Playwright single-threaded. Messages that land during the ~2s generation window are persisted to the meeting record as normal but their LLM dispatch is deferred — buffered into `_pre_intro_buffer` and drained in order on the first iteration after `_intro_ready` fires. On generation failure: log + skip silently (per user — fake-success masks the real problem; if the LLM is broken the next message will surface it honestly). Reconnect re-intros (no per-meeting deduplication — explicit edge-case skip per user). Updated `docs/test-plan.md` Notes section so the next session's test inventory must include intro-on-join coverage in components A (config loader), C (LLMClient), and E (ChatRunner). **Not yet live-tested** — `operator try pm` is the cheapest sanity check (TerminalConnector skips the join wait so intro fires within ~2s of boot); real Meet test via `operator pm`. Pick up from: live-smoke the intro on a real Meet, then start walking the test plan at Component B (MeetingRecord) per the per-session protocol. Carried-over: `test_912::test_timeout_sends_failure_message` still broken from session 129 (pre-existing MagicMock issue). Budget: ~16h remaining vs April 19 launch (day-of). **Prior status: Phase 15.5.7 fully shipped — live-smoked end-to-end via`operator try engineer`(session 127, commit`2a7de34`).** Live smoke surfaced one tangential bug in` pipeline/chat_runner.py`unrelated to the delegate path itself: the harness's tool-confirmation prompt ("I'd like to run X. OK?") was being persisted to the meeting record as`kind="chat"`, then replayed back to the model on the next turn — the model started mimicking the pattern verbatim as plain text *before* raising its hand for a real` tool_call`. Two visible symptoms: (a) every confirmed tool call required the user to type "ok" twice (once to the model's parroted prompt, once to the harness's real one), (b) sometimes after the first "ok" the model just hallucinated a result instead of emitting the real` tool_call`— caught live when Engineer claimed`/tmp/test-delegate-2`contained`README.md`when it actually contained`f.txt`(a file from a different repo's earlier turn). Root cause:`_send()`had no way to distinguish harness plumbing from real conversation; both ended up in the same`kind="chat"`bucket that`pipeline/llm.py:155-157`'s` tail()`-replay reads from. Fix:` _send(text, kind="chat")`now takes an optional`kind`;` _request_confirmation()`passes`kind="confirmation"`; the inbound-message persistence in` _loop()`tags the user's reply with`"confirmation"`whenever`_pending_tool_call`is set. Confirmations stay in the JSONL audit trail but the LLM prompt-builder skips them (only`chat`and`caption`are replayed), so the model literally cannot see the pattern it was mimicking. Re-ran the smoke after the fix — single confirmation prompt per call, repo-2 listing returned ground truth, per-repo session isolation intact (three independent sandboxes coexist across`/tmp/test-delegate/.claude/worktrees/sorted-shimmying-shore`,` /tmp/test-delegate/.claude/worktrees/vivid-mapping-hoare`,` /tmp/test-delegate-2/.claude/worktrees/dynamic-inventing-owl`). 15.5.7 done. Pick up with **Phase 13 — log cleanup (~2h) + 13.1 gap check (~30m)** — 13.1 was flagged by the user at session 124 start as "actually incomplete" and the specific gap still hasn't been captured. Ask the user what remains under 13.1 before touching 13.2. Budget: ~19h vs April 19 launch. **Prior status: Phase 15.5.7 shipped in session 126 (commit` 23bf258`) — delegate multi-repo + per-repo continuity + land flow.** Live` operator try engineer`run at session start exposed three coupled regressions in the delegate path: (1) every call spawned a fresh`--worktree`so follow-ups couldn't see prior files and the LLM silently re-created state; (2) sandbox worktree paths were never surfaced, so Engineer reported "confirmed working" for files the user would never find in their working tree; (3) delegate was hard-pinned to whatever repo Operator launched from — effectively "only edit the Operator repo," which is the wrong default for almost every user. Fix rolled into one rewrite of`agents/engineer/delegate_to_claude_code.py`:` delegate_to_claude_code(task, repo_path)`where`repo_path`is required; module-level`_SESSIONS: dict[str, {session_id, worktree_path, base_sha}]`scoped by canonical repo path. First call per repo runs`claude -p --worktree`with`cwd=repo_path`, diffs` git worktree list --porcelain`before/after to recover the worktree, stores the session id from JSON output. Follow-ups run`claude -p --resume **`with`cwd=worktree_path`(the key insight from verification:`--resume`looks up sessions by project dir = cwd, and you MUST NOT pass`--worktree`on resume or it spawns a new sandbox). Falls back to fresh worktree if resume returns "No conversation found." New`land_worktree_changes(repo_path)`tool stages all changes in the worktree (Claude Code leaves new files untracked so a naive`git diff`misses them), diffs against`base_sha`captured at first call, and applies into the user's working tree — fails cleanly on divergence. Tool result footer carries`[workdir: ...]`+`[repo: ...]`; Engineer's system prompt + delegate hints teach the model to ask for` repo_path`on first delegation, reuse it for follow-ups, mention the workdir when reporting back, and offer to land after success. README gains "How delegation works" section. Spec doc at`docs/delegate_multi_repo_spec.md`. Verified in isolation on three` /tmp/`fixture repos — create/resume-read/land round-trip clean, two repos in parallel hold independent sessions, no cross-contamination. **Not yet live-smoked via`operator try engineer`— explicit 6-step test plan saved to`docs/handoff.md`for session 127 kickoff.** Pick up with that smoke, then Phase 13 log cleanup (~2h) + 13.1 gap check (~30m). Stack dump showed the Playwright greenlet event loop wedged on`kqueue.control(None, ...)`inside`sync_playwright.**exit`**→`playwright.stop()`→ greenlet`run_as_sync`— the Node driver's CDP socket is dead (Chrome self-exits in`--headless=new`after Leave click) but the greenlet is waiting for responses that never arrive. Removing the explicit`browser.close()`alone wasn't enough: the same wedge can happen in the context-manager exit. Fix landed in`connectors/macos_adapter.py`: new` _kill_playwright_drivers()`helper`pgrep -P **`s for` playwright/driver/node ... cli.js run-driver`child processes;`leave()`now does`_browser_thread.join(timeout=2)`→ if still alive, SIGKILL the driver directly → re-join 2s. Killing the driver unblocks the kqueue.select and lets the greenlet exit cleanly. Also fixed a secondary symptom: a stray`participant count changed 2 → 0`log appearing *after`*left meeting`— added`if self._stop_event.is_set(): break`guards in`ChatRunner._loop()`after`read_chat()`and`get_participant_count() `so a blocked call finishing during SIGINT handling doesn't dial through one more iteration. Verified live: 3 clean pm runs (happy path ~1s shutdown, no safety-net line) + one tool-call run that hit the wedge and recovered in 3.1s (`force-killed stuck Playwright driver pid=84330`→`left meeting`4ms later, no outer Safety net line, no stray participant-count log). **Prior status (session 115) — Phase 15.5.3 LIVE-VALIDATED end-to-end.** Auto-admit confirmed working:`operator pm`→ meet.new spins a fresh room → human knocks → tray-click admits →`participant count 1 → 2`. Two iterations to land it. **Iter 1:** added post-action "pill gone" verification; revealed that admission actually succeeded *but* Meet leaves the "Admit N guest" pill widget sticky in the DOM (visible, not hidden) even after the guest is admitted, so a "wait for pill to disappear" verifier loops forever and a keyboard-fallback path was logging false-positive "admitted" lines every 2s. **Iter 2 (the fix):** swapped verification from pill-disappearance to **participant-count delta** (poll` _do_get_participant_count`for up to 3s after click; success = count went up). Added a`(pill_text, participant_count)`cooldown so a stale pill silently skips re-attempts until either text or count changes. Result: clean log of`admit pill detected text='Admit 1 guest' count=1`→`admit_btn count=1 visible=True`→`admitted via tray click (verified — participant count 1 → 2)`and then silence — no spam. New diagnostic snapshot`debug/post_admit_success.{png,html}`saved on verified admission. Found three issues, fixed all three, retested clean. (1) `LLMClient` and the captions path were holding two different `MeetingRecord` instances because `__main__.py` constructed the LLM before the record existed and never wired them — every `@operator` call returned 400 `messages: at least one message is required` whenever captions were enabled. (2) Same-speaker continuations were persisted as "prior + new" because Meet keeps the prior caption text visible in the same speaker's region; ported the `_normalize_for_match` token-prefix idea from `voice-preserved/pipeline/captions.py` into a new `_strip_prior_prefix` helper that's tolerant of Meet's casing/punctuation rewrites between finalizes.
