All 12 tests passed (Test 5 skipped per doc; Test 3 config-driven proof skipped). Confirm flow + correction re-propose works (`save_issue` `demo` → MOJ-16; `foo`→`gloo` correction → MOJ-17). Tool-loop scratchpad never persists (zero `tool_use`/`tool_result` lines on disk). Alone-exit grace fired at 61s. Two minor non-blockers noted: one DOM-poll missed a bare `ok` confirmation (recovered on retry), and the LLM occasionally needs a nudge to surface non-addressed context. Closed the session by auditing `CLAUDE.md` against the post-11.3a codebase — fixed three stale sections (architecture overview missing `meeting_record.py`, data-flow describing pre-11.3a "rolling history", config block listing wrong fields under `agent`/`llm`/`connector`). **Session 97 (April 14)** — positioning session after competitive research surfaced [joinly](https://github.com/joinly-ai/joinly) as a near-peer (multi-platform, voice, MCP, BYOLLM, MIT, hosted cloud, shipped 6+ months ago). Response: lean into **"Claude Code in your Google Meet"** as the launch framing and **opinionated quickstart** as the implicit differentiator. Added new **Phase 15.5 (Opinionated Quickstart)** — agents gallery + minimal `operator setup` wizard + a second chat-native agent slot. `agents/` directory created with format `README.md`; `claude-code` is the canonical starter. `docs/mvp-bar.md` updated with sharpened 3-part differentiation and a new Launch Strategy section (hero framings, visual hooks, distribution ranking, gallery as distribution primitive). Session 96 shipped 11.3a — per-meeting JSONL at `~/.operator/history/<slug>.jsonl` as the single source of truth for chat history. Phase 11 remaining: 11.3b (captions, ~~3h), 11.4 (skill loading, ~2h), 11.5 (Claude Code skill import, ~2h), 11.7 (provider keys optional, ~15m). 11.6 absorbed into 11.3a. After Phase 11: Phase 12 validation, 13 polish, 14 package, 15 cross-platform testing, 15.5 opinionated quickstart (new), 16 launch. Fast-follow audit items remain opportunistic. Post-MVP: Hosted Operator (~~30-35h). Zero-telemetry intact.

## Phase 14.19: Bridge architecture cutover — dial/dial/deploy (~3 days) ← BLOCKS LAUNCH

> **⏸ Steps 14.19.7 F/G/H + 14.19.8 + 14.19.9 + 14.19.10 + 14.19.11 are SUPERSEDED by Phase 14.22 (S210 architecture pivot).** The remaining bridge-architecture deletion + permission-flow rewrite + install-script copy + ladder live-test + docs refresh all collapse into the dial-only + plugin-form-factor work of 14.22. dial/deploy/login deletions land in 14.22.4; the audit pass in 14.22.5 catches anything 14.19.7's earlier sub-steps left behind.

*Strategic pivot, session 190. Cut the entire custom-bot-construction surface from v0.0.1. Operator stops being "a meeting-bot platform" (a category nobody currently shops for) and becomes "the way to bring the Claude you already trust into your Google Meet" (a category that maps to a real, immediate desire).*

### Why this pivot

The wizard, the agent presets (`pm`/`engineer`/`designer`), the `system_prompt` composition layer, the multi-agent dispatch — all of it asks users to evaluate **a bot Operator constructed**, before they've decided they trust AI presence in meetings at all. That's a backwards trust ladder. The bridge model inverts it: Operator becomes a *thin meeting-presence layer* over a tool the user already has and trusts (Claude Code). Trust transfers; we don't have to earn it from scratch.

This is also a massive code reduction. We delete the wizard, the edit command, the `OPERATOR_BOT` env-routing, the `agents/` directory, the entire `agent`/`llm`/`mcp_servers`/`skills`/`system_prompt` config schema, `.env` loading, `READ_TOOLS` allowlist, much of `config.py`. Conservatively half the codebase. Less to slop, less to support, less to test.

The custom-bot work isn't lost — it's deferred to its right product moment as **Operator Studio** (see Post-MVP). Ships when users have already trusted AI presence in meetings and *now* want to compose their own.

### The three-rung ladder (locked verbs)

**dial → dial → deploy.** Each rung escalates one variable while holding others constant:

- `**operator dial claude [meet-url]`** — Claude responds *as you*; no second account; no separate participant. Lowest stakes. CDP-attach to user's existing Chrome session. Replies surface through your identity with a marker (default: `🤖`  prefix, pending iteration — see step 14.19.6) so the room knows what's you and what's Claude. This is the entry rung; most users start here.
- `**operator dial claude [meet-url]*`* — Claude has its own identity; you and Claude join a *fresh* Meet together; no other participants. Private one-on-one with AI. Echoes the 1-800-Operator brand metaphor. Good for solo brainstorms, voice-style sessions, transcribed interviews with yourself. Requires `operator login claude` to have been run once.
- `**operator deploy claude <meet-url>*`* — Claude has its own identity; joins your existing meeting with real participants. Full commitment, full visibility. Used for note-taking, project management, real-time research while you focus on the people. Requires `operator login claude`.

`--yolo` flag available on all three: maps to spawning `claude` with `--dangerously-skip-permissions`. Default is ask-mode (claude pauses per-tool; Operator surfaces the prompt in Meet chat; user types y/n in chat to forward back).

### v0.0.1 = claude only

Codex and Gemini are explicit fast-follows, not launch blockers. The Phase 14.18B codex parity work (already shipped) gets re-homed under v0.0.2 once the bridge architecture is stable. v0.0.1 ships one bridge done extremely well.

### Zero user-facing config files

No `.env`. No `config.yaml`. No user-editable settings of any kind. Everything is hardcoded code constants in `bridges/claude.py`. Persistent state files in `~/.operator/` are runtime state only (`auth_state.json`, `browser_profile/`, `history/`, `debug/`) — written by code, never human-edited.

If a user wants persistent `--yolo` behavior, the answer is a shell alias. Operator stays config-free.

### Steps

| 14.19.1       | **Create `bridges/claude.py`** with hardcoded constants: spawn cmd (`claude -p --output-format stream-json --include-partial-messages --resume? ...`), trigger phrase (`@claude`), default reply prefix, transcript-MCP wiring. ~50 LOC replacing the entire current `agents/claude/config.yaml` + per-agent config-loading machinery.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   | ✅                                                                       | ~2h                                                                      |
| 14.19.2       | **Wire the three commands** in `__main__.py` — `dial`, `dial`, `deploy`. Each runs its own JIT preflight (claude binary check, `claude auth status`, Chrome present, plus `auth_state.json` for dial/deploy). All three accept `--yolo` which appends `--dangerously-skip-permissions` to the spawn cmd. `dial` keeps current "open `meet.new`" semantics; `deploy` is the renamed `dial <name> <url>` path; `dial` is new (CDP attach).                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 | ✅                                                                       | ~3h                                                                      |
| 14.19.3       | **Implement `dial` mode (CDP attach) — separate-profile model.** Original plan was to attach to the user's existing Chrome. **S192 finding:** Chrome 121+ silently disables `--remote-debugging-port` against the user's logged-in default profile (Chromium issue 40066423, security mitigation against OAuth-token harvesting via DevTools, unbypassable). Pivoted to launching a **dedicated Chrome window** under operator's own profile dir (`~/.operator/dial_profile/`) with the meeting URL — sidesteps the restriction entirely. UX consequence: dial is "decide BEFORE joining"; mid-meeting handoff into an already-active Meet tab is not technically possible with CDP-attach. Documented as accepted v1 constraint; mid-meeting attach would require a Chrome extension (Post-MVP). Landed shape: `connectors/attach_adapter.py` (~330 lines) launches via `open -na 'Google Chrome' --args --remote-debugging-port=9222 --user-data-dir=DIAL_PROFILE_DIR --remote-allow-origins=* <url>`, probes CDP for already-running dial Chrome (instant re-attach), silently evicts non-dial Chromes from port 9222 via SIGTERM, waits for user to click 'Join now' (indefinite poll on the 'Leave call' button — no timeout, lobby admission can take many minutes). On leave: detach CDP only; dial Chrome stays running so the meeting continues.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                | ✅                                                                       | ~5h actual ~10h                                                          |
| 14.19.3-quiet | **Quiet mode for dial.** ChatRunner gains `quiet_mode` flag. When True (dial): no intro generated/sent, no "Hold for {agent}…" filler, 1-on-1 trigger bypass disabled (always require `@claude`). Dial/deploy default to False. Also fixed self-reply cascade: AttachAdapter.read_chat strips the reply_prefix (🤖 ) from observed messages so ChatRunner's text-match dedup against `_own_messages` matches. Without this fix, the bot's own prefixed messages got read back as new user input, triggering an infinite reply loop.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      | ✅                                                                       | ~1h                                                                      |
| 14.19.4       | **Implement `operator login claude`** — single-purpose command, not a wizard. Opens Chrome via Playwright, navigates to accounts.google.com, persists `auth_state.json` after sign-in. Lifted from the existing wizard's step-2 auth code. Idempotent — running twice refreshes session. No name-your-bot, no trigger-phrase prompt, no system-prompt composition. Just the auth dance.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  | ✅ S193 (`ac93e89`)                                                      | ~1.5h actual ~30m                                                        |

Prints checklist: claude binary present, claude logged in, Chrome installed, git installed, `auth_state.json` exists (notes "only needed for dial/deploy"). For each missing item, prints the exact fix command. No decisions, no creativity, no construction.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       | ✅ S193 (`3c1dc52`)                                                      | ~1h actual ~45m                                                          |

Test in a real Meet, eye-check what reads cleanest at a glance. Hardcode the winner in `bridges/claude.py`. No user-facing config knob.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        | ✅ S193 (`82694ff`) — winner: hybrid `[🤖 Claude]` (brackets+emoji+name) | ~30m actual ~20m                                                         |

### Post-MVP — dial-related items deferred from S192

The dial pivot to the separate-profile model (14.19.3) closed the original CDP-attach-to-existing-Chrome path. These items would re-open it or expand dial's reach; sequenced as follow-ups, not v1 blockers.

- **First-run sign-in friction.** Fresh dial profile drops the user on Google's sign-in flow inside the dial Chrome window. They figure it out without help. A friendly preflight in `_run_dial` ("first time slipping — sign into the window that just opened, then come back") would smooth the corner. ~30m work.
- **Mid-meeting handoff.** `operator handoff <url>` command that detects user is already in the meeting on main Chrome, instructs them to close that tab, then launches dial. Doesn't bypass the "decide before joining" constraint but smooths the awkward "wait, switch windows" moment when the user changes their mind mid-meeting. ~30m work.
- **Default URL handler.** Register operator as the macOS default app for `meet.google.com` URLs via Info.plist URL scheme. Every Meet link auto-routes to dial, eliminating the pre-planning problem at the OS level. ~2-3h work + first-run hook to ask the user if they want to set it as default.
- **Browser extension.** The only path that delivers "claude joins my existing meeting tab on a whim" mid-meeting. Different distribution (Chrome Web Store), different permission model (extensions can DOM-access without `--remote-debugging-port`), ~1-2 weeks of focused work + content-script architecture + IPC daemon. Reserved for after v0.0.1 ships and we have signal on whether mid-meeting handoff is what users actually ask for.

**Phase total: ~~22h (~~3 days).**

### Decisions locked from S190 conversation

- **Verbs: `dial / dial / deploy`.** Considered and rejected: `merge` (git collision, doesn't carry try-feel), `channel` (too metaphysical), `patch` (more about connecting than blending), `tag` (wrestling sub implies tag-out), `pair` (too software-jargon). `dial` is the entry rung's right-feel; `dial` keeps the brand metaphor; `deploy` carries appropriate commitment-weight for the public-meeting rung.
- **Trigger phrase: `@claude` (hardcoded).** No per-bot configurability. Edge case (user's actual name is Claude) is acceptable collateral.
- `**--yolo` is the only permission flag.** Maps to claude's `--dangerously-skip-permissions`. No `--allowedTools`/`--disallowedTools` exposed in v0.0.1.
- **No persistent permission preference.** Shell alias if a user wants persistent yolo. Stays consistent with zero-config-file goal.
- **Reply prefix: pending iteration.** Three candidates (brackets / robot emoji / italics) get mocked side-by-side; user picks; hardcoded. Robot emoji is the leading default.
- `**operator login claude` is not a wizard** — single-purpose auth command. Renaming away from the `setup` namespace deliberately to avoid evoking the deleted wizard surface.
- **Operator delegates MCP auth + skill management entirely to claude.** Operator's only "is the world ready" check is "does claude itself work." The transitive correctness of claude's GitHub MCP / Linear MCP / etc. is claude's problem, surfaced to the user via `claude mcp list` if they want to investigate. Operator does not duplicate this surface.

### Carry-overs that survive the cutover

- **Phase 14.18 transcript MCP** stays in v0.0.1 — it's the bridge's killer add over "just run claude in your terminal next to a Meet window." Ships unchanged at `mcp_servers/transcript_server.py`. The `~/.operator/.current_meeting` marker file mechanism (Phase 14.18.B1/B2) becomes the canonical way the transcript server finds the active meeting in dial/dial/deploy modes.
- **Phase 14.17 `--resume` crash recovery** stays — implemented inside the bridge, transparent to the user.
- **Captions** stay enabled by default (the YAML toggle disappears, the captions-on default behavior in `connectors/macos_adapter.py` remains).
- `**READ_TOOLS` allowlist DELETED.** Permission policy fully delegated to claude. Two states only: ask-mode (claude prompts per-tool) or yolo-mode (claude skips). No hybrid.

### Done when

Three commands work end-to-end on a fresh Mac. Zero user-editable config files exist. The `agents/` directory is gone. The wizard is gone. `operator doctor` cleanly reports world-readiness. The README and `CLAUDE.md` describe a thin bridge product, not a bot platform.

---

## Phase 14.20: Dial caption capture — Swift + ScreenCaptureKit + Whisper (~2-3 days) ← BLOCKS LAUNCH

*Promoted from Post-MVP in S193. v0.0.1 promised caption parity across bots (Phase 14.18 framing). Dial currently has zero caption capture in AttachAdapter — `@claude what did the other person just say` returns nothing — which breaks that promise for the entry-rung command. Closing the gap is launch-gating.*

### Why Swift + ScreenCaptureKit + Whisper, not DOM captions

S192 considered DOM captions in dial Chrome (cheap, ~1-2h, reuses `captions_js.py`). Rejected: dial Chrome is the user's visible window, Meet's caption overlay would render on top of their meeting view. The "minimize the dial window" workaround is fragile UX — users will forget, captions will surprise them mid-call, and the magic of dial ("claude is just there, invisible") collapses. The Swift pipeline keeps dial Chrome clean — captions are derived from system audio + mic, never from Meet's UI.

Trade-off accepted: two macOS permissions (Screen Recording for system audio capture via ScreenCaptureKit, Microphone for the user's voice). Both are first-run prompts, both surface in `operator doctor` (Phase 14.19.5). Granola does the same; users tolerate it because the resulting transcript quality is materially better than DOM captions (no auto-correction garbage, full speaker separation, latency ~1s vs Meet's 3-5s).

### Sequence and parallelism

Independent of 14.19.4–11 — the audio pipeline doesn't touch any bridge code. Develop in parallel after 14.19.6 lands (so dial's reply-attribution UX is locked first), and **before 14.19.10** so the end-to-end ladder live-test exercises captions too. Final integration into the ladder live-test happens in 14.19.10.

### Carry-over from cancelled S192 scope

The cancelled "Phase 14.19.3c.2 through 14.19.3c.6" (audio capture + Whisper) had already framed the dual-stream merger + permissions story before being dropped for the CDP-attach pivot. Design notes survive in handoff S192 § "Dropped from S192's plan" and roadmap context. Spike artifacts at `debug/resume_spike/` are CDP-related (different domain, not audio); 14.20 starts a fresh spike directory.


| Step    | Description                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                | Status                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   | Time           |
| ------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ | -------------- |
| 14.20.1 | **Spike: ScreenCaptureKit system-audio tap + Whisper streaming.** Validate latency budget on a real Meet — target <2s caption-to-meeting-record latency to compete with Meet's DOM captions. Compare `whisper.cpp` vs `mlx-whisper` (already a dependency on the voice-preserved branch) for streaming throughput on M-series Macs. Deliverable: a 30-line Swift script that prints transcribed system audio to stdout in real time, plus a decision doc on the STT engine. Spike artifacts in `debug/14_20_audio_spike/`. | ✅ S193 — see `debug/14_20_audio_spike/{spike_capture.swift,STT_COMPARISON.md,DECISION.md}`. Locked: mlx-whisper-base (110ms inference, 4× faster than whisper.cpp on M-series), latency budget ~1.7s e2e, two parallel pipelines for mic+system speaker attribution, Developer-ID code-signing is a day-one requirement (not polish — empirically confirmed via TCC silent-failure observed during runtime test).                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        | ~4h actual ~6h |
| 14.20.2 | **Swift helper binary — dual-stream capture.** Single Swift binary that captures system audio (ScreenCaptureKit) + mic (AVFoundation) simultaneously, merges to a single mono PCM stream with speaker tags (`[mic]` vs `[system]`), and writes either to a Unix socket or stdout in a framed format AttachAdapter can read. Build target: `~/.operator/bin/operator-audio-capture`. Built via `swiftc` in `install.sh` on macOS (skipped on Linux — dial is mac-only anyway).                                              | ✅ S197 — `src/_1_800_operator/swift/operator-audio-capture.swift` (288 LOC). Single-binary chosen over two-proc (one cdhash → cleaner TCC UX). Framed stdout `[1B tag 'S'|'M'][4B BE u32 length][N bytes Float32]`. Per-stream 10s watchdog, TCC preflight both perms. Mic path validated end-to-end (AVAudioConverter 48kHz hw → 16kHz target). System path structurally identical to voice-preserved's prod binary; smoke-test triggered the predicted TCC silent-failure (parent-app cdhash propagation), confirming watchdog logic. | 14.20.3 | **macOS permission UX.** First-run prompts for Screen Recording + Microphone surface naturally via the Swift binary's first call (TCC dialogs). `operator doctor` (14.19.5) gains two checks: TCC status for both permissions via `tccutil`/`sqlite3` query against the TCC database, with exact "fix it" guidance ("System Settings → Privacy & Security → Screen Recording → enable for terminal/iTerm").                                                                                                                | ✅ S197 — `--probe` flag on the helper (read-only TCC report via `CGPreflightScreenCaptureAccess()` + `AVCaptureDevice.authorizationStatus(for: .audio)`, prints JSON to stdout, never prompts). `doctor.py` gains `_check_screen_recording` + `_check_microphone` (darwin-only) plus `_audio_helper()` locator preferring `~/.operator/bin/` with `src/_1_800_operator/swift/` fallback. Fix copy points at exact System Settings panes. TCC.db SIP-protection rules out direct sqlite3 query → in-process probe is the only supported path (DECISION.md §2). Smoke-tested both happy + missing-binary paths. Cosmetic: empty `fix:` lines suppressed in `run_doctor()`. | ~1h            |
| 14.20.4 | **Wire into AttachAdapter + MeetingRecord.** AttachAdapter spawns the Swift helper as a subprocess on `join()`; reads framed PCM-or-text output; pipes Whisper output into `MeetingRecord.append_caption()` using the same JSONL shape as `captions_js.py`. The transcript MCP (`mcp_servers/transcript_server.py`) reads the same record file → zero changes there. Dial captions appear in `~/.operator/history/<slug>.jsonl` indistinguishable from dial/deploy captions.                                               | ⬜                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        | ~3h            |
| 14.20.5 | **Live-test on a real Meet.** Run `operator dial claude <url>`, speak a distinctive phrase aloud, ask `@claude what did I just say`. Verify (a) caption captured within ~2s, (b) stored in MeetingRecord JSONL, (c) transcript MCP serves it back to claude correctly, (d) speaker attribution (mic vs system) preserved. Then: same battery against another participant on the call (system audio path).                                                                                                                  | ✅ S207 (system-audio leg) — phone-in-another-room → SCStream → mlx-whisper → meeting JSONL validated end-to-end with the notarized `.app` (`com.1-800-operator.audio-capture`). First three runs hit a wrong-binary bug: `uv tool install`'d `~/.local/share/uv/tools/1-800-operator/` had a pre-S206 resolver pointing at the standalone ad-hoc `~/.operator/bin/operator-audio-capture` (`com.operator.audio-capture`) — different TCC identity from the one the user granted. `uv tool install --force --reinstall` picked up the new resolver, prompt fired cleanly, frames flowed. Mic leg + `@claude what did the other person say` round-trip remaining for S208. Three follow-up TODOs queued (mic-mute privacy gate, TCC pre-prompt UX, doctor probes for both perms) — see Phase 14.21 below.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  | ~2h            |


**Phase total: ~~17h (~~2-3 days).**

### Done when

Dial captions match dial/deploy captions in latency and quality; both macOS permissions prompt cleanly on first run; `operator doctor` reports both as green; live-test on a real Meet shows `@claude what did the other person just say` returning a correct answer.

---

## Phase 14.21: Dial captions hardening — privacy + UX gaps surfaced in S207 live-test

*Three TODOs surfaced during the S207 14.20.5 live-test that aren't in 14.20's "done when" but are pre-launch necessary. Privacy item is highest-priority — anything that hits the meeting JSONL is reachable via `@claude what did I just say`, so muted speech leaking is a real bug.*

> **S209 prereq landed (commit `231c864`).** Before any of the items below could be exercised, the BT HFP exclusivity bug had to be fixed — `AVAudioEngine.inputNode` loses to Chrome's WebRTC over Bluetooth HFP and silently delivers zero-filled buffers to the second binder. Replaced the mic path with `SCStream.captureMicrophone` (macOS 15+) plus dynamic resampler + `kAudioHardwarePropertyDefaultInputDevice` listener that drives stream restart on device change. Validated against AirPods + Bose + built-in across the 14_21_mic_capture_spike rig and a live Meet. Mic-leg E2E gate closed. See `docs/agent-context.md` Hard-Won Knowledge entry "AVAudioEngine.inputNode loses Bluetooth HFP races to Chrome's WebRTC" for the full debugging arc and the gotchas a future session needs to know.

| Step    | Description | Status | Time |
| ------- | ----------- | ------ | ---- |
| 14.21.1 | **Mic-mute privacy gate.** Detect Meet's mic-toggle DOM state via a third MutationObserver in `attach_adapter.py` (same shape as `chat_dom_js.py` + `captions_js.py`); on mute, gate `feed_audio` for the `M` `AudioProcessor` and DROP the mid-utterance buffer (don't just pause — otherwise a half-finalized pre-mute utterance leaks on next silence boundary). Don't gate the `S` stream (system audio is "what other people said to me," no privacy expectation). Optional: write a `{kind: "mic_muted", t_start, t_end}` gap row to JSONL on unmute so `@claude what did I say at 3:14?` can answer "you were muted 3:13–3:15" instead of silently producing nothing. **~50ms race window** between mute-press and observer-fire is acceptable for typical privacy-aside use; don't oversell as "privacy-guaranteed." Verify dial-mode parity — Meet's caption DOM may already suppress your captions when muted; if so, dial is private-by-default and only dial needs the gate. | ⬜ | ~3h |
| 14.21.2 | **TCC pre-prompt at first-run, not first sound.** Today the Screen Recording prompt fires when the first audio frame would land — usually mid-meeting — which is the worst possible moment. Granola does this at install. Easiest win: spawn the helper for ~3s as part of `operator login` (the existing one-time auth step) purely to trigger the prompt while the user is sitting at the terminal expecting setup work. Even better: put the pre-prompt in `install.sh` so it runs during `curl ... | sh`. Helper already has `--probe` mode for exactly this. **Doctor expansion**: `operator doctor` should run `--probe` and surface both `kTCCServiceScreenCapture` AND `kTCCServiceMicrophone` results, with copy pointing at exact System Settings panes for the helper's notarized identity (`com.1-800-operator.audio-capture`). | ⬜ | ~2h |
| 14.21.3 | **Whisper accuracy — observe before acting.** S207 verified the model matches voice-preserved exactly (`mlx-community/whisper-base-mlx`, size `base`, no regression). The "Hosting" mishearing the user observed is whisper-base's known character on short low-context phrases. Voice-preserved supported `tiny | base | small | medium` as YAML; current operator hardcodes `base`. **Don't act yet** — collect 3-5 real-meeting samples first to see if it's actually a problem in context (real meetings have far more surrounding context per utterance than synthetic test phrases). If yes: bump to `small` (one constant edit at `pipeline/audio.py:47`, ~3× model size, ~2× latency). | ⬜ observation-only | ~0.5h decide / 0.5h ship |
| 14.21.4 | **Hide audio helper from Dock + Cmd-Tab switcher.** The notarized `operator-audio-capture.app` currently shows in the Dock when launched as a subprocess from `AttachAdapter` — visual clutter the user notices on every meeting. Add `LSUIElement = true` (or `LSBackgroundOnly = true`) to the bundle's `Info.plist` so it runs as a background process with no Dock icon, no Cmd-Tab presence, and no menu bar. Rebuild via `scripts/build_signed_helper.sh`, re-notarize. **Heads-up:** changing Info.plist changes the cdhash, which TCC keys on — first run after the new build will re-prompt for Screen Recording + Microphone permissions even on machines that previously granted them. Pair with 14.21.2's pre-prompt UX so the re-grant lands during setup, not mid-meeting. Verify: launch helper from terminal, confirm no Dock icon appears, confirm captures still flow, confirm the notarization signature still validates (`spctl -a -vv`). | ⬜ | ~1h |

### Done when

Muting the Meet mic stops the `M` stream within one observer tick (verified by speaking aloud while muted and confirming nothing lands in JSONL); first-time `operator dial claude` on a clean machine without TCC grants prompts cleanly during setup, not mid-meeting; `operator doctor` reports both Screen Recording AND Microphone status against the helper's notarized identity; the audio helper runs invisibly with no Dock or Cmd-Tab presence.

---

## Phase 14.22: Plugin form factor + naked `claude -p` shellouts ← BLOCKS LAUNCH

> **⚠️ S226 (2026-05-13): the `claude -p` spawn mechanism in this phase is being REPLACED.** Anthropic announced that starting 2026-06-15, `claude -p` no longer counts toward subscription limits and drains a small Agent SDK credit instead. Operator must pivot to interactive `claude` driven via PTY + hooks. Plugin form factor and shared-context-by-default invariants in this phase are PRESERVED; only the spawn-and-extract mechanism changes. Full plan in `debug/14_22_pty_spike/DECISION.md`. See the S226 status paragraph at the top of this roadmap for spike findings.

*Strategic pivot, session 210 (2026-05-09/10). Driven by an external Claude-desktop research conversation about the policy + product shape of subscription-auth wrappers (the OpenClaw cutoff, Anthropic's Feb 2026 docs clarification, the "tolerated-not-permitted" line for naked CLI shellouts). The conversation concluded that any system-prompt injection or `--mcp-config` flag at `claude -p` spawn time carries harness identity and is structurally what got OpenClaw blocked. v1 must strip every such flag from the inner-claude spawn and rely instead on the naked `claude -p [--resume <id>]` shape.*

*Architecture is intentionally simplified after a back-and-forth with the user (S210):*

- *Plugin **defaults to shared-context** mode. No `--shared-context` flag. The plugin's slash command always passes `--resume-session ${CLAUDE_SESSION_ID}` to the operator binary, which uses that session ID on every `claude -p --resume <id>` call from the very first @mention onward. **One session, end-to-end** — the user's Claude Code session IS the meeting brain. Pre-meeting prep is in scope; meeting interactions accumulate into the same session and are available post-meeting in the user's Claude Code window.*
- *Terminal-direct invocation (`operator dial claude <url>` without the plugin) gets a fresh session per meeting — no pre-existing session to resume, so the listener spawns naked on first @mention, captures `session_id` from `system_init`, and `--resume <id>` thereafter.*
- *No two-session walled-garden, no `--shared-context` flag, no in-meeting announcement, no pre-flight prompt. The handoff's trust-boundary guardrails are intentionally walked back; users own what's in their Claude Code session before they invoke `/operator dial`.*
- *No Anthropic outreach. No Chrome extension (preserve current dial CDP plumbing). No `--allowedTools` whitelist. `--yolo` keeps mapping to `--dangerously-skip-permissions`; default permissions = Claude Code's native `~/.claude/settings.json`.*
- *dial / deploy / login / `MacOSAdapter` / `LinuxAdapter` / `auth_state.json` go away — dial is the only mode v1 ships.*

*Rebrands much of Phase 14.19's scope (the dial/dial/deploy ladder) into "dial + plugin." Steps 14.19.7 F/G/H, 14.19.8, 14.19.9, 14.19.10, 14.19.11 are superseded by the 14.22 sub-steps below.*


| Step     | Description | Status | Est. |
| -------- | ----------- | ------ | ---- |
| 14.22.1  | **Spike: plugin submission process.** Confirm "plugin vs connector" terminology, identify long-lead-time prereqs (Apple-Dev-style onboarding lag), submission flow, approval timeline, naming/guideline constraints. **Findings (S210):** It's a Claude Code plugin (not connector). **Zero long-lead prereqs** — submission form at `claude.ai/settings/plugins/submit` is always open, no publisher account or identity verification. Manual review, 1-4 week turnaround (no published SLA). Skills get namespaced (`/operator:dial`, not `/dial`). "operator" naming is fine but `operator-meeting-assistant` is the safer alternative if collision concerns. Self-hosted marketplace at `github.com/1-800-operator/operator-plugins` is the fallback if Anthropic review delays past launch. Manifest needs `name` + `description` + `author` + `repository` + `homepage`. | ✅ S210 | shipped |
| 14.22.2  | **Spike: naked-shellout architecture viability.** Validate four load-bearing assumptions before locking the rewrite. **Findings (S210):** (a) Plugin `.mcp.json` does NOT register MCPs into user's `~/.claude.json` — plugin MCPs are scoped to plugin slash-command invocations only; backgrounded `claude -p` calls outside the plugin won't see them. **Workaround:** `curl \| sh` installer runs `claude mcp add transcript --scope user --` once, persisting the MCP into user-scope config so naked `claude -p` calls inherit it transparently. (b) `${CLAUDE_SESSION_ID}` substitution token in SKILL.md content gives the slash command access to the live session ID at execution time (not an env var; substitution-only). (c) `claude -p --resume <id> --output-format stream-json --include-partial-messages` composes — already validated in Phase 14.17 (`debug/resume_spike/probe.py`), in production at `claude_cli.py:307`, cache survives rehydration. (d) `nohup operator dial ... &` from a Bash-tool invocation survives the tool's return — empirically confirmed: PID reparented to PID 1 (init), alive across 24s + multiple subsequent Bash calls. | ✅ S210 | shipped |
| 14.22.3  | ✅ S211 (`4a55313`) — **Rewrite `claude_cli.py` to naked per-@mention `--resume` shellouts + delete `chat_runner.py` heartbeat side-channel.** Strip `--append-system-prompt` (the meeting-tone voice rules + `_PRE_TOOL_VOICE_RULE` block in `claude_cli.py`) — no replacement; whatever steering we want lives in plugin SKILL.md content (client-side, loaded into the user's session before the shellout fires) or in transcript-MCP tool descriptions (read by the model via normal tool discovery). Strip `--mcp-config` + `_maybe_write_mcp_config` (the per-spawn tempfile path) — transcript MCP comes from user-scope registration done by the installer (14.22.6). Add new CLI flag `operator dial claude --resume-session <session-id> <url>` that pre-populates `_session_id` so the very first @mention uses `--resume` instead of spawning fresh (this is what the plugin's slash command always passes; terminal-direct invocation omits it). Switch from long-lived persistent subprocess (current shape) to per-@mention spawn-and-exit. Per-@mention overhead is the new cost; mitigation is `--resume`'s prompt-cache hits (cache_read_input_tokens reuse from S187 spike) plus the existing per-meeting JSONL providing transcript context on demand. **Keep `progress_callback`** — it reads stdout and posts narration into meeting chat via the connector, invisible to the spawn signature; becomes more important now that the model no longer self-narrates. **Delete the `chat_runner.py` heartbeat side-channel** (`_heartbeat_loop`, `_request_heartbeat_text`, `HEARTBEAT_*` constants, `_heartbeat_user_msg`, `_last_heartbeat_post_ts`, the daemon-thread spawn in `_handle_message`) — today it spawns a side-channel `claude -p` with an operator-authored prompt to make claude write a status sentence, which is exactly the harness-shaped signature the architecture pivot strips. Replace with the 20s-throttled progress_callback posting `[☎️ Operator]`-voice narration in operator's voice (no model in the loop). **Atomic cleanup**: vestigial surfaces (`set_meeting_record_path`, `complete()`'s `system` arg, `warmup`, `_restart_after_death`, `set_tick_callback`) get stripped in this same step rather than waiting for 14.22.5. | ✅ S211 | shipped |
| 14.22.3.5 | ✅ S211 (`4a55313`) — **Naked-spawn invariant audit.** Sweep the codebase for every remaining `claude -p` shellout, every operator-authored prompt routed through `self._llm.ask`, and every place operator concatenates instruction text onto user input before sending. Six vectors: (1) direct subprocess invocations of `claude`, (2) indirect prompts through `LLMClient.ask` / `provider.complete*`, (3) operator-prepended payloads, (4) re-confirm zero matches for `--append-system-prompt` / `--mcp-config` / `_PRE_TOOL_VOICE_RULE` / `--allowedTools` outside comments+docs, (5) MCP server tool descriptions for steering language, (6) hidden indirection (`os.system`, `shell=True`, exec of string commands). Each hit classified as harness-shaped (must move/cut), not-harness (leave), or dies-in-14.22.4 (note). The heartbeat side-channel caught in 14.22.3 was the load-bearing example — this audit ensures there isn't a second one waiting. **Outcome (S211):** one finding — `LLMClient.intro()` authored a structured greeting prompt and fed it into `provider.complete`. Dial mode never called it (`quiet_mode=True` skipped intro entirely) but the pattern existed in source. Deleted along with `ChatRunner._generate_intro` + `_advance_intro_state` + intro-related state. All other vectors clean. Audit invariant pinned by `test_first_spawn_omits_resume_subsequent_spawns_pass_resume` which asserts neither `--append-system-prompt` nor `--mcp-config` appear in the cmd-array. | ✅ S211 | shipped |

Any bugs surfaced here loop back to whichever earlier phase owns the surface (CLI / plugin / install.sh / marketplace.json) before proceeding to 14.22.10. **Specifics this live-test must exercise — gaps the S215 self-test sweep could NOT cover (chat→LLM→reply pipeline + trigger gating + multi-turn memory + paragraph streaming + transcript MCP recall + tool-use + operator-voice narration + `claude plugin validate` + `operator doctor` + plugin manifest loading via `claude --plugin-dir` + slash-command dispatch for `/operator:doctor` + `/operator:status` + `/operator:hangup` + marketplace install end-to-end against canonical public repos (`claude plugin marketplace add 1-800-operator/operator` clones public CLI repo + validates clean; `claude plugin install operator@1-800-operator` clones public plugin repo + enables user-scope; fresh `claude` session lists all four `/operator:*` slash commands with no `--plugin-dir` flag — i.e. install.sh's step 7.5 produces a working install) are all already self-test-green; do NOT re-burn cycles on those):** (1) **CDP attach to dial Chrome** — confirm Chrome 121+ doesn't reject the attach, the dedicated `~/.operator/dial_profile/` user-data-dir survives a fresh-Mac install, and the Google sign-in cookie persistence works on first use. (4) **Real Meet join lifecycle** — lobby admission (host approval), participant-list scraping returns real names, the `ALONE_EXIT_GRACE_SECONDS=60` auto-leave fires correctly when the other human leaves but NOT during transient participant-panel drops. (5) **Interactive-mode `${CLAUDE_SESSION_ID}` substitution + `!`-block auto-execution + post-meeting context loop** — the dial skill body uses a ` ```! ` auto-execute block with `${CLAUDE_SESSION_ID}` and `$ARGUMENTS` substitution. S215 confirmed via a PATH-shim probe that `claude -p` non-interactive mode does NOT preserve the literal-block-execution semantics (the model paraphrases the skill body through its Bash tool and gets argv wrong), so substitution behavior can't be probed self-test-side. Interactive Claude Code IS expected to do the substitution at dispatch time, but live verification: open Claude Code interactively → load real pre-meeting context → `/operator:dial <meet-url>` → in the meeting `@claude what's that ticket I was reading earlier?` must recall pre-meeting context (proves `--resume-session ${CLAUDE_SESSION_ID}` resolved + the inner-claude was spawned with `--resume <real-id>`) → after `/operator:hangup` confirm meeting @-mention interactions are visible in the same Claude Code session's history (proves the post-meeting context loop and that the meeting session was actually the SAME id, not a fresh one). (6) **TCC permissions on the test machine** — if Screen Recording / Microphone aren't already granted to Chrome and to the Swift helper, confirm the prompt sequence is friendly. `operator doctor` should still pass before starting; if it doesn't, the install.sh nudges may need tightening. (7) **Terminal-direct invocation** — `operator dial claude <url>` with NO `--resume-session` flag confirms fresh-session-on-first-@mention; second @mention should `--resume` the just-spawned session id (TIMING line in `/tmp/operator.log` should show prompt-cache hits via `cache_read_input_tokens`). | ⬜ | ~1-2h |
| 14.22.9.5 | ✅ S216 (`321cffc`) — **One-character cosmetic fix: `@@claude` listening banner.** Dropped the literal `@` in `chat_runner.py:286` since `TRIGGER_PHRASE` already starts with one. Banner now reads `Listening for @claude — …`. | ✅ S216 | shipped |
| 14.22.9.6 | ✅ S216 — **Desktop-app surface fixes (plugin 0.1.0 → 0.1.3).** Surfaced four bugs running `/operator:dial` from the Claude Code desktop app for the first time, fixed three in-skill + one in-settings: (i) **plugin 0.1.1 (`e817e11`)** — dial skill stdout redirect moved from `/tmp/operator-current.log` to `~/.operator/dial-stdout.log` because the desktop app's bash sandbox refuses writes outside HOME. (iv) **`~/.claude/settings.json` allowlist** — added `Bash(operator:*)` + `Bash(nohup operator:*)` to `permissions.allow`. **This was the actual root cause.** Desktop-app slash-command-dispatched bash silently fails when the command isn't allowlisted (no approval dialog surfaces — unlike a normal in-conversation Bash tool call which prompts the user). With the allowlist in place, `/operator:dial` runs immediately, the session bridge fires (`resume=<pre-populated>, session=<desktop-session-id>` in `/tmp/operator.log`), and dial Chrome launches. **Outstanding for 14.22.9.8 below:** ship the allowlist into install.sh so future users don't hit the same wall. | ✅ S216 | shipped |
| 14.22.9.7 | ✅ S216 (`9a637be` + `6b8a260`) — **Post-meeting recall via transcript MCP.** Live test surfaced a fundamental architectural issue: Claude Code sessions are **conversation trees**, not linear logs. When the user said "@claude we need to talk about the zoo incident" in the meeting, operator's subprocess wrote both turns to the desktop session JSONL — verified, visible, with correct `parentUuid` lineage. But when the user went back to the desktop app and asked "what happened at the zoo incident?", the desktop's continuation attached its `parentUuid` to a node from BEFORE the meeting (`9324e987-…`, a system message at 01:19:15 — before the meeting's 01:19:49 user turn), branching the tree. The meeting's turns are siblings of the desktop's continuation, not ancestors — the desktop app holds stale in-memory session state and doesn't re-read the file after another process appends. **Fix shipped:** sidestep session continuity entirely; post-meeting recall flows through MCP tool calls instead. Three new tools added to `src/_1_800_operator/mcp_servers/transcript_server.py`: `list_meetings(limit)`, `list_meeting_record(meeting_slug?, kinds?, time-window?, last_n?, limit?)` (defaults `kinds=["chat","operator_status"]` to skip Whisper hallucination noise), `search_meeting_record(query, meeting_slug?, kinds?, context?, limit?)`. Plus `/operator:recap [slug]` skill in `operator-plugin@0.1.4` (`6b8a260`). Same data, accessible from any Claude Code session (desktop, terminal, new, resumed); cross-meeting recall by slug is free. Live-smoke-tested via the installed (uv-tool) operator binary: `list_meetings(limit=3)` correctly enumerates 133-meeting history; `search_meeting_record('purple', meeting_slug='oah-hvgw-pcq')` finds both favorite-color exchanges. **NOT yet tested:** running `/operator:recap` from the desktop app — gated on S217 restart-and-retry. | ✅ S216 | shipped |

| 14.22.9.9 | ✅ S217 (`8cb0357` + `00b9633` + `927836e` + plugin `0f9f84c`) — **State-scan tier 3 + operator-side resilience for desktop-app launches.** Tonight's live-test surfaced that the moat was silently broken on the desktop-app surface: every spawn logged `dial: no resume session — starting fresh` despite plugin 0.1.4's `--resume-session ${CLAUDE_SESSION_ID}` in the skill body. Three intertwined root causes were diagnosed in sequence: (i) the env var `CLAUDE_SESSION_ID` doesn't exist — the real env var is `CLAUDE_CODE_SESSION_ID` and the desktop app doesn't export *that* either (terminal Claude Code does); (ii) the desktop-app model rewrites the literal skill `!` block before issuing the Bash call — drops `claude` positional, swallows args, makes up flag values like `--resume-session -`, sometimes fires `cd && bash run.sh || true` (a fabricated run.sh that doesn't exist) masking failures via `|| true`; (iii) the original tier-3 fallback (scan `/private/tmp/claude-{uid}/.../tasks/*.output` for recent mtime) never fired in practice — foreground bash commands don't create .output files, backgrounded ones race operator startup latency. **Five shipped pieces:** (a) **operator-side three-tier resolver** (`__main__.py`): tier 1 `--resume-session` flag, tier 2 `CLAUDE_CODE_SESSION_ID` env (terminal path), tier 3 state-file scan (desktop path). Logs `source=flag|env|state-scan` at startup. (b) **singleton guard**: refuses to start if another `operator dial claude` process is already running, points user at `/operator:hangup`. Catches model's parallel-tool-use retries that would otherwise stack operators on the same dial Chrome. (c) **always-relaunch dial Chrome refactor**: dropped the connect-over-cdp-then-recover reuse path because Chrome 121+ refuses Browser.setDownloadBehavior (which Playwright's connect_over_cdp always issues) on any Chrome that previously had a Playwright session attached and disconnected — every operator-to-operator handoff hit the recovery relaunch anyway, so removing the dance cleans up ~50 LOC and the misleading "zombie Chrome" terminology. (d) **plugin 0.1.5** (`0f9f84c`): simplified skill body to `nohup operator dial claude $ARGUMENTS > ~/.operator/dial-stdout.log 2>&1 &` (no `--resume-session ${CLAUDE_SESSION_ID}` substitution) since operator now resolves the session itself; no flag for the model to mangle. (e) **state-scan tier 3** (`927836e`): replaces the broken tmp-scan; reads `cliSessionId` directly from desktop app's per-conversation state files at `~/Library/Application Support/Claude/claude-code-sessions/<agent>/<workspace>/local_*.json`, sorted by filesystem mtime within 5-min window. **End-to-end validation:** 4 desktop-app spawns this session, all logged `source=state-scan` with the cliSessionId matching the firing conversation (cf04164c, 574e948d, a558f7d6, 6aeb42be). One `@claude hello?` round-trip confirmed inner-claude carries the bridged session context (replied with "operator is already running pid X" because the bridged session had been doing operator-debugging — the moat working AS DESIGNED, though it has a sharp UX edge: meeting brain inherits whatever the user has been doing pre-meeting). | ✅ S217 | shipped |

| 14.22.9.12 | ✅ S219 (operator `6b67e1f` + plugin `caf1cfd` 0.1.10) — **Root-caused the `/operator:dial` double-Bash + shipped lockfile singleton guard + SKILL.md rewrite.** Live-test from desktop app produced a spurious "already running (pid N)" error on a single `/dial` invocation. Pre-existing SKILL.md prose still told the model "Invoke the Bash tool with the command in the `!` block as your first action," so the model dutifully fired a second Bash call after reconstructing the command from context (no `claude` because `claude` was overwritten by output). **Two fixes shipped:** (a) plugin **0.1.10** (`caf1cfd`) rewrites SKILL.md: drop the "Invoke the Bash tool" directive entirely, lead with the `!` block, follow with prose framing the output as already-produced (`"operator has already run by the time you read this. | 14.22.9.11 | ✅ S218 (operator `3e8dcdd` + plugin `db15b10` 0.1.8 + plugin `3d925a3` 0.1.9 + operator `fc84747`) — **Self-daemonize so the Bash tool gets synchronous feedback.** Root-cause for the model's recovery dance (checking tempfiles, retrying with `--resume-session`, re-reading SKILL.md, falling back to run.sh): `operator dial claude <url> &` returned `Bash completed with no output`, leaving the model with no ground truth of success or failure. | 14.22.9.13 | ✅ S220 (`3fe3bb7` + `d4857b8` + `a5d45a9`) — **End-to-end turn-latency instrumentation + POLL_INTERVAL win.** User reported perceived latency on the first @claude reply. Added three TIMING log lines across the receive path and the provider so each turn leaves a greppable breadcrumb trail: `TIMING msg_received id=… poll_lag_ms=… read_to_process_ms=…` (per message; JS MutationObserver stamps `t_dom=Date.now()` on each queued message, adapter stamps `t_drained` per batch in `_do_read_chat`); `TIMING turn_complete turn=N poll_lag_ms=… gate_ms=… to_first_visible_ms=… total_ms=…` (per turn, emitted from `_emit_turn_done`, `t_first_visible` stamped inside `_send` after `connector.send_chat` returns so it reflects DOM visibility not enqueue time); existing `TIMING claude_cli_turn` extended with `spawn=Nms cli_init=Nms api_ttft=Nms warm=0\|1` stage breakdown + `cache_input cache_creation cache_read` from the result event's usage block. | 14.22.9.14 | ✅ S220 (`1071ad9` + `ac14b63`) — **Eager pre-spawn warm subprocess in ClaudeCLIProvider.** Identified by 14.22.9.13 instrumentation that the ~2.6s claude-CLI startup (Node boot + MCP attach + --resume JSONL parse) was the dominant per-turn cost. Architecture: `pre_warm()` spawns `claude -p --resume <id>` ahead of demand and slots it in `(_warm_proc, _warm_out_q, _warm_stderr_buf)`. `_run_one_turn` claims the warm slot if alive; `proc.poll()` check + fresh-spawn fallback handles dead slots (idle timeout, crash). Called from two places: `ChatRunner.run()` after a successful meeting join (covers turn 1), and `complete_streaming`'s tail-on-success via `_schedule_pre_warm` on a daemon thread (covers turns 2+). `_warm_in_progress` latch dedups overlapping callers; the slow spawn runs OUTSIDE `_warm_lock` so a turn arriving mid-prewarm doesn't serialize on it. **Empirical finding driving `ac14b63` (the second commit):** the initial design drained the system_init event during pre_warm to validate auth + capture session_id, but every pre_warm timed out at 15s — claude `-p --input-format stream-json` emits ZERO events until it reads its first stdin input. A 20s empirical probe with no stdin → 0 bytes stdout, then full event burst the instant we wrote an envelope. Conclusion: claude does its boot/attach/parse during the parked window but silently. Pre_warm now just spawns and slots; the in-turn drain consumes init normally. Win materializes as `cli_init` collapsing from ~2600ms → 12-21ms on warm turns (just the input-ack latency). **Live result:** per-turn total dropped from ~5s to ~2s across three turns, ALL with `warm=1` and `cli_init ≤21ms`. **Anti-detection note:** the spawn command stays naked (still `claude -p --resume <id>`); idle pre-spawn does not generate API traffic (no `messages.create` calls while parked); the only Anthropic-visible delta is the auth handshake landing earlier — indistinguishable from a user who runs `claude --resume <id>` and grabs coffee before typing. | ✅ S220 | shipped |
| 14.22.9.15 | ✅ S220 (plugin `a02e378` 0.1.11 + operator `e720f72`) — **Plugin 0.1.11: dial SKILL.md rewrite + /operator:update skill + version-stale chat hint.** Three coupled changes that together address the long-standing plugin-auto-update-friction carryover. (a) **dial SKILL.md** rewritten from a verbatim three-line script ("Reply with these three lines: Operator is joining the Meet…") into in-your-own-words guidance covering: operator is dialing claude in / `@claude` can be mentioned anywhere in a meeting message / context flows both ways via the live Claude Code session / the three slash commands (`/operator:hangup`, `/operator:status`, `/operator:doctor`) and what each does / `--yolo` to skip per-tool permission prompts. Per `feedback_llm_steering_via_tool_results.md` — let the model author the wording from facts/disposition, don't script exact user-facing strings. (b) **New `/operator:update` skill** — two separate `!` blocks (`claude plugin marketplace update 1-800-operator` then `claude plugin update operator@1-800-operator`) for clean allowlist matching (a single compound `&&` line would have required a much wider allowlist pattern). (c) **operator-side version-stale check** (`src/_1_800_operator/pipeline/update_check.py`) — best-effort fetch of remote `marketplace.json` on github via stdlib `urllib.request` (5s timeout, silent on failure), compares to local marketplace cache at `~/.claude/plugins/marketplaces/1-800-operator/.claude-plugin/marketplace.json`. | 14.22.10 | **README + landing-page rewrite + launch tasks.** Cover in README/landing copy: (a) install path = single `curl \| sh` (14.22.8.5 collapsed the prior two-step `curl` + `/plugin install` flow — install.sh handles both); (b) "shared session" privacy implication — the meeting brain has access to the user's pre-meeting Claude Code session contents and meeting interactions become part of that session afterward (this is the value, but it's load-bearing to disclose); (c) one-paragraph policy posture disclosure ("operator runs against your Claude subscription via the local `claude` CLI; this is currently tolerated by Anthropic's terms but not formally documented as a permitted pattern; this could change"); (d) the dial-only product surface (no dial/deploy in v1); (e) reply attribution — meeting participants see Claude's responses prefixed by the dial mode marker. **Phase total: ~15-21h (~2-3 days).** *Sequence: 14.22.3 → 14.22.4 → 14.22.5 (audit) → 14.22.6 + 14.22.7 in parallel → 14.22.8 (self-hosted marketplace) → 14.22.9 (live-test, must validate install path before docs/launch) → 14.22.10 (README + landing-page + launch tasks: flip plugin repo public, tag-pin marketplace, submit to Anthropic directory). 14.22.10 gates phase complete.*

### Decisions locked from S210 conversation

- **Plugin defaults to shared-context.** No flag, no opt-out, no two-session model. The user's Claude Code session IS the meeting brain. Disclose in README; don't engineer guardrails the user explicitly cut.
- **Naked subprocess.** No `--append-system-prompt`, no `--mcp-config`, no harness identity at runtime. Transcript MCP comes from user-scope registration done by the installer.
- **Dial-only product surface.** dial / deploy / login + their adapters deleted entirely.
- **No Anthropic outreach.** Policy posture disclosed in README; treat any future cutoff as a known risk.
- **No `--allowedTools` whitelist.** `--yolo` is the only permission flag (existing behavior); default permissions inherit from Claude Code's native `~/.claude/settings.json`.
- **No Chrome extension.** Current dial CDP plumbing (`AttachAdapter`) preserved as-is.
- **No in-meeting announcement.** Plugin posts no banner on join — README disclosure is the only privacy signal.
- **Self-host marketplace as fallback.** Don't gate launch on Anthropic review; ship via own marketplace if needed.

### Decisions locked from S211 conversation

- **Spawn signature is the detection vector.** Anthropic identifies harnesses-on-subscription via flags + metadata that get passed *into* `claude -p` spawns — `--append-system-prompt`, `--mcp-config`, env breadcrumbs. What operator reads OUT of the stream (stdout events) carries no signature. Implication: every steering surface that today rides on spawn args must move client-side (into the user's own session) or get cut. What operator does after the spawn (inspect events, post to meeting chat) stays unrestricted.
- **Steering homes after the strip.** Two acceptable surfaces for shaping inner-claude behavior in v1: (a) plugin SKILL.md content, loaded into the user's Claude Code session client-side before the shellout fires — visible to Anthropic as user-installed context, not as harness injection; (b) MCP tool descriptions, read by the model via normal tool discovery. The operator binary's spawn must remain naked.
- **`progress_callback` survives.** It reads stdout content blocks and posts narration to meeting chat via the connector — zero spawn-signature impact. Becomes more important now that the model no longer self-narrates per `_PRE_TOOL_VOICE_RULE`; without it, meeting chat goes dark for 30-60s during long tool runs.
- **Atomic cleanup in 14.22.3.** Vestigial methods (`set_meeting_record_path`, `complete()`'s `system` arg, `warmup`, `_restart_after_death`) get stripped in the same commit as the lifecycle rewrite, not deferred to 14.22.5's audit pass.
- **Switchboard-operator failure UX.** Operator narrates failures + status to meeting chat in operator's voice (`[🤖 Claude] connection dropped — reconnecting…`) rather than hiding behind the model. Three concrete cases: (a) subprocess EOF before `result` → post status line, respawn with `--resume`, replay @mention, retry once; (b) long tool runs → `progress_callback` posts the current tool name + input to chat, **throttled to one post per 20s** (fast tool chains collapse into one line; long-running tools get periodic "still working" updates); (c) Claude-Code permission denial seen in `tool_result` stream → operator posts `permission denied for X — re-run with --yolo to skip per-tool approval`. All operator-side: stream-reading + chat-posting, zero spawn-signature impact. Heartbeat watchdog and `TURN_TIMEOUT_SECONDS` ceiling are deleted; trust user-initiated `/operator hangup` for genuine wedges.

### Done when

`/plugin install` is live (Anthropic-hosted or self-hosted). `/operator dial <url>` from a Claude Code session brings the user's session into the meeting via `--resume`; `@claude` references pre-meeting prep correctly; post-meeting debrief in the same Claude Code session works. Terminal-direct `operator dial claude <url>` works as fresh-session-per-meeting. dial/deploy/login no longer exist in the codebase. README documents the shared-session model and the policy posture. All 15 tests pass.

---

## Phase 14.18: transcript tool API beef-up + codex captions parity (~1 day) ✅ shipped S188 (`3ed5ff2`)

**Why launch-blocking.** v1 ships two bots — claude and codex — and the user wants feature parity at launch. Today only the claude bot has caption awareness (via the bundled transcript MCP at `mcp_servers/transcript_server.py`); codex has the documented gap from S179 (R8). Bot parity is a launch promise.

**Two tightly-coupled deliverables in one phase, sequenced deliberately:**

### Part A — beef up the transcript tool first

The current `recall_transcript` tool API is genuinely thin for real-world long-meeting use:

- Only knobs are `minutes_back` and `last_n` — no keyword filter, no time-window-around-X, no by-speaker filter, no length cap.
- Returns the entire requested chunk as one string. A 90-minute steady-talking meeting can dump several hundred KB into the model's context.
- "What were we talking about *around* 30 minutes ago?" forces the model to pull from 30 minutes ago to NOW (not a window around minute 30).
- "What did Sarah say?" forces a full pull and mental filter.
- `last_n` counts caption *lines*, which inflates for chatty speakers and undercounts long pauses.

We're going to ship beefier shape before extending to codex, so codex inherits the better tool from day one rather than us shipping the thin one twice.

**Step A1 — scoping spike (loose inspiration: the GitHub MCP surface).** GitHub MCP solves a structurally similar problem ("model needs to navigate a large indexed corpus of text") and exposes a curated set of tools (`search_code`, `search_issues`, `get_file_contents`, `list_commits`, etc.) rather than one dump-everything endpoint. Skim its tool list at session start as a primer for what shape our transcript tool *could* take. Don't copy directly — our use case is meeting captions (much smaller corpus, narrower query needs), not arbitrary repo navigation. The exercise is "what's the curated set of 3–5 query verbs that covers 90% of real-meeting needs?"

**Step A2 — finalize the new tool surface in conversation with the user.** Candidate verbs to discuss: keyword/semantic search across captions, time-window-around-X (not just since-X), by-speaker filter, summary-of-window, list-speakers, get-N-around-line. Lock final shape together before any code lands.

**Step A3 — implement** in `src/_1_800_operator/mcp_servers/transcript_server.py`. Keep `recall_transcript` for back-compat (or rename to a clearer verb if we add one); add the new tool functions; add a length cap with pagination/truncation hint so a model never blows context unintentionally.

**Step A4 — test (unit + fixture).** Build a fixture transcript file representing a realistic 60–90 minute meeting (synthetic captions, multiple speakers, varied speech density). Unit tests exercise each new tool function against the fixture for happy paths + edge cases (empty windows, single-speaker, long monologues, special chars). Run via the existing standalone-script test pattern.

**Step A5 — live-test on a real Meet, claude bot.** Open a real 30+ minute meeting (or simulate by pre-loading the fixture into a meeting record and running operator dial against a fake-long meeting), exercise each new tool verb via chat ("@claude what was the action item Sarah mentioned around the 20 minute mark?"). Verify the model picks the right tool for each question shape.

### Part B — extend captions to codex via marker file

Once the new tool ships and works for claude, extend it to codex.

**Step B1 — add the marker file mechanism** at `~/.operator/.current_meeting`. Write the active meeting's record path to this file from `_wire_meeting_record`. Delete it from `connector.leave()` and the shutdown handler.

**Step B2 — modify `transcript_server.py`** to read the meeting path from the marker file on each tool call. Falls back to the existing `OPERATOR_MEETING_RECORD_PATH` env var if marker is missing, so claude's existing path keeps working unchanged.

**Step B3 — register the transcript MCP for codex** in `agents/codex/config.yaml`. Append three static `-c` flags to `mcp_servers.codex.args`:

```yaml
- mcp-server
- -c
- 'mcp_servers.transcript.command="python"'
- -c
- 'mcp_servers.transcript.args=["-m","_1_800_operator.mcp_servers.transcript_server"]'
```

No path interpolation needed — the marker file replaces it. (Codex 0.128.0 supports `-c key=value` overrides on `mcp-server` per S187 spike; the S179 finding that "mcp-server doesn't accept --mcp-config" is now obsolete.)

**Step B4 — drop the captions-disabled disclaimer** in the codex YAML's comment block + flip `transcript.captions_enabled: true` for the codex agent.

**Step B5 — live-test end-to-end** with `operator dial codex <meet-url>`. Speak something aloud; ask codex via chat about it; verify codex pulls captions through the new tool surface. Run the same query battery from Step A5 against codex to confirm parity.

**Done when:** both bots have feature parity on captions; the new tool surface handles the realistic long-meeting query shapes we identified in A2; live tests pass against a real Meet for both bots.

**S188 outcome:** Part A shipped as designed (3 new MCP verbs + 12 KB byte ceiling + 26 unit tests). Part B's plan changed mid-implementation when the spike found `codex mcp-server` 0.128.0 doesn't expose `-c`-registered child MCPs to its inner model. Pivoted: codex uses raw shell + marker file instead, framework prompt directs it to `cat`/`grep`/`jq` the JSONL on demand. Same outcome (caption parity), different mechanism per bot. Both bots verified 8/8 on a synthetic load matrix instead of live Meet (user request — testing was driven autonomously via `operator try` with stdin-piped query battery). Three pre-existing bugs killed along the way (see "Hard Won Knowledge" in agent-context.md).

---

## Phase 14.17: claude_cli `--resume` for crash recovery (~half-day) ✅ shipped S187 (`4a4035f`)

**Why.** When the `claude -p` subprocess dies mid-meeting today, `_restart_after_death` (`pipeline/providers/claude_cli.py:553`) re-spawns cold and feeds a synthesized opener built from `_turn_history` — but `_turn_history` only carries `(user_text, assistant_text)` pairs, dropping tool calls and tool results (S166 deferred carry-over). So if the subprocess crashed after claude opened files, edited Linear, etc., the resumed bot inherits a sanitized story without ground truth and may hallucinate or contradict prior actions.

`claude -p --resume <session-id>` rehydrates a fresh subprocess from claude's local session store on disk (`~/.claude/projects/<project>/<session-id>.jsonl`) with the full message history including tool use + tool results. We already capture `session_id` from the system-init event (logged at `_validate_init_event`, line 582) — just need to persist it and use it on restart.

**Note on scope:** `--resume` does NOT replace tail-replay on the `anthropic`/`openai` API providers — it's a `claude -p` flag, not an API feature. Steady-state turns on `claude_cli` already don't replay tail (the long-lived subprocess holds context in-memory). So this phase is exclusively about closing the crash-recovery fidelity gap on track A.

**Cross-meeting continuity is an explicit non-goal of this phase** — `--resume`-ing a prior meeting's session-id when the bot rejoins a follow-up meeting is mechanically possible but sits in tension with the "fresh meeting = fresh context" default, and `MeetingRecord` is slug-keyed (no natural cross-meeting state). Revisit post-MVP.

**Steps:**

1. **Spike (~30min): confirm `--resume` + stream-json compose.** Verify `claude -p --resume <id> --input-format stream-json --output-format stream-json` works end-to-end. The engineer's delegate MCP (`agents/engineer/delegate_to_claude_code.py`) already uses `--resume` but in one-shot mode (`-p "<task>"`). If stream-json + resume compose, the swap is clean. If not, recovery becomes a two-step shape: one-shot `--resume` to reconstruct context, then re-init stream-json — uglier but still wins on fidelity vs. the synthesized-opener.
2. **Capture and persist session_id.** Add `self._session_id` to `ClaudeCLIProvider`; populate from the `payload["session_id"]` already extracted at line 582. Set on every successful spawn.
3. **Rewire `_restart_after_death`** to spawn with `["claude", "-p", "--resume", self._session_id, ...]` (or the two-step fallback if step 1 says so). Delete the `_build_synthesized_opener` codepath (lines ~513–550) and the `_turn_history: list[tuple[str, str]]` field + every `_turn_history.append(...)` site (lines 699 + 827, plus the wrap-around references near lines 683 + 805). Also delete the corresponding restart path that re-feeds the synthesized opener on streaming retries.
4. **Test (live): kill the subprocess mid-meeting after a tool call; verify the resumed subprocess answers correctly about the prior tool call.** Kill via `pkill -9 -f "claude -p"` or similar between turns. Ask "what did you just do?" — pre-fix answer goes vague, post-fix answer cites the actual tool result.
5. **Test (unit): subprocess crash → `--resume` invocation.** Mock the subprocess; assert the second spawn call uses `--resume <captured-id>` and that `_turn_history` is no longer touched.

**Done when:** mid-meeting crash recovery preserves tool-call fidelity end-to-end, the `_turn_history` + `_build_synthesized_opener` plumbing is gone, and a regression test pins the `--resume` invocation.

## Completed Phases

Phases 1–6 + Caption Refactor + MCP Integration (all ✅)

### Phase 1: Extract the Agent Pipeline ✅

Pulled all "brain" logic out of `app.py` into `pipeline/` with zero macOS-specific code.

### Phase 2: Define the Connector Interface ✅

Defined `MeetingConnector` abstract interface. Wrapped macOS logic as `MacOSAdapter`.

### Phase 3: Docker/Cloud Adapter ✅

Built headless Linux adapter in Docker. Verified end-to-end in live Google Meet.

### Phase 4: Reorient — Cloud Cleanup + Linux Local Adapter ✅

Moved cloud artifacts into `cloud/`. Adapted Docker adapter into `LinuxAdapter` for local Linux machines.

### Phase 5: Config System ✅

All hardcoded constants moved into `config.yaml` with `config.py` reader.

### Phase 6: Consolidate Entry Points ✅

Shared loop extracted into `pipeline/runner.py`. OS auto-detection via `python -m _1_800_operator`. Calendar poller replaced `calendar_join.py`.

### Caption Refactor ✅

Replaced ScreenCaptureKit + Whisper with Google Meet DOM caption scraping. Eliminates echo problem, privacy issues, and Whisper dependency on macOS.

### Phase 11 (original): MCP Integration ✅

MCP client connects to configured servers at startup, discovers tools. Tool-call loop in LLMClient handles tool_call → execute → result → re-prompt. Chat-specific LLM settings. Config schema for `mcp_servers`. Validated with Linear and GitHub MCP servers end-to-end in live Meet. GitHub MCP server upgraded from deprecated npm package to official Go binary (`github/github-mcp-server` v0.32.0).

### Phase 7: Performance Iteration ✅ (partial)

Audio quality, TTS 3-tier architecture, latency masking, STT accuracy (mlx-whisper), streaming classification, playback interrupt classification, latency docs. Deferred to voice phase: TTS error handling/retry, premature finalization at 0.7s silence threshold.
